Solar Power is two-part (Sp. Atk ×1.5 in sun via `attack_modifier_uq412`; maxHP/8 self-damage in sun via `try_end_of_turn`, sharing Dry Skin's `SOLAR_POWER_HP_DROP`-labeled result key). Poison Heal inverts the existing `StatusManager.end_of_turn_damage` to return a **negative** (heal) value instead of duplicating poison-tick logic — a flat maxHP/8 heal regardless of poison vs. toxic, though the toxic counter still increments. Primordial Sea/Desolate Land reuse the ordinary `WEATHER_RAIN`/`WEATHER_SUN` constants directly (no separate "Primal" weather value, no Primal-item gate, per Section 8.5's explicit recommendation). Delta Stream needed a genuinely new `DamageCalculator.WEATHER_STRONG_WINDS` constant plus its type-effectiveness side effect (weakens super-effective hits against Flying-type defenders, checked per-type-component) wired into BOTH of this project's independent type-effectiveness computations (`TypeChart.get_effectiveness`'s early immunity/ability-gate check, gained a new `weaken_flying_se` bool param, and the actual per-type UQ4.12 damage-multiplier block in `DamageCalculator.calculate`) since they aren't unified into one function the way source's is. New `m17d_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 30/30 assertions, passed clean on the first run — every damage-calc scenario checked against `TypeChart.TABLE` directly first, per CLAUDE.md's type-immunity-precedes-ability-logic convention. 1424 total assertions across 25 numbered suites, all green. **M17e (Terrain system) is void** — Rob's locked-in scope decision (confirmed before M17a began) excludes all 10 terrain-reliant abilities (Electric/Psychic/Misty/Grassy Surge, Surge Surfer, Grass Pelt, Quark Drive, Mimicry, Hadron Engine, Seed Sower), so the Terrain system Section 11 proposed for M17e will never be built for this project — the letter is skipped, not renumbered, to avoid touching the already-shipped M17a-d labels/citations for no benefit.
- M17f (Trapping check — new infrastructure — + Shadow Tag/Arena Trap/Magnet Pull): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-02. First genuinely new-infrastructure tier since M14a — every M17a-d tier before it was pure reuse. Source: `battle_util.c :: IsAbilityPreventingEscape` (L4917-4941), called only from two selection-time sites in `battle_main.c` (the wild-battle Run menu, the party-switch-menu's `B_ACTION_SWITCH` case) — `CanBattlerEscape`, the separate function backing forced switches/faint-replacement/Baton Pass, literally has "no ability check" per its own source comment, confirming trapping is a selection-time-only gate. New `AbilityManager.is_trapped(mon, live_opponents) -> bool` encodes: a global Ghost-type exemption from all three abilities (`B_GHOSTS_ESCAPE >= GEN_6`, unconditional at this project's GEN_LATEST config); Shadow Tag's mirror-match exemption when both sides have it (`B_SHADOW_TAG_ESCAPE >= GEN_4`, also unconditional here); Arena Trap gating on `AbilityManager.is_grounded` (reused directly from M16d); Magnet Pull gating on Steel-type. New `BattleManager._get_live_opponents` mirrors `_apply_switch_in_abilities`'s existing live-opponent loop shape. Wired into `_phase_move_selection` immediately after a queued/AI-chosen switch sets `_chosen_switch_slots` — a blocked switch falls back to the mon's first move, the same fallback expression already used elsewhere in that function. Forced switches, faint replacement, and Baton Pass are confirmed unaffected by construction (none of those three call sites ever reads `_chosen_switch_slots` or calls `is_trapped` — not a special-cased exemption, just architecturally disjoint paths), and trapping only ever reads the OPPONENT's side, never the holder's own. Shed Shell (source's one item-based exemption) isn't modeled — this project has no Shed Shell item anywhere, confirmed via grep. New `m17f_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 28/28 assertions (ability data; 12 direct `is_trapped` unit tests covering every positive/negative/exemption case including a dual Ghost/Steel mon proving the Ghost exemption overrides Magnet Pull's type gate; full-battle integration for the block itself, Arena Trap's Flying exemption, Magnet Pull's Steel-only gate, Roar/Baton Pass/faint-replacement all bypassing trapping, and the holder's own side switching freely). Total assertions across all 27 numbered suites: **1476**, all green (a direct recount during this sweep found the actual suite count was already 27, not 26 as M17d's "25 prior suites" line implied — a stale count, not a regression; every suite passed clean). See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17f]` entry for full source citations and the Step 0 exclusion cross-check.
- M17g (Ability-suppression plumbing — new infrastructure — Mold Breaker / Neutralizing Gas): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-03. Second genuinely new-infrastructure tier in M17. Step 0 excluded Turboblaze (163)/Teravolt (164) as legendary-exclusive (Reshiram/Kyurem-White, Zekrom/Kyurem-Black — Section 13.1), the correction M17f's own "next tier" note flagged in advance, and deferred Mycelium Might (298, a genuine hybrid whose ability-ignore half fits this tier but whose turn-order-last half needs the not-yet-built Stall shape) — final list just Mold Breaker (104) and Neutralizing Gas (256). Confirmed from source that the two abilities have fundamentally different suppression shapes and implemented each faithfully rather than sharing one mechanism: Mold Breaker is attacker-scoped and move-scoped (`moldBreakerActive` is set only while processing the Mold-Breaker holder's own current move, per `battle_util.c` L9799-9802, and never suppresses its own wielder — `CanBreakThroughAbility`'s `battlerDef == battlerAtk` exclusion, L4822-4827), and only bypasses abilities source flags `.breakable = TRUE` (26 of this project's abilities qualify — see `AbilityManager.MOLD_BREAKER_BREAKABLE`); Neutralizing Gas is field-wide and holder-presence-scoped (`IsNeutralizingGasOnField`, L4794-4803 — suppresses every OTHER live battler's ability, never its own, for as long as it's on the field). New `AbilityManager.effective_ability_id(mon, ng_active, attacker)` is the single suppression-aware chokepoint (mirrors source's `GetBattlerAbilityInternal`) that ~30 `AbilityManager` functions, 6 `StatusManager` functions, and `DamageCalculator.calculate` were all rewritten to route through instead of reading `mon.ability.ability_id` raw — confirmed via a full grep sweep, zero raw reads remain outside the primitive itself. New `AbilityManager.is_neutralizing_gas_active(combatants)` / `BattleManager._is_neutralizing_gas_active()` check the field fresh at each call site. **Retrofitted during M17h**: the `MOLD_BREAKER_BREAKABLE`/`NEUTRALIZING_GAS_UNSUPPRESSABLE` hardcoded arrays mentioned below were replaced with direct `AbilityData.breakable`/`.cant_be_suppressed` field reads after discovering `AbilityData` already had these exact fields defined and unused — see M17h's entry and `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17g]` addendum. A source-verified correction to this tier's own task brief: Neutralizing Gas DOES suppress trapping (Shadow Tag/Arena Trap/Magnet Pull all route through the same `GetBattlerAbility` chokepoint `IsAbilityPreventingEscape` uses), but Mold Breaker does NOT (trapping is checked only at selection time, entirely outside any move-processing window) — `is_trapped` gained an `ng_active` param but deliberately no `attacker` param, documented explicitly so this doesn't get "fixed" backward later. A pre-existing, unrelated dead-code gap was found and flagged (not fixed): Ripen's ability-aware resist-berry modifier is computed correctly but never actually called by the real damage pipeline, which hardcodes the un-doubled constant instead — predates M17g, out of scope for this tier. New `m17g_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 31/31 assertions across 9 sections (ability data; `effective_ability_id`/`is_neutralizing_gas_active` direct unit tests including the NG-suppresses-Mold-Breaker-itself recursive interaction and a fainted-holder negative case; Mold Breaker bypassing a defending Levitate holder's Ground immunity via direct `DamageCalculator` calls, both the bypass itself and confirmation it doesn't apply when the Mold Breaker holder isn't the actual attacker; full-battle Neutralizing-Gas-suppresses-Intimidate and stops-once-holder-leaves scenarios; the `is_trapped()` interaction in both directions; a negative control proving the "did not fire" assertions were real discrimination, not vacuous passes). A regression-baseline discrepancy was found, surfaced to Rob, and resolved before implementation began: this file's own last-recorded total (1478, from M17f's follow-up) and the task's expected baseline (1444) both disagreed with a fresh direct recount (1454, 0 failures) — Rob confirmed proceeding on the measured 1454 baseline; root cause of the historical drift wasn't further investigated (out of scope), matching M17f's own similar "stale count, not a regression" resolution. Total assertions across all 28 `.tscn` files: 1454 prior + 31 = **1485**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17g]` entry for full source citations.
- M17h (Ability-copy/overwrite plumbing — new infrastructure — Trace / Mummy / Receiver / Power of Alchemy / Wandering Spirit / Lingering Aroma): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-03. Third genuinely new-infrastructure tier in M17. Step 0 re-verified all 6 IDs against Section 13's exclusion sweep — none needed correction, unlike the M17f→M17g handoff. Traced each ability's exact mechanic from source and kept them as genuinely separate functions rather than one shared "copy" primitive: Trace (switch-in, copies a live opponent's ability — battle_util.c L2964-3000, 50/50 random pick between two eligible doubles targets or deterministic if only one is eligible); Receiver/Power of Alchemy (doubles-only ally-fainting-triggered copy — confirmed from source these share the EXACT SAME dispatch function, `battle_script_commands.c :: BS_TryActivateReceiver` L12946-12968, not separate implementations); Mummy/Lingering Aroma (contact → one-directional overwrite of the ATTACKER's ability — confirmed mechanically identical via the same shared switch-case block, battle_util.c L3859-3883); Wandering Spirit (contact → BIDIRECTIONAL swap with the attacker, both sides reassigned, the opposite direction from Mummy's overwrite). All four read/write the RAW `.ability` field, never the suppression-aware accessor — confirmed from source, meaning a copied/traced ability is unaffected by suppression at copy time; suppression is purely a separate runtime check applied whenever the ability is later consumed (tested explicitly). A source-verified correction worth flagging: Mummy/Lingering Aroma's exemption is checked via `cant_be_suppressed` on the ATTACKER's current ability, NOT `cant_be_overwritten` as the task's own framing assumed — `cant_be_overwritten` is actually consumed by Skill-Swap/Entrainment-style moves this project doesn't have. Mid-tier design correction: discovered `AbilityData` already had `cant_be_copied`/`cant_be_swapped`/`cant_be_traced`/`cant_be_suppressed`/`cant_be_overwritten`/`breakable` fields defined and fully supported by `gen_abilities.py`, entirely unused — rather than add hardcoded arrays for M17h's own exemption needs on top of M17g's two existing arrays, all five were migrated to read directly off each ability's own `.tres` resource (a pure refactor — M17g's `m17g_test` suite re-ran unchanged at 31/31 post-retrofit). New `BattleManager.ability_changed(pokemon, new_ability_id)` signal, mirroring M16e's `type_changed` shape. New `m17h_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 64/64 assertions across 10 sections, including the bidirectional-swap confirmation (both sides checked, not just one), the doubles-targeting determinism (caught and fixed a test-authoring bug where `force_pick_second` was passed into the wrong positional parameter, silently falling back to real RNG), and the copy-time-vs-suppression-time cross-tier interaction. `.tres` data: 6 new abilities added with real source-cited descriptions (all previously empty placeholders) plus the M17g-retrofit field additions on 27 existing abilities — 114 total `.tres` files. Full regression: all 27 prior suites unchanged and still passing. Total assertions across all 29 `.tscn` files: 1485 prior + 64 = **1549**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17h]` entry (and the addendum on `[M17g]`) for full source citations.
- M17i (Switch-out trigger hook — new infrastructure — Regenerator / Natural Cure): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-03. Fourth genuinely new-infrastructure tier in M17. Step 0 re-verified both IDs against Section 13's exclusion sweep — neither Regenerator (144) nor Natural Cure (30) needed correction. Resolved Section 11's own hedge about splitting this tier from Wimp Out/Emergency Exit's HP-threshold forced-self-switch: confirmed from source that Regenerator/Natural Cure are purely reactive (fire only once a switch-out is already underway) while Wimp Out/Emergency Exit would need a genuinely different switch-*initiating* mechanism — the split is correct, and Wimp Out/Emergency Exit stay out of this tier entirely (deferred to a possible M17i-2). Both abilities share one dispatch function in source (`battle_script_commands.c :: Cmd_switchoutabilities`, L9322-9372) — new `AbilityManager.try_switch_out(mon, ng_active)` mirrors this exactly, wired via `BattleManager._apply_switch_out_abilities` into all three sites that reach source's `switchoutabilities` call (`_do_voluntary_switch`, `_do_forced_switch_in`, Baton Pass's inline switch-out block) but deliberately NOT `_do_switch_in` (faint replacement never reaches that source call at all). A source-verified correction worth flagging: the natural framing "fires only on voluntary switches" is wrong — source's `BattleScript_RoarSuccessRet` reaches the same `switchoutabilities` call, so Roar/Whirlwind-forced switch-outs trigger both abilities too; the real gate is "left the field alive," not "switch was voluntary" (verified via a dedicated Roar-forced-switch test). Confirmed via the `[M17f]` trapping gate that a blocked voluntary switch never reaches the new hook (architecturally disjoint, not a special-cased exemption), and confirmed neither ability carries a `.cantBeSuppressed` flag in source, so Neutralizing Gas correctly suppresses both through the existing `effective_ability_id` chokepoint. Per the `[M17h]`-established dormant-field-check discipline, confirmed neither ability needed any new/existing `AbilityData` exemption field populated — no hardcoded-array or field retrofit was needed this tier. New `m17i_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 35/35 assertions (ability data; direct `try_switch_out` unit tests for both abilities including the Neutralizing-Gas-suppression no-op; full-battle voluntary switch, faint-replacement non-trigger, Roar-forced-switch trigger, Baton Pass trigger, `is_trapped()` interaction, and Neutralizing Gas suppression interaction). Total assertions across all 30 `.tscn` files: 1549 prior + 35 = **1584**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17i]` entry for full source citations. Note: a real flaky-test bug was found and fixed in `m17i_test.gd` at the start of the `[M17j]` session (Section 9's `S9.02` read post-battle HP instead of snapshotting via signal — see `[M17j]`'s addendum in decisions.md); the 1584 total above already reflects the fix.
- M17j (Item-transfer primitive — new infrastructure — Pickpocket / Sticky Hold / Magician / Symbiosis): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-03. Fifth genuinely new-infrastructure tier in M17. Step 0 re-verified all four IDs against Section 13's exclusion sweep — none needed correction (Pickpocket's ID is defined symbolically in source, independently recounted to confirm it resolves to 124). Traced four genuinely different shapes rather than one uniform "steal" ability: Pickpocket (defender-keyed reactive, steals the attacker's item on a contact hit — folded into the existing `try_contact_effects` dispatch), Magician (genuinely attacker-keyed — the opposite direction from every existing entry in `try_contact_effects`/`try_hit_reactive_effects` — steals the target's item on any damaging hit, contact not required; needed a new top-level `try_magician` called directly from `_do_damaging_hit`), Sticky Hold (a passive blocker, not a trigger — gates whether Pickpocket/Magician's steal is allowed), Symbiosis (doubles-only voluntary give, not a steal — fires when an ally's item is removed by any means). New shared primitive `AbilityManager._try_steal_item(stealer, victim, ng_active)` mirrors source's `StealTargetItem` and is the ONE place Sticky Hold's block lives, reused by both Pickpocket and Magician rather than duplicated; Symbiosis uses a separate one-directional "give" (mirrors `BestowItem`) since Sticky Hold does NOT gate a voluntary give. Confirmed all three transfer functions reuse the existing `BattlePokemon.held_item` field directly — no parallel item-tracking mechanism. Per the `[M17h]`-established dormant-field-check discipline, confirmed no `AbilityData` field exists for "item cannot be removed" (Sticky Hold's block is a direct ability-ID check, the same precedent `[M17f]`'s trapping check set) — but source-verified that Sticky Hold DOES correctly carry the *existing* `breakable=true` flag, traced through to confirm it has no reachable consumer among these four abilities' own dispatches (would only matter for a future Knock-Off/Thief-style move, none of which exist yet) — untested-but-implemented, not a silently-dropped check. New `BattleManager.item_transferred` signal and `_try_symbiosis` wrapper (called from `_consume_item`'s single existing choke point, plus directly after Pickpocket/Magician's steals). New `m17j_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 48/48 assertions (ability data; direct unit tests for all three trigger abilities including a real `DamageCalculator.calculate()`-driven type-immunity test for Magician; full-battle Pickpocket; full-battle Sticky-Hold-blocks-Pickpocket with a source-verified role correction — Sticky Hold belongs on the ATTACKER being stolen from, since Pickpocket's holder is always the one hit; full-battle Magician; a chained doubles scenario where Magician's steal triggers Symbiosis; Neutralizing Gas suppression of all three). A quick, targeted check of `switch_test.tscn`'s long-standing unresolved flakiness (piggybacking on the m17i_test.gd bug fresh in mind) found the same superficial shape in Section 5A's post-battle field reads but confirmed it's not actually exploitable given that test's move roster — checked and ruled out, not re-fixed. Total assertions across all 31 `.tscn` files: 1584 prior + 48 = **1632**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17j]` entry for full source citations.
- M17k (Priority-move-block check — new infrastructure — Dazzling / Queenly Majesty / Armor Tail): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-03. Sixth genuinely new-infrastructure tier in M17. Step 0 re-verified all three IDs (literal, not symbolic) against Section 13's exclusion sweep — none needed correction. Confirmed from source (`IsDazzlingAbility`, battle_move_resolution.c L1499-1509) — not assumed — that all three share the exact same dispatch, genuinely identical mechanic. New `AbilityManager.blocks_priority_move(defender, defender_ally, attacker, move, ng_active)` mirrors source's `CancelerPriorityBlock`: an EXECUTION-TIME gate (dispatched before `CancelerAccuracyCheck` in source's canceler chain — confirmed via `sMoveSuccessOrderCancelers`'s fixed ordering), not a selection-time block, so the move is chosen normally and then fails, mirroring this project's existing "chosen, then fails" pattern (Roar's `no_switch_target`) rather than a pre-move `move_skipped` cancellation. Gated on `move.priority > 0` only. Confirmed SIDE-WIDE from source (matches Queenly Majesty's own "targeting the user or an ally" framing): the check covers both the move's actual target and that target's doubles partner, not holder-only — verified with a dedicated full-battle doubles test where the direct target holds no ability at all but its ally holds Dazzling, and the priority move still fails. Confirmed the block never affects the holder's own outgoing priority moves. Confirmed via `[M16d]`/`[M16e]` cross-reference that this is a structurally different concern from turn-order/speed-sorting (Trick Room, Pursuit) — no changes to `_phase_priority_resolution`'s comparator were needed. Verified the source's field-targeting-move exclusion (Trick Room/hazards) is already non-applicable here since none of this project's three field-targeting moves has positive priority — a confirmed-non-applicable simplification, not an assumed one. All three abilities carry `breakable=true`, and — unlike Sticky Hold's non-applicable case in `[M17j]` — this one is genuinely, immediately reachable (attacker and Dazzling-family holder are always different battlers), so a Mold-Breaker-holding attacker correctly bypasses the block, verified with a dedicated unit test. Per the `[M17h]`-established dormant-field-check discipline, confirmed no `AbilityData` field applies (a direct ability-ID check, same precedent as `[M17f]`'s trapping and `[M17j]`'s Sticky Hold). New `m17k_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 26/26 assertions (ability data; direct unit tests including the side-wide/fainted-ally/Mold-Breaker-bypass/Neutralizing-Gas-suppression cases; full-battle priority-blocked, priority-zero-not-blocked, side-wide doubles, holder's-own-move-unaffected, and a negative control). Baseline reconfirmed exactly at 31 files/1632 assertions before starting (no drift this time). Total assertions across all 32 `.tscn` files: 1632 prior + 26 = **1658**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17k]` entry for full source citations.
- M17l (Doubles-redirect/aura abilities — Lightning Rod / Storm Drain / Friend Guard / Telepathy / Propeller Tail / Stalwart): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-03. Unlike every tier since `[M17f]`, this one's task explicitly asked to VERIFY rather than assume "no new infrastructure" — verified directly: none was needed. Step 0 found nothing to correct (first time since `[M17d]`) — all six literal IDs clean against Section 13. Two genuinely different mechanic shapes plus a separate pair: Lightning Rod/Storm Drain are redirect-TRIGGER abilities (defender-side) that both redirect a matching-type move onto themselves (doubles only) AND fully absorb + Sp.Atk+1 whenever hit directly or by redirect (two separate source functions, `CanAbilityAbsorbMove` + `HandleMoveTargetRedirection`); Propeller Tail/Stalwart are redirect-BYPASS abilities (attacker-side, the opposite direction) — confirmed genuinely identical from source, not assumed. Telepathy (a damage exemption when the target is the attacker's own ally — source-verified NOT gated on the move being a spread move specifically, despite the flavor text) and Friend Guard (×0.75 reduction for the defender when the defender's ALLY holds it, not the holder's own damage) are a separate, unrelated pair. Checked this project's EXISTING Follow Me/Rage Powder implementation (`[M14b]`) for redirect precedence, per the task's explicit instruction — confirmed from source that Follow Me takes precedence over the ability-redirect, and Propeller Tail/Stalwart bypass both identically; wired accordingly. **No new infrastructure**: every mechanic reuses an existing pipeline hook — `absorbs_move_type`/`blocks_ally_damage` slot into `DamageCalculator`'s existing early ability-immunity gate (alongside Levitate); Friend Guard reuses the existing `defender_ally` parameter (`[M17c]`'s Flower Gift); Telepathy reuses the existing `ally` parameter (`[M17a]`'s Battery/Power Spot/Steely Spirit) with zero new plumbing; the redirect functions extend the existing Follow Me block in `_phase_move_execution` rather than adding a parallel path. Confirmed Lightning Rod/Storm Drain/Friend Guard/Telepathy all correctly carry `breakable=true` and are genuinely, immediately reachable Mold-Breaker-bypass cases (verified with dedicated tests for both the absorb and the redirect); Propeller Tail/Stalwart correctly carry no such flag. New `m17l_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 45/45 assertions across 12 sections (ability data; direct unit tests for all four mechanic shapes including Mold-Breaker-bypass and Neutralizing-Gas-suppression; full-battle doubles redirect+boost for both Lightning Rod and Storm Drain; Lightning Rod's direct-hit absorb confirmed working in singles too; Telepathy blocking an ally's attack but not an opponent's; Friend Guard's deterministic damage-reduction proof; Propeller Tail bypassing Lightning Rod's redirect — the tier's key cross-ability interaction; a negative control). Caught and fixed a real test-authoring bug during this tier (same class as `[M17j]`'s `switch_test.tscn` finding): two negative "never hit" assertions read events accumulated across the WHOLE battle rather than the specific queued turn-1 action, and failed intermittently once the original redirect target fainted in later turns and the single-move attacker legitimately retargeted the ability holder directly — fixed by filtering to each attacker's first recorded event. Stable across 8 reruns post-fix. Baseline reconfirmed exactly at 32 files/1658 assertions before starting (no drift). Total assertions across all 33 `.tscn` files: 1658 prior + 45 = **1703**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17l]` entry for full source citations, including a flagged finding for M17m: Volt Absorb/Water Absorb/Sap Sipper/Flash Fire/Motor Drive/Well-Baked Body all share the exact same source dispatch (`CanAbilityAbsorbMove`) this tier's `absorbs_move_type` already partially extended.
- M17m (Absorb-family abilities — Volt Absorb / Water Absorb / Sap Sipper / Flash Fire / Motor Drive / Well-Baked Body / Earth Eater / Dry Skin's water half): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-04. Pre-recon (`docs/m17m_absorb_recon.md`) run first, then re-verified fresh at Step 0 per standing discipline. **Scope note**: the recon's original M17m proposal was ~15 abilities (also Wonder Guard, Scrappy, Overcoat, Normalize+the "-ate" family, Mind's Eye) — this session narrowed scope to just the absorb family; those five remain unimplemented and unscheduled (see `docs/decisions.md` [M17m]'s "Next tier" section — NOT covered by M17n either). All eight route through the same source dispatch (`CanAbilityAbsorbMove`) `[M17l]`'s Lightning Rod/Storm Drain already partially extended, but split into three genuinely different on-absorb effect shapes: heal maxHP/4 (Volt Absorb/Water Absorb/Earth Eater, plus Dry Skin's previously-deferred water half — the same divisor, confirmed distinct from Dry Skin's own end-of-turn /8 tick), stat-stage boost of VARYING magnitude (Sap Sipper Atk+1, Motor Drive Speed+1 — confirmed NOT Sp.Atk despite the type overlap with Lightning Rod — Well-Baked Body Def **+2**, the tier's flagged highest-risk detail), and a persistent flag with a delayed payoff (Flash Fire — new `BattlePokemon.flash_fire_active`, cleared by `_clear_volatiles` like `minimized`/`defense_curled`; its own later Fire-move ×1.5 boost wired into the EXISTING `attack_modifier_uq412`, the same function Overgrow/Blaze/Torrent/Swarm occupy — confirmed a separate source function from the absorb dispatch itself). **Cross-cutting design decision**: widened `AbilityManager.absorbs_move_type`'s return type from a bare `int` to a `Dictionary` (`{}`/`{"kind": "stat"/"heal"/"flag", ...}`) to express all three shapes through one function, matching source's single dispatch — a deliberate breaking change to `[M17l]`'s existing contract, with its one call site and six direct unit-test assertions updated in place (`m17l_test` reran unchanged at 45/45). A second, unavoidable existing-test update: `m17c_test.gd`'s Dry Skin water-move assertion directly encoded the old "not implemented, deferred" premise as a passing test — now permanently false, so it was updated in place to assert the new absorbed-hit reality (not duplicated elsewhere; `m17c_test` reran at 79/79). New `m17m_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 63/63 assertions across 17 sections (ability data; direct `absorbs_move_type`/`attack_modifier_uq412` unit tests per group incl. Motor Drive's not-Sp.Atk and Well-Baked Body's not-+1 discriminators; Mold Breaker bypass and Neutralizing Gas suppression per group; full-battle heal-delta tests for Volt Absorb (incl. a full-HP-still-absorbs case), Water Absorb, Earth Eater, and a DEDICATED Dry Skin water-absorb test kept separate from `[M17c]`'s existing coverage; full-battle stat-boost tests for Sap Sipper/Motor Drive/Well-Baked Body; full-battle Flash Fire absorb plus a direct `DamageCalculator` comparison proving the later ×1.5 boost is real; a negative control). One anomaly investigated and ruled out: `doubles_test.tscn` failed once (53/54) with zero references to any of this tier's abilities, then reran clean 6/6 times — the same pre-existing RNG-flakiness class already documented for `switch_test.tscn`. Total assertions across all 34 `.tscn` files: 1703 prior + 63 = **1766**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17m]` entry for full source citations. **M17n (unique/grab-bag, ~50+ abilities) is next** — will need its own sub-tier-splitting pass before implementation, not attempted here; whoever picks it up should also re-decide the fate of the five abilities flagged above as unscheduled.

- M17n-1 (Group 1: status-immunity family + simple no-ops — Insomnia/Vital Spirit/Immunity/Limber/Water Veil/Magma Armor/Inner Focus/Own Tempo/Shield Dust/Leaf Guard/Early Bird/Aroma Veil/Soundproof/Bulletproof/Illuminate/Honey Gather/Oblivious/Cute Charm/Damp/Run Away/Pickup/Ball Fetch): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-04. Ran FIRST among M17n's sub-tiers (ability-ID-group order) rather than the recon's own risk-based recommendation (Group 5 first) — a deliberate sequencing choice by the task, not an oversight. Four categories: genuine status-immunity abilities (12, extending `StatusManager.try_apply_status`/`try_apply_confusion`, the same shape `[M17b]`'s Purifying Salt/Sweet Veil/Pastel Veil already established); move-flag immunity (Soundproof/Bulletproof — a real Step-0 finding cut this tier's cost: `MoveData` already had dormant `sound_move`/`ballistic_move`/`biting_move`/`punching_move`/etc. fields since the original schema, so ZERO new `MoveData` flags were needed, just a new `AbilityManager.blocks_move_flag` wired before the accuracy check); documented cosmetic no-ops (Illuminate/Honey Gather, matching the Anticipation/Forewarn/Frisk precedent); and abilities confirmed genuinely out-of-battle-engine scope (Run Away/Pickup/Ball Fetch — deliberately given NO constant or `.tres` entry at all, unlike the no-ops). Two real findings beyond the recon's own scope: (1) all seven status/confusion-immunity abilities ALSO cure a matching pre-existing condition on switch-in (`TryImmunityAbilityHealStatus`, a genuinely separate trigger point from infliction-blocking, extending `try_switch_in` with two new result keys); (2) Inner Focus/Own Tempo/Oblivious fully block Intimidate's Attack drop under this project's GEN_LATEST config (`IsIntimidateBlocked`) — found while checking Oblivious's assumed-no-op scope, turned out to be a real, currently-buildable mechanic. A source-verified discrepancy was flagged (not silently resolved): Aroma Veil's AI-facing effect list includes Disable/Encore, but the actual pokeemerald_expansion execution commands for those two never check it (only Attract/Torment's own commands do) — implemented matching the AI's real-intended-behavior list, via a new `MoveData.blocked_by_aroma_veil` flag designed to auto-extend to Taunt/Torment/Heal Block later. Retroactively fixed a real pre-existing gap: Ice Ball's `ballistic_move` flag was cited in a comment since `[M16b]` but never actually set on the data dict. New `m17n1_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 75/75 assertions across 20 sections (ability data; direct unit tests per Category-A ability with a discriminating negative case; Leaf Guard's sun-gate; Early Bird's decrement-rate comparison; the switch-in-cure section; full-battle Intimidate-block/Aroma-Veil-block/Soundproof/Bulletproof tests; Mold Breaker bypass and Neutralizing Gas suppression per category; a negative control). Caught and fixed a real bug on the first run (73/75): the new move-flag-block signal emitted with `attacker` instead of `defender` (copied from `[M17k]`'s `blocks_priority_move` precedent, which itself uses `attacker` — but this codebase's OTHER defender-side blocks like `aroma_veil_blocked`/`immune` correctly use `defender`), fixed in the implementation to match that closer precedent. - M17n-2 (Group 2: weather/evasion + speed family, plus Air Lock — Sand Veil/Snow Cloak/Swift Swim/Chlorophyll/Sand Rush/Air Lock/Cloud Nine/Sand Spit): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-04. Air Lock confirmed as Section 13.1's established KEPT precedent (not itself excluded, despite the Rayquaza association) — re-read directly rather than assumed. Cloud Nine/Air Lock confirmed genuinely identical from source (the literal same `HasWeatherEffect` case branch, no asymmetry). Three shapes: weather-conditional Speed doublers (Swift Swim/Chlorophyll/Sand Rush, extending `[M17c]`'s Slush Rush precedent in `StatusManager.effective_speed` — a source-verified nuance NOT shared uniformly: Swift Swim/Chlorophyll additionally respect the HOLDER's own Utility Umbrella, since Umbrella only ever strips rain/sun, while Sand Rush/Slush Rush's sandstorm/hail conditions are untouched by it); weather-conditional evasion (Sand Veil/Snow Cloak, extending `[M17a]`'s Compound Eyes/Hustle precedent in `AbilityManager.accuracy_modifier_percent`, now also defender-aware); and a reactive weather-setter (Sand Spit, reusing the EXISTING `try_set_weather` Drizzle/Drought/Sand Stream already use). **The key design decision**: rather than retrofitting Air Lock/Cloud Nine awareness into every individual weather-conditional ability, new `BattleManager._effective_weather()` substitutes `WEATHER_NONE` at the small number of call sites that thread `weather` into a downstream ability function — covering `DamageCalculator.calculate` (Flower Gift/Solar Power/Dry Skin/Delta Stream, for free), `try_end_of_turn` (Rain Dish/Ice Body/Dry Skin heal, for free), the end-of-turn sandstorm/hail chip check, `try_secondary_effect` (Leaf Guard, for free), and `effective_speed`/`check_accuracy` (this tier's own abilities plus Slush Rush for free) — all without touching any of those functions' own code. Confirmed from source that weather-SETTING itself (Sand Spit, Drizzle, etc.) is unaffected by Air Lock/Cloud Nine — only weather's effects are negated — so `try_set_weather` was correctly left untouched. New `m17n2_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 41/41 assertions across 14 sections, including the tier's explicitly-requested key cross-ability test (Air Lock present negates Swift Swim's speed-doubling, restoring normal turn order despite rain being active) plus full-battle confirmation of Air Lock negating both the weather damage multiplier and end-of-turn chip damage. Caught and fixed a real flaky-test bug during reruns (not the first run): a full-battle damage-comparison test forced the damage roll but not the crit chance, so an occasional natural crit inflated damage above its forced-roll baseline — fixed by also forcing `_force_crit = false`; stable across 8 reruns after. Baseline reconfirmed exactly at 35 files/1841 assertions before starting (no drift). Total assertions across all 36 `.tscn` files: 1841 prior + 41 = 1882, all green. **Follow-up (2026-07-04, same day)**: the Air Lock/Sand Spit interaction — checked post-hoc via a manual scratch scene, never committed — was formalized into a permanent `m17n2_test.gd` Section 15 (5 new assertions, test-only, no production code changed): a 2-member-bench battle where the Air Lock holder's HP is tuned via a direct `DamageCalculator` probe to survive exactly 3 hits and faint on the 4th, checked via signal-ordering (not turn-counting) against a tagged event log. Confirms Sandstorm is genuinely set despite Air Lock's presence (weather-SETTING is confirmed from source to be unaffected by Air Lock/Cloud Nine — only the read side, `GetWeather()`, is filtered) and that chip damage resumes the moment Air Lock leaves the field. Reran 8 consecutive times, stable. Total assertions across all 36 `.tscn` files: 1882 prior − 41 (old `m17n2_test` count) + 46 (new count) = **1887**, all green. **Follow-up (2026-07-05, found during `[M17n-6]`'s Overcoat work, fixed here)**: this tier's original conclusion that Sand Veil/Sand Rush grant no sandstorm-chip immunity was WRONG — current source (`battle_end_turn.c :: HandleEndTurnWeatherDamage` L143-169) explicitly exempts Sand Veil/Sand Force/Sand Rush from sandstorm chip and Snow Cloak from hail chip, the same shape as Overcoat's own exemption. Fixed via a new `weather` param on `AbilityManager.blocks_weather_chip_damage` (the function `[M17n-6]` built for Overcoat); the stale code comment in `BattleManager._phase_end_of_turn` was corrected. New `m17n2_test.gd` Section 16 (12 new assertions, 58 total in the file): per-ability direct tests with a same-other-weather discriminator each, one Neutralizing-Gas-suppression test, and two full-battle confirmations (Sand Rush/sandstorm, Snow Cloak/hail) each paired with a plain-Pokémon control. Stable across 5 reruns; `m17n6_test.tscn` also rerun 5 times to confirm no regression in Overcoat's own weather-chip/Air-Lock composition test. Total assertions across all 40 `.tscn` files: 2172 prior + 12 = **2184**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-2]` entry (including both follow-up subsections) for full source citations.
- M17n-3 (Group 3: turn-order/priority modifiers — Prankster/Gale Wings/Triage/Quick Draw/Stall/Mycelium Might): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-04. Two shapes: priority-bonus abilities (Gale Wings +1 Flying-type-at-full-HP, Prankster +1 status-category, Triage +3 healing_move-flagged — new `AbilityManager.move_priority_bonus`, wired into `_phase_priority_resolution`'s `pa`/`pb` computation) and same-priority-bracket tiebreak abilities (Quick Draw 30% act-first on non-status moves, Stall always-last unconditionally, Mycelium Might always-last ONLY when its own chosen move is status-category — a source-verified nuance NOT shared with Stall — new `AbilityManager.quick_draw_activates`/`has_slow_turn_order_effect`, precomputed once per battler per turn into Dictionaries before the sort, checked strictly before the speed/Trick-Room comparison). Mycelium Might's second half (ignores the target's ability while using a status move) extends `effective_ability_id` with a new optional `attacker_move` param, threaded through `try_apply_status`/`try_apply_confusion`/`try_secondary_effect`; verified end-to-end bypassing Limber via Thunder Wave. Wired the previously-dormant `MoveData.healing_move` flag onto Recover/Slack Off/Heal Order (the only 3 of source's 24 flagged moves in this project's roster). **A real cross-tier gap was found and fixed**: `[M17k]`'s `blocks_priority_move` checked raw `move.priority` instead of the same ability-boosted priority that feeds turn-order sorting (source's `CancelerPriorityBlock` computes its priority via the identical `GetChosenMovePriority` function) — unreachable at `[M17k]`'s own implementation time, now fixed via the same `move_priority_bonus` helper; a null-attacker/null-mon crash surfaced by `[M17k]`'s own pre-existing sanity-check test was also caught and fixed with defensive null guards. Confirmed Trick Room's speed-tiebreak inversion never overrides the priority-bracket comparison (even ability-boosted) and confirmed Stall's slow-effect overrides Trick Room's own tiebreak preference too; confirmed Pursuit is structurally disjoint (no dedicated test needed). New `m17n3_test.gd` Section 17 (8 assertions, 62 total in the file), stable across 6 reruns. (2) Explicit sequencing comparison, re-verified against the current codebase rather than the recon's original framing: Group 7 (Color Change/Protean/Libero/Multitype/RKS System/Gorilla Tactics, 6 abilities) needs ZERO new infrastructure (confirmed `_set_mon_type`/`_reset_mon_type`/`original_types`/`is_choice_item` all still exist unchanged), while Group 4 (27 abilities) contains at least one genuinely new mechanism (the Ruin quartet's field-aura shape) alongside its otherwise-`[M17a]`-shaped abilities — Group 7 is the more natural next step, not Group 4; see `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-3]` follow-up subsection for the full comparison. Total assertions across all 37 `.tscn` files: 1941 prior − 54 (old `m17n3_test` count) + 62 (new count) = **1949**, all green. **M17n-4 (Group 7: type-mutation/choice-lock cheap reuses, 6 abilities)** was queued next here but was **NOT implemented at the time** — see the `[M17n-5]` entry below, which found this gap still open at the start of its own session and proceeded past it per explicit instruction. **Resolved in a later session** — see the M17n-4 status line immediately below, inserted in its correct chronological position; the gap is now closed.
- M17n-4 (Group 7: type-mutation/choice-lock cheap reuses — Color Change/Protean/Libero/Multitype/Gorilla Tactics): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-04. Inserted here in its correct chronological position even though implemented in a later session than `[M17n-5]` below — this tier was originally queued to run BEFORE `[M17n-5]` but didn't; the gap is now closed, not relitigated. 5 abilities, not 6 — RKS System (225) excluded per Rob's explicit decision (recorded in memory). Zero new `BattleManager` mechanisms: Color Change/Protean/Libero/Multitype all reuse the EXISTING `_set_mon_type`/`_reset_mon_type`/`BattlePokemon.original_types` infrastructure (`[M16e]`/follow-up-fixes), Gorilla Tactics reuses the EXISTING `BattlePokemon.choice_locked_move` field (`[M12]`). Color Change extends `try_hit_reactive_effects` (fires on any damaging hit, gated on not-already-that-type/not-Struggle/not-Stellar-Mystery; confirmed via source that a Ghost-vs-Normal immune hit — 0 damage — correctly never reaches it). Protean/Libero confirmed genuinely the SAME source function/condition (`ProteanTryChangeType`), not flavor-text twins; new `BattlePokemon.used_protean_libero` gate wired into `_phase_move_execution` right after the choice-lock block (matching `CANCELER_PROTEAN`'s early position in source, before accuracy/Protect checks) — source's own code comment says "once per Battle" but the flag lives in the same `Volatiles` struct that's memset at every switch-in, so it's operationally once-per-switch-in-stint, confirmed by tracing the actual clear mechanism rather than trusting the comment. Multitype wired into `_apply_switch_in_abilities` (switch-in only) reading a new `ItemManager.HOLD_EFFECT_PLATE`/`multitype_plate_type` (reusing `hold_effect_param` for the type, the same pragmatic field-repurposing already established for Resist Berry, since this project has neither Judgment nor Natural Gift to need the source field's literal purpose) — **a real correction to this tier's own inherited assumption**: confirmed via a full `TryBattleFormChange` call-site enumeration that `FORM_CHANGE_ITEM_HOLD` is an OVERWORLD-only trigger, never dispatched in-battle, so a mid-battle held-item change (Trick, Knock Off, this project's own `[M17j]` Pickpocket/Magician/Symbiosis) does NOT retype a Multitype holder — verified with a real Magician-driven theft integration test, not just asserted. Multitype's `cant_be_suppressed=true` (source-faithful) means Neutralizing Gas correctly does NOT suppress it, unlike the other four. Gorilla Tactics confirmed via source to share the LITERAL SAME `choicedMove` storage slot as an item-based choice lock (an OR condition, not two locks) — extended the existing gate directly; its physical-move base-power ×1.5 (`move_power_modifier_uq412`) is a different pipeline stage from Choice Band/Specs' attack-stat modifier, and composes multiplicatively to 2.25× with an actual Choice item exactly as source's own test confirms — verified with a dedicated integration test, no special-case stacking code needed since the two stages already multiply independently. New `m17n4_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 44/44 assertions across 9 sections (ability data incl. Multitype's full 5-flag set; Color Change incl. the deliberate Ghost-vs-Normal immune-hit negative case and a same-defender second-hit-different-type re-trigger; Protean direct-function unit tests plus a full-battle first-use/no-second-use pair and a switch-out/switch-in stint-reset proof; Libero confirming the identical mechanism and its own `"libero"` signal tag; Multitype's Plate-driven type, no-Plate default, and the key does-NOT-live-update Magician-theft integration test; Gorilla Tactics' lock/boost/Choice-Band-composition trio; Mold Breaker non-bypass and Neutralizing Gas suppression incl. Multitype's asymmetric exemption; a negative control). Caught and fixed one real test-authoring bug on the first run (43/44): the Color Change re-trigger test queued only 2 actions but asserted the resulting event array had exactly 2 entries; once the queue drained the battle continued and the attacker auto-selected its first move again, firing a 3rd event — the same "repeatable-effect auto-select" pitfall CLAUDE.md's snapshot-via-signals section already documents, fixed by checking only the first two recorded events. Stable across 6 reruns. Baseline reconfirmed exactly at 38 files/2027 assertions before starting (no drift; the documented `doubles_test.tscn` flake recurred once and reran clean immediately after — the same known non-blocking class). Total assertions across all 39 `.tscn` files: 2027 prior + 44 = **2071**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-4]` entry for full source citations.
- M17n-5 (Group 4: damage-pipeline leftovers — Sturdy/Iron Fist/Technician/Reckless/Sheer Force/Analytic/Tangled Feet/Strong Jaw/Mega Launcher/Stakeout/Long Reach/Fluffy/Punk Rock/Sharpness/Slow Start/Serene Grace/Super Luck): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-04. Ran instead of the still-outstanding M17n-4 (Group 7), per explicit instruction — see the flagged gap above. Two real discrepancies found and resolved at Step 0: the task's own count (19) didn't match its own 18-name enumeration (this project's re-derivation also lands on 18, not 19); of those 18, Skill Link (92) was further deferred — confirmed via grep that no multi-hit mechanic exists anywhere in this codebase's battle logic (`multi_hit`/`strike_count` are dormant `MoveData` schema fields only), so it has nothing to modify. **17 abilities actually implemented.** Mechanism shapes: attacker move-power modifiers (`move_power_modifier_uq412`: Iron Fist/Technician/Reckless/Sheer Force incl. its own secondary-effect suppression/Strong Jaw/Mega Launcher, new `pulse_move` flag/Punk Rock's own half/Sharpness/Analytic); attacker stat modifier (`attack_modifier_uq412`, new `defender` param: Stakeout, Slow Start's Atk half); defender damage modifiers (`defense_damage_modifier_uq412`: Fluffy — confirmed a contact Fire move triggers NEITHER of its two mutually-exclusive branches, netting ×1.0, not both stacking to cancel out — and Punk Rock's defense half); crit stage (`DamageCalculator._roll_crit`: Super Luck, additive with Focus Energy); accuracy (`accuracy_modifier_percent`: Tangled Feet, reusing Sand Veil/Snow Cloak's exact hook); a new shared `AbilityManager.move_makes_contact` helper (Long Reach, wired into the 3 real contact-flag read sites); the first "survive a lethal hit" mechanism this project builds (Sturdy, both the full-HP-gated endure half and the unconditional OHKO-block half); a new `slow_start_timer` volatile (Slow Start's Speed half + the 5-turn switch-in/end-of-turn lifecycle); and a secondary-chance doubler with an explicit 100% cap (Serene Grace). Also closed a real dormant-flag gap: `biting_move`/`slicing_move` existed in the `MoveData` schema but were never wired into `gen_moves.py` (same class of gap `[M17n-3]` closed for `healing_move`); `pulse_move` was genuinely new. No move in this project's current roster carries any of the three flags — Strong Jaw/Sharpness/Mega Launcher are tested via synthetic `MoveData`. New `m17n5_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 78/78 assertions across 20 sections, including two genuinely new testing patterns for this codebase — statistical-sample rate tests for Super Luck/Serene Grace (no prior suite tests a probabilistic rate directly) and a signal-snapshot fix for Sturdy caught on the very first run (post-battle-state would see the holder fainted, since Sturdy only protects the first lethal hit). Stable across 10 reruns. Baseline reconfirmed exactly at 37 files/1949 assertions before starting (no drift). Total assertions across all 38 `.tscn` files: 1949 prior + 78 = **2027**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-5]` entry for full source citations, including the then-still-open Group 7 gap (**resolved** in a later session — see the M17n-4 status line immediately below, inserted in its correct chronological position between M17n-3 and this entry).
- M17n-6 (Group 5: type-effectiveness-pipeline leftovers — Wonder Guard / Scrappy / Overcoat / Normalize / Refrigerate / Pixilate / Galvanize / Aerilate / Dragonize / Liquid Voice / Mind's Eye, 11 abilities): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-05, with a same-day follow-up adding Aerilate and Dragonize. The highest-risk remaining tier in all of M17, per both `[M17l]`'s and `[M17m]`'s own advance flags — required a genuine pipeline restructure, not just a new branch. Wonder Guard's check (`AbilityManager.blocks_non_super_effective_hit`) reads the FULL combined type-effectiveness multiplier AFTER `TypeChart.get_effectiveness` computes it in `DamageCalculator.calculate`, unlike every prior ability-immunity gate (Levitate/absorb-family/Telepathy), which are flat 0x-or-nothing checks positioned BEFORE that value exists; confirmed it still blocks fixed/level-damage moves (Night Shade etc., which carry the same `power=1` placeholder as source) while correctly exempting status moves (power=0) and Struggle (TYPE_MYSTERY). Scrappy/Mind's Eye's Ghost-immunity bypass is threaded as a new `bypass_ghost_immunity` param into BOTH of this project's independent type-effectiveness computations (`TypeChart.get_effectiveness` and `get_uq412`), mirroring the Delta Stream `weaken_flying_se` precedent; Mind's Eye's second, independent half (evasion-ignore) simply extends the pre-existing `ignores_defender_evasion_stage` function, whose own doc comment had already anticipated this. Overcoat is two independent halves (powder-move immunity via the existing `blocks_move_flag`/dormant `powder_move` flag; weather-chip immunity as a new per-mon exemption alongside Air Lock/Cloud Nine's field-wide negation, confirmed non-conflicting via a dedicated composition test) — a real discrepancy was found and initially FLAGGED, not fixed, here: current reference source lists Sand Veil/Sand Force/Sand Rush/Snow Cloak as weather-chip exemptions too, directly contradicting `[M17n-2]`'s already-shipped "neither grants chip immunity" finding (**since fixed** — see `[M17n-2]`'s own status line above and its decisions.md follow-up); also flagged (still not fixed): Overcoat's un-modeled Effect Spore interaction. Normalize/Refrigerate/Pixilate/Galvanize/Liquid Voice (plus, from the same-day follow-up, Aerilate and Dragonize) mutate the MOVE's own effective type — implemented via a shallow-duplicated `MoveData` (only `.type` overridden) substituted for `DamageCalculator.calculate`'s own `move` parameter, so every existing type-aware ability/item check downstream sees the mutated type for free, with zero changes to any of them; confirmed all six power-boosting members (including Normalize itself, symmetrically) share the exact same ×1.2/UQ4.12=4915 value, and that Normalize boosts literally every move it uses (even an already-Normal one) since its own branch is unconditional on the original type, unlike the "-ate" family's. A real test-authoring bug was caught on the first run: comparing a Pixilate'd/Liquid-Voice'd move's damage against a single-Normal-typed attacker confounds the power-boost measurement with a STAB loss (mutating away from the attacker's own type loses STAB) — fixed by using a dual-typed attacker so STAB holds constant across the comparison. **Follow-up (same day)**: Aerilate (184, Mega-exclusivity exclusion reversed by Rob) and Dragonize (312) added, reusing this tier's exact infrastructure — Dragonize's own ID was flagged BEFORE implementing, since direct source inspection shows it sitting in `pokeemerald_expansion`'s own cluster of 6 hack-project-only custom ability slots (`m17_recon.md` Section 8.3's original exclusion, independently re-confirmed: no `aiRating` field, flanked by two literal blank `"-------"` placeholder slots and two abilities whose source description is literally `"Unimplemented."`); Rob confirmed implementing it anyway as a deliberate override (Dragonize has since become real in a newer generation than this reference tree models). New `m17n6_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 101/101 assertions across 22 sections (95 original + 6 from the follow-up), stable across 8 reruns (original) and 5 reruns (follow-up). Baseline reconfirmed exactly at 39 files/2071 assertions before starting (no drift). Targeted regression (`ability_test`/`m17a_test`/`m17m_test`/`m17n2_test`) plus two full 40-file sweeps (original + follow-up) all passed unchanged (0 real failures — one grep false-positive on `stat_test.tscn`'s own "fail at +6 max"-style test labels, confirmed harmless). Total assertions across all 40 `.tscn` files: 2071 prior + 95 + 6 = **2172**, all green. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-6]` entry (and its same-day follow-up subsection) for full source citations.
- M17n-7 (Group 6: item/berry interaction — Klutz / Unnerve / Gluttony / Unburden / Harvest / Cud Chew): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-06, a recovery-and-completion session (a prior session's implementation work was found already in the working tree, uncommitted, with no test file or decisions.md entry — re-verified from scratch against `include/constants/abilities.h` and source rather than trusted at face value). Step 0 confirmed all six IDs clean; none carry `breakable`/`cant_be_suppressed`. Klutz (`ItemManager.effective_held_item`, the single held-item chokepoint every other function already routes through) and Unnerve (blocks ALL berry effects via source's single `ItemBattleEffects` dispatcher gate, not just resist berries — already correctly scoped in the inherited code) both verified correct as found. Gluttony confirmed a no-op for this project's entire current item roster (Sitrus's fraction is hardcoded to 2 regardless of ability), wired in generically per the Sticky-Hold precedent. Unburden's unconditional Speed ×2 (`battle_main.c` L4686-4687) verified wired into `StatusManager.effective_speed`, activated via `CheckSetUnburden`'s every-item-removal-site pattern. Harvest finally builds the "last consumed berry" tracker `[M17d]` deferred twice — `BattlePokemon.last_consumed_berry`, confirmed against `include/battle.h`'s `struct PartyState` to be genuinely switch-persistent (unlike Unburden/Cud Chew's own switch-cleared volatiles). **A real bug was found and fixed** (not merely inherited-and-confirmed like the rest of this tier): Cud Chew's re-trigger sets source's `overrideBerryRequirements` flag, which makes BOTH the HP-threshold check AND the Unnerve check return unconditionally-bypassed (`battle_util.c` L5465, L338-339) — the inherited `sitrus_berry_heal`/`lum_berry_cures` calls still applied both gates unconditionally even with `override_item` set. Fixed by gating both checks on `override_item == null`, preserving only the one source-verified exception (no heal at exactly full HP even under override). New `m17n7_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 62/62 assertions across 13 sections including a dedicated discriminating test for the bug fix (Section 10: the bypass itself plus a without-override negative control proving it wasn't vacuous). Two test-authoring bugs caught and fixed on the first run (59/62): an out-of-domain Gluttony fraction test, and hardcoded (rather than dynamically read) Speed values for the Unburden test. A baseline discrepancy was found during this session and initially "resolved" by adopting a fresh recount of 2160 — **that figure was itself wrong**, confirmed by a dedicated follow-up diagnostic session (2026-07-06) that root-caused the recurring drift: `scenes/battle/integration_test.tscn` (24 real, always-passing assertions) prints a third result format (`"Integration tests: N passed, M failed"`) that every ad-hoc recount so far — including this tier's own 2160 figure — failed to recognize, silently dropping its 24 assertions. See CLAUDE.md's testing-conventions section for the full mechanism and the standing rule this established. Full regression: all 40 prior files pass unchanged (`item_test.tscn`, whose call sites this session's fix directly touched, reran clean at 77/77). **VERIFIED: 2246 total assertions across 41 `.tscn` files**, confirmed via two independent methods (`scripts/count_assertions.sh` against a fresh sweep, and a per-file instrumented-source cross-check) and reproducible across two independent clean runs (2026-07-06). See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-7]` entry for full source citations.
- M17n-8 (Group 8, sub-tier 1: contact/faint-timing + reactive/one-off — Aftermath / Innards Out / Corrosion / Merciless / Opportunist): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-06. Step 0 confirmed all five IDs clean against `include/constants/abilities.h`; Perish Body (blocked on the unimplemented Perish Song move) and Suction Cups (deferred) explicitly excluded from this sub-tier per Rob's instruction, not silently dropped. None of the five carry `breakable`/`cant_be_suppressed`. Aftermath/Innards Out share one mechanism (`AbilityManager.faint_retaliation_damage`, wired into `_phase_faint_check` alongside Destiny Bond/Moxie's existing `_last_attacker` killer-lookup) but differ in two source-verified ways: Aftermath requires contact and is blocked by any Damp holder on the field (new `is_damp_active`, NG-aware per source's `GetBattlerAbility`-routed `IsAbilityOnField`); Innards Out has neither restriction and deals the fainted mon's own HP immediately before the fatal hit (new `_last_attacker_hp_before`/`_last_attacker_move` companion trackers), not a fixed fraction — confirmed via a deliberate overkill full-battle test. Corrosion bypasses Poison/Steel-type poison immunity via the attacker's own ability (`bypasses_poison_steel_immunity`, mirroring Scrappy's `bypasses_ghost_immunity` precedent), closing a gap M3's own code comment flagged since this project's earliest milestone. **A second, genuinely independent bug was found and fixed** while writing Corrosion's full-battle test: `_phase_move_execution`'s own general "type immunity check for foe-targeting moves" ALSO blocks Toxic (Poison-type) against a Steel-type target (a real, separate 0x type-chart immunity, correct for cases like Thunder Wave vs. Ground) — entirely independent of the status-specific check Corrosion was wired into. Source confirmed `ABILITY_CORROSION` appears exactly once in the whole reference tree, and its failure branch reuses the same "doesn't affect" script a flat type immunity does — meaning real source resolves this through the ONE status-specific check with no separate downstream gate for this purpose. Fixed by threading the same Corrosion check into that general gate, scoped narrowly to Poison-type moves only. Merciless is a guaranteed (not stage-bonus) crit vs. a poisoned/toxic'd target, tested via a 30-trial statistical sample mirroring `[M17n-5]`'s rate-testing pattern. Opportunist copies an opponent's stat INCREASE only (never decreases, never self-triggers by construction — opponents-only scope) at the same primary move-driven stat-change site `[M17b]`'s Defiant/Competitive already occupy; deliberately not gated on `move.stat_change_self` (source cares which side rose, not whether the move was self-targeted) and confirmed no infinite-loop risk (the copy calls `apply_stat_change` directly, never re-entering the reactive dispatch). Known simplification, documented: wired into this one call site only, not retrofitted into every `apply_stat_change` call site — ability-driven raises (Moxie, Weak Armor, Download) and Baton-Pass/Psych-Up copies aren't covered. A real test-authoring bug (infinite-battle deadlock from a Swords-Dance-only moveset) was caught and fixed on the first run (55/58). New `m17n8_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 58/58 assertions across 11 sections, stable across 8 reruns. Full regression (direct foreground sweep, `pkill -9` first, `scripts/count_assertions.sh` against fresh output, re-run twice from a clean state): all 41 prior files pass unchanged, 0 real failures both runs. Total assertions across all 42 `.tscn` files: 2246 prior + 58 = **2304**, confirmed via `count_assertions.sh` and reproducible across both runs. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-8]` entry for full source citations.
- M17n-9 (Group 8, "wide-but-shallow systems" — Magic Guard / Infiltrator / Magic Bounce): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-06. Step 0 confirmed all three IDs clean against `include/constants/abilities.h` (Magic Guard=98, Infiltrator=151, Magic Bounce=156); Good As Gold explicitly excluded from this sub-tier per Rob's instruction even though the recon's original text lists it alongside these three. Verified each ability's actual cost independently rather than trusting the recon's "cheap" framing — Magic Bounce needed genuinely new infrastructure, and this tier ended up touching more call sites than its name implied. Magic Guard's exemption list, verified per-site rather than assumed uniform: weather chip, status residual (burn/poison/toxic — toxic counter still ticks even though damage is zeroed), standard recoil moves (alongside Rock Head), Rough Skin/Iron Barbs' damage to the ATTACKER, Life Orb recoil, and Spikes/Stealth Rock switch-in damage — one reusable predicate (`AbilityManager.blocks_indirect_damage`) consulted at each of those six pre-existing call sites (no single shared chokepoint existed, and building one purely for this ability wasn't worth the blast radius). Deliberately NOT blocked, confirmed from source: Struggle's fixed recoil and `[M17n-8]`'s own Aftermath/Innards-Out retaliation against the killer (both gated only by other mechanisms in source, never Magic Guard) — plus Toxic Spikes' poison infliction itself (only the resulting residual damage is gated). Infiltrator bypasses screens (`GetScreensModifier`'s unconditional ×1.0 override) and Substitute (source's single shared `IsSubstituteProtected` chokepoint) for both damaging and status moves — one predicate (`bypasses_infiltrator_barriers`) threaded through all 5 existing substitute-check call sites plus the one screens computation; deliberately scoped narrower than source (no Mist/Safeguard, neither implemented here). Magic Bounce reflects the FIRST foe-targeting status move back at its own user — re-derived this project's exact bounceable subset directly from source's per-move `magicCoatAffected` flag (exactly 9 of 91 implemented moves qualify: Sand Attack, Tail Whip, Leer, Growl, Sleep Powder, Thunder Wave, Toxic, Confuse Ray, Will-O-Wisp; Stealth Rock is also flagged bounceable in source but hazard-setting's separate side-wide dispatch is a documented, deliberate scope gap for this tier). Implemented as a single non-recursive attacker/defender swap in `_phase_move_execution`, which gets "only one bounce ever" for free even in a Magic-Bounce-vs-Magic-Bounce matchup (tested explicitly). Confirmed from source and tested explicitly: Magic Bounce's check sits BEFORE the Dark-type Prankster-immunity gate, so a Prankster'd status move against a Dark-type Magic Bounce holder correctly bounces rather than being eaten as a no-op; `.breakable = TRUE` in source (the one exception among this tier's three abilities) — a Mold-Breaker attacker's status move is NOT reflected. New `m17n9_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 63/63 assertions across 13 sections, stable across 8 reruns. One real test-design bug was caught and fixed on the first run (61/63): the Magic-Bounce-vs-Magic-Bounce scenario originally gave both mons Growl, so each mon's own independent Growl also got reflected by the other's Magic Bounce — two legitimate but unrelated bounce events masquerading as "the same move bouncing twice." Full regression (direct foreground sweep, `pkill -9` first, `scripts/count_assertions.sh` against fresh output, re-run twice from a clean state, plus 5 extra reruns each of `m16c_test.tscn` and `tier4_test.tscn` given how extensively this tier touches screens/Substitute): all 42 prior files pass unchanged, 0 real failures across every run. Total assertions across all 43 `.tscn` files: 2304 prior + 63 = **2367**, confirmed via `count_assertions.sh` and reproducible across both clean sweeps. - M17n-10 (Group 8, "unique/standalone" part 1 — Screen Cleaner / Liquid Ooze / Pressure / Quick Feet / Guard Dog / Forecast): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-06, a recovery session after a prior session crashed mid-implementation. Step 0 re-verified everything from scratch rather than trusting the crashed session's own transcript: Liquid Ooze and Forecast turned out to already be fully and correctly implemented (confirmed independently against source), but none of the 6 abilities' `.tres` files had been regenerated yet — a real gap even in the "already done" abilities. Pressure's new `AbilityManager.pressure_pp_cost` covers the doubles-spread edge case confirmed from source (a spread move vs. two Pressure holders costs 3 PP, not 2) and the TARGET_OPPONENTS_FIELD hazard exclusion; `BattlePokemon.use_pp` gained an `amount` param. Quick Feet closes the M3-era decisions.md S19 known gap (which itself cited the wrong ability_id, 7 instead of 95, corrected in place) — a paralyzed Quick Feet holder's speed is REPLACED (×1.5), never stacked (×1.5×0.5), with the halving. Guard Dog is genuinely TWO independent mechanics: an Intimidate-reversal half (`try_switch_in`'s new `opponent_guard_dog_change` key, reusing Defiant's `BattleScript_DefiantActivates` shape and the same -6-floor no-op gate `[M17b]` established) and a completely separate forced-switch-block half (new `AbilityManager.blocks_forced_switch`, wired into the Roar/Whirlwind block). A genuine mid-session correction, caught only because writing the test for it exposed the scenario was physically impossible to construct: Guard Dog's `.breakable=true` flag does NOT make the Intimidate-reversal half Mold-Breaker-aware — traced `moldBreakerActive`'s own source set-site and confirmed it's never active outside a move-processing window, which a switch-in trigger structurally isn't (same reasoning `[M17f]`/`[M17g]` already established for trapping's attacker-less `is_trapped()`); `.breakable` only actually matters for the forced-switch-block half. New `m17n10_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 59/59 assertions across 11 sections, stable across 8 reruns; caught and fixed two other test-authoring bugs along the way (a `_make_mon` HP-vs-base-stat parameter confusion breaking 3 Pressure PP tests, and an unwitting reliance on paralysis's own uncontrollable 25% full-para RNG making the Quick Feet turn-order test flaky — fixed by testing with poison instead, which triggers the same status-agnostic boost). Full regression: all 43 prior files pass unchanged, 0 failures; `count_assertions.sh` run twice from independently clean states with identical totals; `m16c_test.tscn`/`pp_test.tscn` each rerun 5x given this tier touches both directly. - M17n-11 (Group 8, "unique/standalone" part 2 — Comatose / Costar / Wonder Skin / Mirror Armor): **COMPLETE for these 4 abilities** — 2026-07-06. **Correction to this tier's own task framing, caught during mandatory Step 0 context-gathering before implementation began: M17n-11 is NOT the final Group 8 sub-tier and M17 is NOT fully closed by it** — see `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M17n-11]` entry, "M17 status" subsection, for the full reconciliation; do not treat M17 as done. Comatose's real source mechanic touches ~7 call sites (Sleep Talk/Snore/Rest/Nightmare/Wake-Up-Slap), but a full roster grep confirms NONE of those moves exist in this project — the only implementable piece is full non-volatile-status immunity, confirmed the exact same source case branch as Purifying Salt (`[M17b]`), NOT breakable, `cant_be_suppressed=true`. Costar reuses `[M16e]`'s Psych Up stat-stage-array-copy shape directly, gated on the ally having anything worth copying (a confirmed no-op otherwise, not a reset). Wonder Skin floors a status move's own accuracy stat to 50 (not a flat final-chance override) before the stage-ratio multiplication, confirmed via 2000-trial statistical tests (no deterministic accuracy-roll seam exists in this codebase). Mirror Armor redirects a non-self-inflicted stat decrease onto its source (NOT reversed in sign, unlike Guard Dog's own +1 reversal) at two independent call sites — confirmed self-inflicted drops are never redirected (tested via a synthetic move, since this roster has no Overheat/Draco-Meteor equivalent) — and confirmed architecturally independent from `[M17n-10]`'s Guard Dog via a dedicated doubles test (a single mon can only hold one ability, so the two never compete for the same Intimidate event); like Guard Dog, its Intimidate-specific redirect is NOT Mold-Breaker-aware (switch-in triggers are outside any move-processing window), while its move-based redirect correctly is. New `m17n11_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 51/51 assertions across 11 sections, stable across 8 reruns; two GDScript multi-line-lambda parse errors caught and fixed before the first real run. Full regression: all 44 prior files pass unchanged, 0 failures; `count_assertions.sh` run twice from independently clean states with identical totals; `m17n1_test.tscn`/`m17n10_test.tscn` each rerun 5x. Total assertions across all 45 `.tscn` files: 2426 prior + 51 = **2477**, confirmed via `count_assertions.sh` and reproducible across both clean sweeps. **M17 status, definitively reconciled the same day (see `[M17 Final Reconciliation]` in decisions.md and the new `docs/m17_final_ledger.md`)**: this tier's own guess of a ~12-ability unreconciled gap was itself incomplete — the real picture is **226 implemented + 91 excluded + exactly 1 open (Stench, ability 1) = 318**, verified programmatically with zero overlaps and zero gaps. The 91 exclusions include 24 that were already sitting in this file's own decisions.md (across `[M17n-4]`-`[M17n-9]`'s Step-0 sections) but never cross-referenced here, 3 abilities (Run Away/Pickup/Ball Fetch) confirmed out-of-battle-engine scope back in `[M17n-1]` but never added to any exclusion tally, and 5 (Skill Link, Good As Gold, Illusion, Perish Body, Suction Cups) Rob confirmed excluded directly in the reconciliation session. Stench (1) has no blocker at all — it simply fell out of `docs/m17n_recon.md`'s own Group 1-8 planning prose (that document's Group 4 header claimed 27 abilities while only naming 26; Stench was the uncounted 27th). **`docs/m17_final_ledger.md` is now the single source of truth for every ability's status — consult it before starting any future ability work, and update it in place rather than re-deriving a count from scratch. M17 will be fully closed the moment Stench is either implemented or explicitly excluded — that is the only remaining step, not a new tier or a scope conversation.**

- Item data infrastructure (`gen_items.py` + `ItemData`/`.tres`/`ItemRegistry`, cross-cutting, not tied to a specific M18 sub-tier): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. Closes the gap M18a's own entry flagged. New `scripts/gen_items.py` mirrors `gen_moves.py`/`gen_abilities.py`'s exact structure (dict → `DEFAULTS` → `FIELD_ORDER` → `render()` → `main()`), populated with M18a's 40 items only (re-derived from M18a's actual implementation, cross-checked programmatically against zero mismatches) — every future M18 sub-tier must add its items here, not inline. New `ItemData.item_id` field (mirrors `AbilityData.ability_id`; `MoveData` has no equivalent — the two pre-existing patterns already diverged on this point, noted rather than silently picked). New `ItemRegistry.get_item(id)` mirrors `MoveRegistry`'s path-convention loader exactly. **Key finding: `ItemManager.move_power_modifier_uq412` had no inline per-item data table to migrate** — it's pure generic logic reading whatever `ItemData` a `BattlePokemon` already holds; the 40 items' field values lived only inside `m18a_test.gd`'s inline construction calls. "Migration" was therefore building the missing by-ID lookup capability, not moving existing dispatch code. Verified via a new `item_registry_test.tscn` (204/204 assertions: full data-integrity loop over all 40 `.tres` files, plus a behavioral-parity check proving a registry-loaded `ItemData` and an inline-constructed one produce IDENTICAL `move_power_modifier_uq412` output) — `m18a_test.tscn` itself was re-run UNMODIFIED and still passes 160/160, confirming zero behavior change. Per-item tests (E01/E02) instead call `ItemManager.crit_stage_bonus()` directly for a fully deterministic proof (no RNG involved at all); the one true pipeline-integration claim — item_bonus and Super Luck's ability_bonus SUM rather than one overriding the other — used a statistical crit-rate sample (n=5000, three configurations: ~1/24 neither, ~1/8 either alone, ~1/2 both combined), mirroring `[M17n-5]` Section 12's established pattern. - M18g (Species-gated stat/crit items + Soul Dew — Light Ball, Leek, Thick Club, Lucky Punch, Metal Powder, Quick Powder, Deep Sea Scale, Deep Sea Tooth, Soul Dew, 9 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. **Major correction: the task's cited species-gate precedent doesn't exist.** `[M17n-4]` establishes no species-restriction mechanism at all — Multitype's own held-item read is a Plate-TYPE check, not a species check. Built the species-gate mechanism fresh: two new `ItemData` fields (`required_species`/`required_species2`, plain scalar ints, avoiding Godot typed-array `.tres` risk) plus `ItemManager._species_matches()`. **Five further corrections found and tested independently**: (1) Metal Powder (Defense) and Quick Powder (Speed) are NOT the same stat, despite the "Ditto powder pair" framing — tested with explicit cross-discriminators each way; (2) Deep Sea Scale/Tooth/Metal Powder live in `CalcAttackStat`/`CalcDefenseStat`'s raw-stat-before-formula stage (same as Choice Band/Specs), confirmed distinct from `AbilityManager.defense_damage_modifier_uq412`'s post-effectiveness stage (a similarly-named but different source function, Thick Fat/Marvel Scale's home) — required a genuinely new `DamageCalculator` pipeline stage, since no item-side defense-stat modifier existed before this tier; (3) Lucky Punch/Leek are +2 crit stage, not +1 like Scope Lens/Razor Claw, despite sharing the exact same source function — extended `crit_stage_bonus()` in place; (4) Lucky Punch does NOT extend to Blissey (Chansey's own evolution) — tested explicitly; (5) Soul Dew's mechanism depends on `B_SOUL_DEW_BOOST`, which resolves to Gen7+ under this project's `GEN_LATEST` config — confirmed type-boost ONLY (Psychic/Dragon), no SpDef stat component at all (a completely different, unimplemented mechanism would apply under a pre-Gen7 config). Confirmed but flagged, not silently dropped: Metal Powder/Quick Powder's "untransformed" condition is untestable — this project has no Transform/Imposter mechanic at all. A real bug was caught and fixed during implementation, before any test ran: the first draft wrote the matched-pair second species (Marowak, Latios) into `hold_effect_param` instead of the newly-added `required_species2` field. 90 total `.tres` items now (81 prior + 9). - M18i (Status Orbs — Flame Orb, Toxic Orb, 2 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. **Correction to the task's own framing**: the open question was whether the trigger is "first turn held only" or "every turn until applied" — neither is right. Source (`TryFlameOrb`/`TryToxicOrb`, `battle_hold_effects.c` L600-630) fires at `IsOrbsActivation` timing inside the standard per-turn end-of-turn item dispatch (same neighborhood Leftovers already occupies), checked literally every end of turn with no turn-counter mechanic of any kind — it only ever visibly fires once because the holder then has the status and `StatusManager.try_apply_status`'s existing "already has a status" gate blocks re-application. The "turns held" counter the task asked to look for reusing (Slow Start's timer, `switched_in_this_turn`) isn't needed at all. New `ItemManager.status_orb_status()` has no turn parameter in its signature at all, structurally confirming it can't be turn-gated. Self-infliction reuses `StatusManager.try_apply_status` directly — the same function moves use — with the holder passed as its own attacker, so existing type immunities (Fire-type/burn, Poison-or-Steel-type/toxic) compose for free with zero new immunity logic; tested with three explicit discriminators (Fire, Poison, Steel). Confirmed NOT Unnerve-gated — both are `POCKET_ITEMS` not `POCKET_BERRIES`, and `IsUnnerveBlocked` returns false immediately for any non-berry item. Toxic Orb confirmed to apply `STATUS_TOXIC` (badly poisoned) specifically, not regular `STATUS_POISON`. 99 total `.tres` items now (97 prior + 2). - M18j (Power/accuracy flat-modifier misc — Muscle Band, Wise Glasses, Expert Belt, Wide Lens, Zoom Lens, Bright Powder, Lax Incense, 7 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. **Major correction: the plan's "power items" grouping hid a real pipeline-stage split.** Expert Belt is NOT the same pipeline stage as Muscle Band/Wise Glasses — source places it in `GetAttackerItemsModifier` (the SAME function this project's `post_roll_modifier_uq412`/Life Orb already implements, applied AFTER the roll/type-effectiveness), not `CalcMoveBasePowerAfterModifiers` where Muscle Band/Wise Glasses (and `move_power_modifier_uq412`) live. Extending the wrong function would have produced a wrong pipeline position; tested explicitly that Expert Belt does NOT respond to `move_power_modifier_uq412` at all. **Second correction**: Muscle Band/Wise Glasses use `PercentToUQ4_12_Floored` (no rounding), a DIFFERENT formula than `[M18a]`'s Charcoal-family items (`PercentToUQ4_12`, rounds) — a real 1-unit difference at 10% (4505 floored vs. 4506 rounded), confirmed by reading both source formulas directly. - M18k (Flinch-on-hit items — King's Rock, Razor Fang, 2 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. Both genuinely identical (literal same `HOLD_EFFECT_FLINCH`=30, both param=10) — unlike `[M18g]`/`[M18h]`/`[M18j]`'s apparent pairs, this one really is symmetric, confirmed independently rather than assumed. **Trigger is mutually exclusive with a move's own native flinch, NOT an additive second roll** — source's `TryKingsRock` guards on `!MoveHasAdditionalEffect(move, MOVE_EFFECT_FLINCH)`, gated on the move's static definition (Rock Slide/Sky Attack/Stomp already having flinch), not on whether that native chance actually fired this turn; implemented as `move.secondary_effect != MoveData.SE_FLINCH` at the call site. `MoveIgnoresKingsRock` confirmed unreachable at this project's `GEN_LATEST` config (every condition behind it is gated to pre-Gen-5 comparisons, none unconditional) — not modeled, not a gap.
