- M18n (Forced-switch items — Red Card, Eject Button, 2 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. Preceded by a mandatory first step generalizing an existing testing pitfall: CLAUDE.md gained a new standalone "aggregating across an uncontrolled number of battle turns breaks both absence checks and rate measurements" convention, unifying `[M17l]`'s absence-checking discovery and `[M18k]`'s independent rate-measurement rediscovery under one entry (previously both only existed as status-bullet narrative, no dedicated convention section). Genuinely different mechanics despite the shared "forced-switch items" grouping: Red Card forces the ATTACKER to switch, Eject Button forces the HOLDER itself — both dispatch through a wholly separate source mechanism (`TryRedCard`/`TryEjectButton`, `MoveEndCardButton`) from every other M18 item, confirmed via both items' EMPTY `hold_effects.h` timing-table entries. Both trigger on any direct damaging hit (no category/contact gate, Substitute-absorption excluded for free by this project's existing `went_to_sub` early return). Real asymmetries confirmed from source: Guard Dog blocks Red Card's switch specifically (but the item still consumes) while having ZERO interaction with Eject Button at all (tested as an explicit discriminator — a Guard Dog holder still gets ejected normally); the no-valid-target case is a THIRD distinct outcome (no consumption at all, unlike Guard Dog's block). `CanBattlerSwitch` (both items' gate) confirmed via direct read to be a pure party-composition check, not a trapping check — no Arena Trap/Shadow Tag/Magnet Pull interaction with either item. Magic Guard confirmed to have no interaction with either item (forced switching deals no damage), tested explicitly. **Closes a gap this project's own code had already flagged**: `AbilityManager.blocks_forced_switch`'s doc comment explicitly anticipated "this project has no Red Card item" when written for `[M17n-10]` — reused unmodified here, roles swapped from Roar's own call (comment updated in place). New `m18n_test.tscn`: 22/22 assertions across 2 sections (Red Card incl. the Guard-Dog-still-consumes/no-valid-target-no-consumption/attacker-recoil-death distinctions; Eject Button incl. the Guard-Dog-does-NOT-block and Magic-Guard-non-interaction discriminators). - M18o + M18q (Survive-lethal-hit items — Focus Sash, Focus Band — + Self-heal-on-action items — Big Root, Shell Bell — 4 items, combined session): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. Two genuinely unrelated mechanic families sharing one session for scheduling efficiency; documented, tested, and reported as fully separate `[M18o]`/`[M18q]` entries throughout. **M18o**: Focus Band/Focus Sash extend the exact same shared `else if` chain this project's existing Sturdy already lives in (`[M17n-5]`'s block) — confirmed a strict first-match-wins chain (Sturdy → Focus Band → Focus Sash), so a Pokemon with BOTH Sturdy and a held Focus Sash never reaches the Focus Sash branch when Sturdy fires: not consumed, not "wasted," simply untouched (tested explicitly). Focus Band is probabilistic (10%, no HP gate, NOT consumed — repeatable every hit); Focus Sash is full-HP-gated (same gate as Sturdy) with no roll at all, and SINGLE-USE — corroborated by a direct changelog citation (`docs/changelogs/1.8.x/1.8.4.md`'s "Focus Sash but not consuming the item" bugfix entry) since no C-level function directly differentiates the two items' consumption. Confirmed no analogous current_hp-vs-.fainted timing bug (both checks read the target's own pre-hit HP, not a post-hit aliveness check on a different Pokemon). New generic `item_effect_triggered` signal (Focus Band's survive isn't consumption or an ability, so neither `item_consumed` nor `ability_triggered` fit). Flagged (not fixed) a pre-existing gap surfaced while wiring Focus Sash's consumption: `_consume_item`'s "every item is a berry" comment was already false before this tier (`[M18k]`/`[M18n]`'s non-berry items already call it), so Cheek Pouch incorrectly heals on ANY item consumption, not just berries — predates this session, not fixed. **M18q**: Big Root's real scope is move-drain only (not "all drain sources" — the other half, Ingrain/Leech Seed/Strength Sap/Aqua Ring, doesn't exist in this project); its formula is source-confirmed to deliberately NOT be UQ4.12 (`(hp*1300)/1000`, plain integer math), and is applied BEFORE the existing Liquid Ooze branch, so a Liquid-Ooze-inverted hit against a Big Root holder is ALSO boosted — tested explicitly. Shell Bell reads the FINAL damage (source's `savedDmg`, set immediately after damage applies — this project's own `damage` local, already final by construction), tested with a stacked crit+type-effectiveness scenario comparing against the OBSERVED (not hand-derived) damage; gated on not-already-at-max-HP (genuinely new, no prior precedent). Two real cross-tier interactions found and flagged not built (same class as `[M18n]`'s own flagged doubles gap): Shell Bell should skip healing if Red Card just forced the attacker to switch this same resolution (not modeled), and source's spread-move damage accumulation (heal once per move, not once per target) isn't reproduced by this project's per-target dispatch. 114 total `.tres` items now (110 prior + 4 across both tiers). **Two real test-authoring bugs caught and fixed**, both instances of documented CLAUDE.md pitfalls recurring in the same session that documented them: (1) M18o's O01.04/O02.05 initially read HP straight off the `item_effect_triggered` signal's own argument, assuming the HP write had already happened — it hadn't (the elif chain only caps a local variable before emitting; the real write happens several lines later, right before `move_executed`) — fixed by snapshotting from `move_executed` instead; (2) M18q's Q02.08 discriminator initially ran a multi-turn battle where a later legitimate Shell Bell trigger (once the attacker took counter-damage) got misread as contradicting the max-HP gate — the exact whole-battle-aggregation pitfall (`[M17l]`/`[M18k]`) — fixed by guaranteeing a one-hit-kill battle, which itself needed two attempts since this project's HP formula's `+level+10` floor keeps `max_hp` from going below ~60 regardless of how low `base_hp` is set alone (had to also lower `base_def`). - M18m (Stat-change-reactive consumed items — Weakness Policy, White Herb, Eject Pack, Mirror Herb, 4 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. Despite the tier's own "stat-change-reactive" grouping, the 4 items are genuinely NOT one shared trigger shape — corrections found on 3 of the 4. White Herb and Eject Pack are NOT the same "any stat lowered" condition: White Herb unconditionally scans all stat stages for any negative value at every MoveEnd (not gated on a decrease "just happening"), while Eject Pack genuinely needs a "decrease just applied this resolution" signal — reproduced via a new `BattlePokemon.eject_pack_snapshot` field compared at BattleManager's own MoveEnd-equivalent checkpoint (`_phase_faint_check`, which already runs once per resolved move regardless of outcome — the closest match to source's `MoveEndItemOnStatChange` granularity). Eject Pack's decrease can come from ANY source (self-inflicted included, not opponent-only), tested explicitly. Mirror Herb confirmed a genuine structural twin of Opportunist (`[M17n-8]`) AT THE SOURCE LEVEL — both checked in the literal same source loop — so Opportunist's own documented "primary move-driven increases only" scope limit is a shared source-level fact, correctly inherited rather than a new simplification; wired directly alongside Opportunist's own block, immediate copy-and-consume (source's queue-and-batch-until-MoveEnd behavior judged unneeded given this project's one-stat-per-move architecture and the item's single-use nature). Weakness Policy wired alongside Enigma Berry (`[M18c]`) at the same on-hit dispatch site, and confirmed consumed UNCONDITIONALLY once triggered — a real, tested difference from `[M18r]`'s Blunder Policy, which only consumes if the stat genuinely changed. White Herb tested via a DIRECT `_phase_faint_check()` call on a minimally-configured bare BattleManager — the first time this project has called a phase-dispatch function directly rather than through the normal `advance()` driver loop, confirmed safe since `_set_phase` is a plain setter with no cascading dispatch. 4 new `.tres` items (131 total, 127 prior + 4). New `m18m_test.tscn`: 27/27 across 4 sections, every assertion scoped to a single well-defined event from the start — this exact whole-battle-aggregation pitfall had recurred in four consecutive prior tiers, and this one held the line. Two real (non-aggregation) test-authoring bugs caught and fixed: a fixture helper that silently ignored the requested move type (so a "super-effective" test hit was actually neutral), and a test listening for a signal (`pokemon_switched_out`) that `_do_forced_switch_in` never actually emits (only the caller-emitted `forced_switch` does, matching `[M18n]`'s own pattern) — both confirmed via debug tracing to be test bugs, not implementation bugs. - M18p (Contact-reactive damage family — Rocky Helmet, Sticky Barb, Protective Pads, Punching Glove, 4 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. The plan flagged reading `[M18d]`'s contact-vs-category lesson first, but the real finding here was a DIFFERENT shape: source's contact-detection is genuinely TWO functions, not one — `IsMoveMakingContact` (the narrow, universal primitive Tough Claws/Poison Touch call directly) and `CanBattlerAvoidContactEffects` (a wrapper ONE LEVEL UP, adding a Protective Pads check, called ONLY by genuine contact-retaliation consumers — Rough Skin/Static/Mummy/Pickpocket/Aftermath/etc., confirmed by reading all ~11 call sites). Punching Glove's contact-strip lives INSIDE `IsMoveMakingContact` itself (same level as Long Reach, so it's universal — even suppresses Tough Claws' own boost, tested explicitly); Protective Pads' gate lives ONLY in the wrapper (narrow, retaliation-only — confirmed to NOT touch Tough Claws). Folding Protective Pads into the shared `move_makes_contact()` would have incorrectly broken Tough Claws — so this project's new `AbilityManager.move_triggers_contact_retaliation` sits ALONGSIDE `move_makes_contact` rather than replacing it, swapped in only at `try_contact_effects`'s top gate and `faint_retaliation_damage`'s Aftermath branch. Rocky Helmet: contact-gated ONLY (the mirror image of `[M18d]`'s Jaboca/Rowap, which are category-gated only) — maxHP/6 to the attacker, gated on the attacker's own Magic Guard, not consumed. Sticky Barb: genuinely TWO unrelated mechanisms sharing one item — a contact-gated item-transfer to the attacker (that explicitly bypasses Sticky Hold, a real source-confirmed exception requiring a new `bypass_sticky_hold` param on the shared `_try_steal_item` primitive Pickpocket/Magician also use) plus an unconditional end-of-turn maxHP/8 self-damage gated by the HOLDER's own Magic Guard, wholly unrelated to contact. 4 new `.tres` items (135 total, 131 prior + 4). New `m18p_test.tscn`: 33/33 across 4 sections, passing on the first run — no aggregation-pattern bugs, no test-authoring bugs. Regression: `item_registry_test.tscn` 204/204, `m18d_test.tscn` 19/19, `ability_test.tscn` 64/64 (the general contact-mechanism consumer suite), `m17j_test.tscn` 48/48 + `m17h_test.tscn` 64/64 (extra coverage for the `_try_steal_item`/`try_contact_effects` signature changes), `m17n8_test.tscn` 58/58 (Aftermath, extra coverage for its gate swap) — all unchanged. Recommend **M18t, M18v, or M18x** (all remaining, none blocked), or the end-of-M18 legacy-item cleanup pass, per Rob's preference.
- M18t (Iron Ball + Air Balloon, 2 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. Confirmed NOT mechanical opposites on one shared toggle — each is wired as an independent, separately-gated branch on the same shared functions, and Iron Ball carries a wholly unrelated second effect (Speed) Air Balloon has no counterpart for. The real finding: source's actual grounding logic (`IsBattlerGroundedInverseCheck`, battle_util.c L5879-5894) is ONE unified, priority-ordered check — Iron Ball (forced-grounded, checked first, beats even Levitate/Flying-type) > Gravity/Ingrain/Smack Down (confirmed absent from this project) > Telekinesis/Magnet Rise (absent)/Air Balloon/Levitate (ungrounded) > Flying-type (ungrounded) > grounded by default — and this project's pre-existing `AbilityManager.is_grounded` (`[M16d]`) already had Air Balloon/Iron Ball flagged as a known, anticipated gap in its own doc comment, written well before this tier existed. Chose to extend rather than restructure: `is_grounded()` gained both items with zero signature changes (a free correctness win for hazard immunity and Arena Trap too, confirmed via regression), while the SEPARATE damage-calc pipeline (`AbilityManager.blocks_move_type`, Mold-Breaker-aware, + `TypeChart.get_effectiveness`'s raw table) got a parallel extension — a new `grounded_override` param on `get_effectiveness` mirroring the existing `bypass_ghost_immunity`/Scrappy precedent exactly — rather than risking `is_grounded()`'s two existing callers by adding Mold-Breaker-awareness it was explicitly documented as never needing. Real correction found: Air Balloon's consumption trigger is NOT "blocked a Ground move" — source's own `IsBattlerTurnDamaged(battler, INCLUDING_SUBSTITUTES)` means it pops from ANY damaging hit landing, Ground-type or not, even one absorbed by Substitute; a blocked Ground hit deals 0 damage so it correctly never pops from the hit it just deflected. This `INCLUDING_SUBSTITUTES` semantic placed the new consumption check before `went_to_sub`'s early return, the same spot Rapid Spin already established for the identical reason. 2 new `.tres` items (137 total, 135 prior + 2). New `m18t_test.tscn`: 22/22 across 2 sections. Two test-authoring bugs caught and fixed on the first run (both confirmed not to be implementation bugs): a baseline assertion wrongly assumed `blocks_move_type` was Flying-type-aware (it never has been — that immunity lives purely in `TypeChart`'s raw table); a full-battle check wrongly assumed a `move_missed("immune")` signal fires for ordinary type-immune damaging moves (it doesn't — that signal is scoped to the OHKO branch and the status-move `foe_targeting` check only). Regression went beyond routine scope given how central the touched functions are: `item_registry_test.tscn` 204/204, `damage_test.tscn` 24/24 (including the unrelated Electric-vs-Ground immunity fact, confirmed untouched), `m17n1_test.tscn` 82/82 (M17.5 batch fix), `m17n6_test.tscn` 101/101 (Wonder Guard/type-mutation, `bypass_ghost_immunity`'s own suite), `m17f_test.tscn` 30/30 (Arena Trap), `m16d_test.tscn` 71/71 (hazards, `is_grounded`'s origin suite) — all unchanged. Recommend **M18v or M18x** (both remaining, none blocked), or the end-of-M18 legacy-item cleanup pass, per Rob's preference.

Re-verified the tier table's own "Disable/Encore only" narrowing against source directly rather than trusting it — found a real gap in the plan's prose (it omitted Infatuation from Mental Herb's cure list, even though `TryMentalHerb`, battle_hold_effects.c L416-476, checks Infatuation unconditionally at the top of the function, ahead of the five Gen-5+-gated conditions Torment/Disable/Heal Block/Encore/Taunt). Confirmed source's real scope is SIX conditions, not five; of those six, this project implements only Disable and Encore, so the narrowing holds up on a fuller citation rather than a rubber-stamp. Trigger timing confirmed the SAME unconditional per-checkpoint scan shape as White Herb (`[M18m]`) — `TryMentalHerb` never branches on which of its two dispatch timings triggered it — so this tier reused the identical `_phase_faint_check()` insertion point rather than building new infrastructure. - M18x (Covert Cloak, 1 item): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-07. LAST M18 implementation tier — **M18 is now functionally complete**, pending only the end-of-M18 legacy-item cleanup pass. Flagged "wide-but-shallow," but confirmed genuinely a single insertion point: real source's `IsMoveEffectBlockedByTarget` (battle_util.c L9811-9825) is the literal same function for Shield Dust (ability) and Covert Cloak (item) — an if/else-if chain — and this project's Shield Dust already lives in exactly one place, `StatusManager.try_secondary_effect`, gated on `is_true_secondary` (`secondary_chance > 0`). Confirmed that gate correctly reproduces source's own `!primary` exemption (a move's guaranteed/primary effect, like Thunder Wave's paralysis, is never blocked): all 5 of this project's `secondary_chance=0` moves (Sleep Powder, Thunder Wave, Toxic, Confuse Ray, Will-O-Wisp) are genuine status moves, and `stat_change_stat` (Growl/Swords Dance) has no probability field in this project's schema at all — that whole category is architecturally unreachable by Covert Cloak's gate, not merely untested. Two genuine pre-existing gaps discovered as side effects of tracing this code carefully, both flagged and explicitly NOT fixed (out of scope for a 1-item tier): (1) real source also gates Poison Touch/Toxic Chain through this same check, but this project's Shield Dust has no such gate for Poison Touch (Toxic Chain is excluded entirely) — a real gap from `[M17c]`, predating this tier; Covert Cloak deliberately matches Shield Dust's CURRENT scope rather than introducing a new asymmetry. (2) `try_contact_effects` merges Poison Point and Poison Touch into one branch keyed on the DEFENDER's ability but applies the poison to the ATTACKER in both cases — correct for Poison Point, backwards for Poison Touch (which real source keys on the ATTACKER's ability, poisoning the DEFENDER) — a separate, unrelated ability-direction bug, also from `[M17c]`. Sheer Force confirmed unrelated/non-conflicting (a separate sequential check keyed on the attacker's ability). Consumption confirmed permanent, never consumed — tested explicitly surviving three separate blocks in a row. New `m18x_test.tscn`: 15/15 across 8 sections, passing on the first run, stable across 2 reruns — every status/confusion/flinch assertion via direct `try_secondary_effect`/`try_contact_effects` calls with a forced roll, avoiding whole-battle-aggregation by construction (the clean streak now runs `[M18m]`/`[M18p]`/`[M18t]`/`[M18v]`/`[M18x]`, five tiers). 1 new `.tres` item (139 total, 138 prior + 1). Regression: `item_registry_test.tscn` 204/204, `m17n1_test.tscn` 82/82 (Shield Dust's own origin suite), `m17n5_test.tscn` 78/78 (Sheer Force's own origin suite), `stat_test.tscn` 78/78 — all unchanged.

**M18 status: fully complete in every sense — implementation, testing, and pipeline migration.** See the "Post-M18 Review" section below for every flagged-but-unfixed item found across the whole M18 effort; all six are now resolved (four via `[M18.5a]`, the remaining two via `[M21]`).

- M18.5a (Post-M18 technical debt — Poison Touch fixes + 2 test-authoring bugs, 4 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. Closed Post-M18 Review items 1, 2, 5, and 6. **Items 1+2 (Poison Touch)**: confirmed via direct source read (`ABILITYEFFECT_MOVE_END_ATTACKER`, battle_util.c L4281-4299 — an explicitly-commented "same as above, but for attacker" SEPARATE dispatch pass) that Poison Touch is ATTACKER-keyed and poisons the DEFENDER, unlike every other ability in `try_contact_effects` (all defender-keyed reactions to being hit, Poison Point included, confirmed still correct via its own `CanBePoisoned` argument order). Fixed by checking Poison Touch independently before `id` is even computed (so a defender with no ability doesn't block it), gated by the same Shield Dust/Covert Cloak check `[M18x]` already established — checked against the DEFENDER (the poison recipient), the same battler role `StatusManager.try_secondary_effect`'s existing gate uses. Flagged, not fixed: a rare double-ability-holder edge case (attacker holds Poison Touch AND defender independently holds Poison Point) where only one of the two fires, since this function's single-effect-per-call return shape has no way to report both. **Items 5+6 (found during `[M18-cleanup]`'s regression sweep)**: both confirmed TEST bugs via direct debug tracing, zero production code touched for either. Item 5 (`m17n7_test.gd` S8.07/S11.01, Harvest/Cud Chew): the file's own `_make_item` helper predates `[M18-patch-1]`'s `pocket` field and never set it, so every berry it constructs fails `_consume_item`'s `item.pocket == POCKET_BERRIES` gate — `last_consumed_berry` silently never gets set even though the berry's own heal effect fires correctly, starving both abilities of anything to regenerate/re-fire. Fixed by adding a `pocket` param to the helper and passing `POCKET_BERRIES` at all 11 genuine-berry call sites. Item 6 (`m18q_test.gd` Q02.09, Shell Bell): NOT the M17n-2-shaped "missing forced crit" hypothesis in the literal sense assumed, but adjacent — direct debug tracing showed the fixture's non-crit forced-max-roll hit (56 dmg) couldn't one-shot its target (61 max HP, per `[M18r]`'s own `+level+10` floor finding), so the target survived to counter-attack and legitimately dent the holder below max HP before a later, correctly-firing heal was misread as a bug — a fresh recurrence of the whole-battle-aggregation pitfall. Fixed by adding `_force_crit = true` (1.5× pushes 56→84, exceeding 61), mirroring the same file's own already-established forced-roll-plus-forced-crit sibling test. New discriminators added to `m17c_test.gd` (Poison Point/Touch's own origin suite — S5.03 corrected direction, S5.03b/c/d/e new): 85/85 (was 79). Regression: `m18x_test.tscn` 15/15, `m17n1_test.tscn` 82/82, `item_registry_test.tscn` 309/309, `m17n7_test.tscn` 62/62, `m18q_test.tscn` 16/16 — all unchanged/fixed as expected, stable across 3-4 reruns each. Post-M18 Review's remaining items 3+4 (Shell Bell doubles gaps) stay correctly deferred to M22. Recommend **M18.5d (Gender), M18.5f (Binding-move), M18.5g (Multi-hit), or M18.5h (Nature/IV/EV)** — all four remaining Phase 1 tracks are independent and dependency-free at this point, per Rob's preference.

- M18.5d Phase 1 (Gender infrastructure): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. The one genuine hard dependency in M18.5's Phase 1 — Attract (M18.5e) was blocked on this. Two real Step-0 findings reshaped scope: (1) most of the "extraction pipeline" work was already done — `data/pokemon.json` already carries an accurate `gender_ratio` field for all 386 species (spot-checked against source for 5 categories: Bulbasaur 31/skewed-starter, Rattata 127/50-50, Chansey 254/always-female, Ditto 255/genderless, Tyrogue 0/always-male — all exact), and `PokemonSpecies.gender_ratio` already exists in the schema with a correct doc comment — both dormant since `[M15]`, the same "unpopulated schema field" shape `ItemData.pocket` had before `[M18-patch-1]`. The Python extractor itself (`tools/convert_pokedata.py`, per `[M15]`'s own decisions.md entry) doesn't exist anywhere in this repo — unlike `gen_items.py`/`gen_moves.py`/`gen_abilities.py`, it was never kept as a rerunnable generator — so there was nothing to "extend"; also confirmed `data/pokemon/` (the would-be per-species `.tres` directory) is empty and no JSON-to-`PokemonSpecies`-Resource converter exists anywhere in production code — species data lives only as bulk JSON + `PokemonRegistry`'s dictionary API, a pre-existing architectural gap flagged, not built. (2) the task's own "mirrors how IVs are already handled" assumption was WRONG — `from_species` hardcodes `ivs = [0,0,0,0,0,0]` unconditionally (a deliberate M1-era placeholder per the field's own doc comment) and contains zero `randi()` calls anywhere, so there was no existing "roll once at creation" pattern to mirror; designed fresh instead. New `BattlePokemon.gender: int` (clean `GENDER_MALE/FEMALE/GENDERLESS` enum, matching this project's own `STATUS_*`/`STAGE_*` style rather than reusing source's raw 0/254/255 sentinel bytes), rolled once in `from_species` via new `_roll_gender()`, porting `GetGenderFromSpeciesAndPersonality` (pokemon.c L1847-1861) exactly — the three sentinels short-circuit with no roll, everything else is `gender_ratio > randi() % 256`. No forcing seam added — `gender` is freely reassignable post-construction like every other field, matching this project's ~70 existing `_make_mon`-style fixture helpers; a future Attract test should just set it directly. Confirmed zero existing ability/item logic reads gender anywhere (grep, zero hits outside the schema declaration) — a genuine greenfield addition, nothing needed immediate gender-awareness. New `m18_5d_test.tscn`: 11/11 (5 data-integrity + 6 instance-generation, including n=2000 statistical-rate checks for a skewed and a 50/50 species matching `[M17n-5]`/`[M18e]`'s tolerance-band convention), stable across 5 reruns. Regression: smoke test unchanged (386 species), `battle_test`/`damage_test` 24/24/`status_test` 78/78/`move_test` 49/49/`stat_test` 78/78 (all `from_species` consumers with fixed IV/EV) — all unchanged, confirming the new `randi()` call doesn't disturb existing determinism. **M18.5e (Attract) is now unblocked.** Recommend **M18.5e (Attract, now unblocked)**, or **M18.5f (Binding-move)/M18.5g (Multi-hit)/M18.5h (Nature/IV/EV)** (still independent, no dependency change), per Rob's preference.

- M18.5d Phase 2 (Gender-dependent mechanics — Attract, Rivalry, Cute Charm, Oblivious, 4 items): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. Closes out the gender-dependent mechanics track entirely (Destiny Knot stays separately deferred to M18.5i, pending M28/breeding readiness). Built in dependency order within the combined session: Attract's own infliction logic first, since Cute Charm and Oblivious both react to it directly. **Attract**: corrected a pre-existing `[M17n-1]`-era mis-citation in `move_data.gd` (it cited `BS_TrySetInfatuation`, actually a side-wide Z-move-only effect this project has no reason to implement, not Attract's real command) — Attract's real script (`BattleScript_EffectAttract`) calls a side-wide Aroma Veil check then `Cmd_tryinfatuating` (which ALSO re-checks Aroma Veil plus Oblivious plus gender/already-infatuated). 50% chance to be unable to move each turn while infatuated (`CancelerInfatuation`, the LAST canceler in source's own order, wired into `pre_move_check` accordingly), cured by the infatuated mon's own switch-out via the existing `_clear_volatiles` mechanism every other volatile already uses. Taunt immunity re-confirmed still moot (Taunt remains unimplemented). - M18.5d-3 (Infatuation source tracking): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. Closes the one gap `[M18.5d Phase 2]` deliberately flagged: infatuation previously only cured on the INFATUATED mon's own switch-out, missing real source's reciprocal condition — the infatuated mon is ALSO cured the instant the Pokémon who attracted it leaves the field (switch-out or faint), even if the infatuated mon itself never switched. Confirmed via source (`INFATUATED_WITH(battler) = battler + 1`, a raw slot-index encoding driven by C's bitfield constraints) that this project didn't need to reproduce that raw-index shape — `BattlePokemon.infatuated: bool` replaced with `infatuated_by: BattlePokemon = null` (a direct object reference), matching this project's own existing `_last_attacker` dictionary precedent for "who did this to me" tracking rather than inventing a new pattern. Confirmed source's two separate trigger functions (`SwitchInClearSetData`/`FaintClearSetData`, both battle_main.c) collapse cleanly into this project's ONE existing `_clear_volatiles(mon)` chokepoint (already called at all 4 real "a battler left the field" moments — regular faint, Destiny-Bond-triggered faint, Aftermath/Innards-Out-triggered faint, and switch-out) — added a single reciprocal scan there (loop `_combatants`, clear anyone else's `infatuated_by` if it points at the mon that just left), rather than two separate insertion points. Doubles confirmed a non-factor requiring no new infrastructure (the scan works generically) but also not specifically tested, consistent with the project's "don't build unreachable doubles coverage prematurely" precedent (Shell Bell). Extended `m18_5d2_test.gd`'s existing Attract section (no new file) — 3 new assertions: source-battler-leaves cures the victim (the fix itself), an unrelated third battler leaving does NOT cure it (discriminator), and fainting the source also cures it (confirms both real trigger conditions). The holder's own switch-out cure was explicitly reconfirmed as a regression check, not assumed. **49/49** (was 46/46), stable across 5 reruns. Regression: `item_registry_test.tscn` 309/309, `status_test.tscn` 78/78 — both unchanged. Recommend **M18.5f (Binding-move), M18.5g (Multi-hit), or M18.5h (Nature/IV/EV)** — all three remain independent and dependency-free, unaffected by this fix.
- M18.5f (Binding-move mechanic): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. 10 moves, not the 11 `docs/m19_recon.md` claimed — Bind/Wrap/Fire Spin/Clamp/Whirlpool/Sand Tomb/Magma Storm/Infestation/Snap Trap/Thunder Cage all share the identical real-source `MOVE_EFFECT_WRAP` mechanic; **Jaw Lock is excluded**, a direct source read shows it dispatches `MOVE_EFFECT_TRAP_BOTH` instead — a completely different, zero-damage, permanent, bidirectional trap (the Mean Look/Block family's `escapePrevention`), conflated by the recon on flavor-text similarity alone. Confirmed binding does NOT restrict move selection (absent from every pre-move canceler in source) — only blocks voluntary switching and deals maxHP/8 recurring end-of-turn damage for a random 4-5 turns. Reused the EXISTING generic `secondary_effect`/`secondary_chance` fields (`SE_WRAP`) rather than a bespoke move flag — cheaper than Attract's own dedicated dispatch, since binding is a damage move with an attached generic effect, not a status move. New `BattlePokemon.wrapped_by`/`wrapped_turns`; `AbilityManager.is_trapped()` extended with a `wrapped_by` check right after its existing Ghost-type gate (a Ghost-type still takes the recurring damage, only the switch-block exemption applies); `BattleManager._clear_volatiles` extended with the exact same `[M18.5d-3]`-pattern reciprocal cross-battler scan — the source battler leaving the field also cures the victim's trap, confirmed via the identical two source functions `[M18.5d-3]` already unified. Confirmed a genuine off-by-one in the duration counter (checked BEFORE decrementing in source, so an N-turn trap deals N damage ticks then one silent free "ends" tick) and reproduced it exactly rather than assuming the simpler decrement-then-clear shape `disable_turns`/`encore_turns` already use. Found and avoided a real correctness pitfall: SE_WRAP was given its own dispatch branch (same shape as SE_FLINCH's existing carve-out) rather than falling into the shared status/confusion-cure-berry branch, which would have spuriously evaluated an unrelated pre-existing status against a held cure berry. New `m18_5f_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 137/137, stable across 6 reruns (one intermittent accuracy-roll flake caught and fixed via `bm._force_hit = true`, not preemptively guessed). Regression: `item_registry_test.tscn` 309/309, `status_test.tscn` 78/78, `m17n9_test.tscn` (Magic Guard's own origin suite) 63/63, plus `m17f_test.tscn` 30/30 and `m18_5d2_test.tscn` 49/49 (both directly-extended functions' own origin suites, beyond the named regression scope). **Grip Claw is now unblocked** (7-turn duration extension) but still deferred to M18.5i's reconsideration pass, same for Binding Band (maxHP/6 variant) — neither item is built here. Recommend **M18.5g (Multi-hit) or M18.5h (Nature/IV/EV)** — both remain independent and dependency-free.
- M18.5g (Multi-hit move mechanism): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. 30 moves — confirmed via direct source grep, matching `docs/m19_recon.md`'s count of 31 exactly this time; **Population Bomb is excluded** — the one `.strikeCount` move with per-hit accuracy checks AND a uniquely-shaped Loaded Dice range, a genuinely higher complexity class than the other 30, flagged for a future tier. Roll distribution confirmed exact: **35%/35%/15%/15%** (2/3/4/5 hits) for this project's default Gen5+ config — a real correction to the commonly-cited 37.5/37.5/12.5/12.5 figure, which is actually the older pre-Gen5 branch of the same source function. Triple Kick/Triple Axel (`is_triple_kick`) each independently roll accuracy per hit (unlike every other move in the family, which checks once) and escalate power ×1/×2/×3; Scale Shot (`is_scale_shot`) applies a one-time self stat change once after the whole sequence, not per hit. Refactored `BattleManager._do_damaging_hit` from `void` to `int` (returns real damage dealt) plus a new `suppress_shell_bell` param, since **Shell Bell must heal ONCE from the damage ACCUMULATED across the whole sequence, not per hit** — confirmed via source's `savedDmg +=` accumulation; a per-hit heal would under-heal due to floor-division truncation. Every other per-hit mechanism (contact abilities, King's Rock, the survive-lethal-hit chain, hit-reactive abilities, Twineedle's own per-hit poison chance) fires correctly for free simply by calling `_do_damaging_hit` once per loop iteration, confirmed individually rather than assumed uniform. Mid-sequence termination verified as three genuinely different shapes: target fainting stops immediately; a Substitute absorbs MULTIPLE hits before breaking (continues, unlike fainting) and only stops the sequence the instant it actually breaks; a wholly-immune/ability-absorbed hit stops after just one attempt. Found and fixed two small, genuinely in-scope pre-existing gaps: `SE_POISON` didn't exist at all (only `SE_TOXIC`), needed for Twineedle's real (non-toxic) poison chance — also corrected a mislabeled `_status_to_se` mapping this surfaced (Poison Point/Poison Touch's `secondary_applied` signal was silently reporting regular poison as Toxic); `strike_count`/`multi_hit`/`always_critical_hit` were never wired into `gen_moves.py`'s own `DEFAULTS`/`FIELD_ORDER` at all, meaning no hand-authored move entry could have ever actually emitted them to a `.tres` file before this fix. Skill Link/Loaded Dice are now unblocked but not implemented — mechanism-only scope, matching Grip Claw's own precedent from `[M18.5f]`. New `m18_5g_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 315/315, stable across 6 reruns, sectioned by mechanism concern per the task's own instruction (only Triple Kick/Axel get a dedicated section). Regression treated as a wide sweep (matching `[M18t]`'s own scoping, not a routine 2-3-suite check, given how many existing mechanisms the `_do_damaging_hit` refactor touches): 18 suites, all clean — `item_registry_test` 309/309, `damage_test` 24/24, `move_test` 49/49, `stat_test` 78/78, `tier3_test` 62/62, `tier4_test` 86/86, `m17c_test` 85/85, `m17j_test` 48/48, `m17n5_test` 78/78, `m17n8_test` 58/58, `m17n9_test` 63/63, `m18k_test` 16/16, `m18q_test` 16/16, `m18d_test` 19/19, `m18p_test` 33/33, `m18o_test` 19/19, `m18_5f_test` 137/137, `m18_5d2_test` 49/49. Recommend **M18.5h (Nature/IV/EV)** as the next tier — the last of the three independent M18.5 Phase 1 tracks, now that binding and multi-hit are both complete.
- M18.5h-1 (Nature system): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. First of two sequential M18.5h sub-tiers (`[M18.5h-2]`, IV, next). 25 natures re-verified directly from source (`include/constants/pokemon.h` L52-76, no corrections needed this time), 5 neutral (Hardy/Docile/Serious/Bashful/Quirky). Applies as `floor(stat*110/100)`/`floor(stat*90/100)` wrapping `_stat_formula`'s existing return value, HP double-insulated and confirmed unaffected. `NATURE_*` constants + `nature: int` live on `BattlePokemon` only (source's `GetNature` is pure `personality % 25`, zero per-species bias — no `PokemonSpecies` change needed). **New `forced_nature: Variant = null` parameter on `from_species`**, reusing this project's existing forcing-parameter convention (`force_hit`/`force_confusion_hit`) rather than a new pattern — **ready for M24 (Trainer Data) to assign specific deterministic natures**, built now rather than retrofitted later per Rob's explicit requirement. Flagged and avoided a real correctness trap: source's `enum Stat` orders Speed before SpAtk/SpDef, this project orders it after — the nature-to-stat table was built by stat NAME, never a raw source index. New `m18_5h1_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 46/46, stable across 6 reruns, including an explicit `forced_nature=NATURE_HARDY(0)` determinism test pinning the "0 vs null" footgun. **Regression was this session's headline finding**: turning on a real default random-nature roll broke ~25 suites' worth of pre-existing exact-value stat/damage assertions that all implicitly assumed no Nature system existed — found only via the full 75-suite sweep this task required (not a routine check), taking 5 iterations to fully converge since 3 suites (`damage_test`/`move_test`/`status_test`) used a `"X passed, Y failed"` summary format invisible to a literal `"FAILED"` grep across 4 sweeps. Every fix was a test-fixture change only (pin `NATURE_HARDY` on each suite's own fixture helper, or copy the source mon's `.nature` forward for 4 clone-style helpers) — zero production code changed beyond `battle_pokemon.gd` itself. Likes/dislikes and EV gain remain explicitly excluded/deferred per Rob's own scope decisions on `docs/m18_5h_recon.md`. Recommend **M18.5h-2 (IV)** next — it will need the identical `forced_iv`-style override pattern established here.
- M18.5h-2 (IV system): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-08. Second of two M18.5h sub-tiers — **M18.5h is now fully complete** (EV gain remains deferred to M20; likes/dislikes remain excluded, both per Rob's own scope decisions on the recon). Corrected a factual error in the task's own framing: its cited "`[M18.5h-1]` UQ_4_12 truncation-rounding lesson" does not exist in that entry — Nature used plain `floori()` truncation, not UQ_4_12 fixed-point math. Re-verified the combined stat formula directly against `pokemon.c` L1406-1425 and found it **already 100% correct** in `_stat_formula`/`_hp_formula` since Milestone 1 — **zero formula changes needed anywhere**; this tier's entire surface is `from_species` + one new `_roll_ivs()` function. 6 INDEPENDENT `randi() % 32` rolls (source's real IVs come from a separate random "IV word," not personality — same reproduce-the-distribution-not-the-bit-packing precedent as gender/nature). **New `forced_ivs: Variant = null` parameter on `from_species`**, resolving an explicit design question beyond simple all-or-nothing forcing: accepts either a fully-concrete `Array[int]` (all 6 forced) OR a per-stat-nullable `Array` (SOME stats forced, others still roll normally) — directly matching M24's real future need for competitively-built trainer Pokémon with some stats maxed and the rest left alone. New `m18_5h2_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 27/27, stable across 6 reruns, including a statistical independence discriminator (`P(ivs[0]==ivs[1])` near the true 1/32 rate, guarding specifically against a "one shared roll for all 6 stats" bug) and both full-array and partial-forcing determinism tests. **Regression converged in 2 sweep iterations, versus `[M18.5h-1]`'s own 5** — credited directly to two lessons applied from that tier: proactively pinning `forced_ivs` on all 26 already-known-sensitive files BEFORE running any sweep, and using the broad `passed|fail` grep from sweep 1 onward instead of retrofitting it partway through. Sweep 1 still found 7 more files (`damage_test.gd`, missed from the proactive batch, plus 6 suites — including `integration_test.gd` — that `[M18.5h-1]`'s own regression never touched at all, since IV has NO neutral no-op case the way Nature's 5/25 chance provided, so nothing was ever "lucky" under IV). Sweep 2: 100% clean across all 76 suites. 31 test files touched total this session (listed in full in the `[M18.5h-2]` decisions.md entry) plus `battle_pokemon.gd`. `forced_nature` and `forced_ivs` (including partial per-stat forcing) are both now ready for M24 (Trainer Data) to consume whenever that milestone starts. Recommend **M18.5i** (the Grip Claw/Binding Band/Destiny Knot reconsideration pass, per its own already-established deferral point in `[M18.5f]`'s and `[M18.5d Phase 2]`'s entries) as a natural next tier, though Rob's own preference governs sequencing from here.

- M20 Recon (scoping only, not a milestone): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14. `docs/m20_recon.md` covers Experience & Leveling scoping, per the roadmap's own M20 label. Confirmed real existing infrastructure beyond the usual fresh-milestone baseline: `data/exp_curves.json` (all 6 growth-rate cumulative-Exp tables, `[M15]` Task 4a), `PokemonRegistry.get_exp_for_level()` (already reads them correctly), `pokemon.json`'s `growth_rate` column (populated for all 386 species), and the EV formula's read-side (`floori(ev/4)`, already correct since M1) — but `PokemonSpecies.exp_yield` is a dormant schema field never populated per-species (same gap class as `gender_ratio`/`base_friendship` before their own fixes), EV-yield data doesn't exist anywhere, and there is genuinely zero Exp/leveling mechanism of any kind (`current_exp`/`level_up` confirmed absent via direct grep). Traced the exact live config branch at this project's `GEN_LATEST=GEN_9`, each `B_*` re-verified line-by-line against source (re-checked after an initial challenge to the trainer-bonus claim — confirmed accurate, not a misread): `B_SCALED_EXP`'s `/5` formula (a real non-monotonic history — Gen5 scaled, Gen6 reverted to unscaled, Gen7+ scaled again); `B_SPLIT_EXP`'s full-undivided-Exp-to-every-participant model (Gen 6+ in origin, not Gen-9-specific); and `B_TRAINER_EXP_MULTIPLIER`'s 1.5× trainer bonus being OFF at this config (`<=GEN_7` gate, `GEN_9` fails it) — a real, separately-timed Gen 7 change distinct from Gen 6's bigger formula overhaul, per the config's own comment and this project's standing source-over-Bulbapedia principle; flagged for an independent spot-check given how easy this specific detail is to miss. Identified the single highest-leverage open design question (full party-wide/Exp-Share-aware recipient dispatch, matching source, vs. a simpler single-recipient model extending Moxie's existing `_last_attacker` hook — the same tension `docs/m18_5h_recon.md`'s own Section F1 flagged for EV gain, now unavoidable since Exp gain is M20's own primary deliverable rather than a deferrable side-system) plus a move-learning-at-level-up scope question (auto-replace vs. a first-ever mid-battle player-choice prompt). Proposed a 4-part sub-tier sequence (M20a data pipeline → M20b core Exp/level-up dispatch → M20c EV-gain grant logic, closing `[M18.5h]`'s own deferred loop → M20d level-up move learning), with Rare Candy/hard level caps/the Exp Share bag item/friendship mechanics/trainer-side leveling all flagged out of scope for the milestone's own core deliverable. No code/test changes — report-only, decisions for Rob before M20a starts. **Two follow-up Step 0 addenda (same day)**, both report-only: (1) full multi-participant split mechanics (eligibility = alive-right-now via `IsValidForBattle`'s HP check, layered on top of `gSentPokesToOpponent`-style per-opponent-instance tracking that resets whenever a NEW opponent occupies a field slot but is never cleared by a participant's own fainting) plus an Exp-Share/Exp-All feasibility pass (confirmed `ITEM_EXP_ALL` is a plain compile-time alias for `ITEM_EXP_SHARE` in source — no distinct mechanic exists, recommend dropping "Exp All" from scope entirely); (2) the Traded-bonus-vs-additive-components summation order (confirmed source sums ALL of a recipient's components first, THEN applies any per-recipient multiplier exactly once to the total — demonstrated numerically divergent from a "multiply-then-sum" alternative).
- M20 EXP design (Gen VII+ base formula, final 3-piece design locked in): **COMPLETE (design)** — 2026-07-15. A further Step 0 pass superseded the Gen III formula target from the recon above with a Gen VII+ canonical base formula plus two fully-custom pieces. **I.1 (base formula)**: source-verified with one material correction — the draft's `floor(sqrt(A)*A^2)` was wrong; source's real 211-entry table (`sExperienceScalingFactors`, `battle_script_commands.c:100-311`) encodes `floor(i^2*sqrt(i)/4)` (the `/4` is real and load-bearing, verified numerically against 6 spot-checked table entries, not assumed to cancel out) — recommended porting the literal table rather than computing `sqrt()` at runtime. Confirmed `A`/`C` index formulas otherwise match the draft exactly, with `C` fetched fresh per-recipient (confirming each recipient's value is fully independent). B's modifiers (Lucky Egg/Traded/Affection/Exp Charm) all confirmed unbuilt in this project (no trade/OT system, no item, no affection concept exists) — plus a 5th modifier not in the original list (`B_UNEVOLVED_EXP_MULTIPLIER`, flagged not silently added/dropped, deferred to M26). Net: B carries zero modifiers. **I.2 (custom 1-6 participant distribution table, 100/65/55/50/45/40%)** and **I.4 (Difficulty Setting enum: NORMAL ×1.0/HARD ×0.5/CASUAL ×1.35, applied last)**: original design, not source-verified, confirmed final. Difficulty Setting confirmed as a genuine mutually-exclusive `enum DifficultyMode` (matching `BattleManager`'s own existing `enum BattlePhase`), stored as a new `var difficulty_mode: int` directly on `BattleManager` — the only option given this project has no persistent save/settings layer yet (M32), flagged for future migration. **I.3 (20% automatic non-participant bonus) explicitly DEFERRED, not built** — and corrects `[M20 Recon]`'s own Section G conclusion: the real final target is the Gen VI+ "always-on, no item" mechanic, NOT the classic held-item Exp Share Section G investigated (a dated correction note was added directly into Section G itself). No code written — design/verification only, per instruction.
- M20 EXP implementation (I.1 base formula + I.2 distribution table + I.4 Difficulty Setting): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-15, same day. The first real Exp-gain/leveling infrastructure this project has ever built (`[M20 Recon]` confirmed this was genuinely greenfield). Implements exactly the 3 authorized pieces using the literal 211-entry `EXP_SCALING_FACTORS` table (independently Python-diff-verified against the source-extracted array, not hand-retyped and trusted) — zero runtime `sqrt()`. New participant-tracking infrastructure (`BattleManager._exp_participants`, `_reset_exp_participants_for_opponent_slot`, `_add_exp_participant`) mirrors source's `gSentPokesToOpponent[flank]` exactly — reset per-opponent-field-slot whenever a NEW opponent switches in there, added-to whenever ANY player mon switches in, wired into all 4 established switch-in call sites (`_do_voluntary_switch`/`_do_forced_switch_in`/`_do_switch_in`/Baton Pass) plus `_phase_battle_start`'s one-time init — reproducing `[M20 Recon]` Section G1's two-layer eligibility rule exactly (tracked membership persists across a participant's own later fainting; only `current_hp > 0` at award time excludes it, per this project's own standing current_hp-not-.fainted convention). New `_award_exp_for_fainted_opponent`, wired after all 14 `pokemon_fainted.emit(...)` sites in `battle_manager.gd` (every faint cause — direct hit, status/weather/hazard/item damage, Destiny Bond/Aftermath retaliation — now awards Exp when the fainted mon is on the opponent's side, mirroring source's `IsOnPlayerSide` gate). New `BattlePokemon.current_exp` (pure accumulator, no level-up trigger yet — B5/B6 remain out of scope) and `BattleManager.difficulty_mode`. **Deliberately NOT done**: the 386-species `exp_yield` data-pipeline backfill (M20a) — the mechanism reads `species.exp_yield` directly regardless, and nothing in this project's current architecture converts `pokemon.json` rows into real `PokemonSpecies` instances at runtime yet, so the backfill has zero effect on anything testable this session; still open, matching the recon's own M20a/M20b split. One real test-authoring bug caught and fixed on the first run (a hand-computed expected value used the wrong recipient level from a different worked example — confirmed via direct debug printing, not guessed), stable across 4 reruns after. Full regression: `scripts/count_assertions.sh` run twice via the hardened absolute-path invocation (one dispatch hit the still-separately-flagged transient empty-log/exit-1 failure, resolved by a bare retry) — both clean, 122 files, GRAND TOTAL 12726 and 12725 respectively, each differing from the clean **12727** baseline (12693 prior + 34 new) only by already-documented pre-existing flaky suites rotating between runs (`m17l_test` in sweep 1; `m18q_test`+`m19a_gen1_test` in sweep 2 — a different subset each time, exactly the scattered-noise pattern this file's own baseline note already describes) — zero failures traceable to this session's own changes in either run. - M20a (exp_yield / ev_yield_* data-pipeline backfill): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-15, same day. Closes the one item `[M20 EXP implementation]` deliberately left open. Recon confirmed exact source struct fields (`include/pokemon.h:403-410`): `u16 expYield` (widened from `u8` "for the new Exp System," per source's own comment) and 6 **2-bit bitfields** `evYield_HP`/`evYield_Attack`/`evYield_Defense`/`evYield_Speed`/`evYield_SpAttack`/`evYield_SpDefense` (confirming a hard `[0,3]` range from the struct itself, not assumed). Found 3 distinct value shapes across the 386 species (plain literal; an inline ternary gated on `P_UPDATED_EXP_YIELDS`/`P_UPDATED_EVS`, both resolving to this project's real `GEN_LATEST=GEN_9`; and, expYield only, 9 species routed through a named `#define` macro resolved via its own `#if/#elif/#else` block) — confirmed via full-source grep before writing any extraction logic, not assumed uniform. Ran once: **2702 field values updated across 386 species**; **7 spot-checks against known real reference values, all exact matches** (Bulbasaur 64/+1SpAtk, Ivysaur 142/+1SpAtk+1SpDef, Venusaur 263 via the named-macro branch/+2SpAtk+1SpDef, Charizard 267/+3SpAtk, Pikachu 112/+2Spe, Raichu 243/+3Spe, Unown 118/+1Atk+1SpAtk). - M20b (Level-up trigger + stat recalculation + move-learning — the last major piece of M20's original scope): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-15, same day. Report-only recon first (6 explicit questions), then approved implementation. **Level derivation**: confirmed source's real `GetLevelFromMonExp` (`pokemon.c:1466-1476`) is a fresh re-scan of the whole growth-rate curve every time, not an increment-and-check-once loop — a single Exp award crossing several level thresholds lands on the correct final level in one pass with no special multi-level handling needed. Dispatch order traced directly (`Cmd_getexp` states 2-4, `battle_script_commands.c:3960-4066`): give-Exp → level-up check → stat recalc/move-learn, all per-recipient-immediate, confirming `_award_exp_for_fainted_opponent` (right after `recipient.current_exp += amount`) as the correct insertion point. **Stat recalc**: `BattlePokemon._calculate_stats()` already existed and was already correct; the real HP rule (`CalculateMonStats`, `pokemon.c:1429-1448`) is a flat ADDITIVE delta — `current_hp += (new_max_hp - old_max_hp)`, clamped — not proportional scaling, not a full heal, not left unchanged. **Move learning**: source's real 3-way branch (`MonTryLearningNewMove`, `battle_script_commands.c:5553-5615`) is already-known→no-op, <4 moves→auto-learn, 4 moves known→a real player yes/no+replace-slot prompt this project has no UI for (M23 still ahead) — flagged for Rob's sign-off rather than resolved unilaterally; Rob approved auto-skip-by-default with a `_force_move_replacement_slot` forcing seam (mirroring `forced_nature`/`forced_ivs`) wired now, not deferred. **Evolution safety**: confirmed no caching anywhere — growth-rate and learnset are read fresh from `PokemonRegistry` by the recipient's CURRENT `species.national_dex_num` on every level crossed (`PokemonSpecies.growth_rate`'s own dormant `int` field, unpopulated by any production converter same as `exp_yield` before M20a, is deliberately bypassed in favor of this fresh-lookup approach — satisfies both "no int↔string enum needed" and "evolution-safe" at once). Implementation: new `BattleManager.level_up`/`move_learn_skipped` signals (reuses the pre-existing `move_learned` signal from Mimic/Sketch for the learn-event itself), `_check_level_up`/`_try_learn_move_at_level`, new `BattlePokemon.replace_move()` (mirrors `add_move`'s shape). New `scenes/battle/m20b_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 30/30 assertions — single level-up, multi-level-up-in-one-award (Bulbasaur 8→12, `level_up` firing 4 times ascending), the HP-delta math specifically (below-max and at-max starting HP cases), a negative control, the Bulbasaur-style multi-move-per-level case (level 15 → both Poison Powder and Sleep Powder), auto-learn under 4 moves, already-known-move skip, the 4-moves-known skip case, the 4-moves-known forced-replacement-slot override case, a dedicated evolution-interaction-safety test (mid-battle species reassignment Bulbasaur→Charizard, confirming the very next level learns Charizard's own move not Bulbasaur's — proving fresh, non-cached lookup), and one full-battle integration test driving the real `_award_exp_for_fainted_opponent` call site end-to-end. All 30 passed clean on the first run. Full regression: two sweeps via the hardened absolute-path invocation, 124 files each, GRAND TOTAL 13147 (sweep 1, exactly clean — 13117 prior + 30 new) then 13146 (sweep 2) — a direct line-by-line diff found exactly one differing suite, `m19a_gen1_test.tscn` (51/51 vs 50/51), confirmed by name against CLAUDE.md's own documented flaky-suite list (the Hydro Pump/Rough Skin whole-battle-aggregation bug from `[D4 CHEAP bundle]`), not a new or unexplained finding this time. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M20b]` entry and `docs/m20_recon.md`'s Section B (B4/B5/B6/B8) and Section E for full detail. **[Corrected by `[M20c]` below, shipped the same day]: at this point M20 was NOT yet fully complete** — EV-gain grant logic (M20c) still remained; see the `[M20c]` bullet immediately below for the actual completion of M20.
- M20c (EV-gain grant logic — the last piece of M20's original 4-part sequence): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-15, same day. Report-only recon first (6 explicit questions), then approved implementation, with one explicit correction requested up front: eligibility must be traced precisely, not assumed identical to Exp's own `alive_participants` set. **Trigger point**: `MonGainEVs` (`pokemon.c:5049-5152`) fires from two `Cmd_getexp` branches — the normal eligible-recipient branch (unconditional on the Exp reward itself) and a separate max-level/partner-excluded branch (`B_MAX_LEVEL_EV_GAINS>=GEN_5`, true at this project's config) where Exp is forced to 0 but EVs still gain. **Eligibility, traced precisely per the correction request**: the true recipient candidate list is built ONCE per fainted-opponent event (`IsValidForBattle` AND sent-in-or-Exp-Share, `battle_script_commands.c:3887-3900`) and BOTH branches draw from this same list — source's "max-level mon still gets EVs but 0 Exp" is a difference in OUTPUT VALUE for one category, not a different INPUT SET. **Stated plainly, as requested**: in this project's current code, `alive_participants` (already computed for Exp) genuinely IS the correct and complete EV-eligible set — no separate tracking exists or is needed, since this project's own Exp dispatch never special-cases max-level recipients either (a level-100 mon's Exp just accumulates harmlessly per `[M20b]`'s own early-return, a pre-existing simplification unrelated to EV-gain). **Grant formula + items**: exact order confirmed from source — base `ev_yield_X` → Power Item +8 to its one targeted stat (`POWER_ITEM_BOOST=(I_POWER_ITEM_BOOST>=GEN_7)?8:4` → 8 at this config, `src/data/items.h:11`) → Macho Brace ×2 (after the Power Item check) → clamp vs remaining TOTAL cap room → clamp vs remaining PER-STAT cap room → add. Macho Brace + all 6 Power items were already implemented (`[M18h]`) but only their Speed-halving half — their EV-modifying half was explicitly "permanently moot" pending EV-gain existing, now false; **real gap found and closed**: `ItemData` had no field distinguishing which Power item targets which stat, closed with a new `ev_boost_stat` field (matching THIS PROJECT'S OWN `STAT_*` order, not source's raw `secondaryId` enum order which places Speed before SpAtk/SpDef), populated for the 6 Power items via `gen_items.py`. **Caps**: `MAX_PER_STAT_EVS=(P_EV_CAP>=GEN_6)?252:255` → **252** at this project's `GEN_LATEST=GEN_9` config; `MAX_TOTAL_EVS=510` unconditionally; confirmed no badge-gated progressive cap is needed (source's own `GetCurrentEVCap()` defaults to `EV_CAP_NONE`, bypassing the badge system entirely, and this project has no badge/save-state system anyway). Rob's confirmed decisions: EVs full-value-always (no participant-count distribution — source has no split logic for EVs at all, doubly confirmed); Pokérus excluded (zero infrastructure, matches the Rare-Candy/level-cap precedent); Power Item/Macho Brace built now. New `BattleManager.EV_CAP_PER_STAT`/`EV_CAP_TOTAL`/`POWER_ITEM_EV_BONUS` constants, `ev_gained` signal, `_grant_evs(recipient, fainted_species)` (iterates in this project's own STAT_* order — HP/ATK/DEF/SPATK/SPDEF/SPEED — breaking the loop ENTIRELY once the total cap is hit, no partial credit to remaining stats, matching source's own early `break`), wired directly into `_award_exp_for_fainted_opponent`'s existing `alive_participants` loop alongside the Exp award and level-up check. New `scenes/battle/m20c_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 30/30 assertions — data integrity (cap constants, the 6 Power items' `ev_boost_stat` values); a basic single-stat grant; the key discriminator (2 participants sharing a kill both get the FULL undivided EV yield, contrasted directly against their own *Exp* amounts which ARE scaled identically by the 65%-for-2 distribution); both cap types independently including the STAT_-order tie-break at the total-cap boundary (DEF and SPATK fill exactly to 510, SPDEF — processed last — gets nothing); Power Item's +8 and Macho Brace's ×2 tested independently plus a dedicated "mutually exclusive" test (a single held item can never be both); the max-level-still-gains-EVs case through the real production call site; the EVs-don't-retroactively-change-stats discriminator (only a subsequent `_calculate_stats()` call — the same one `_check_level_up` uses — makes a granted EV visible); Klutz suppression; and a negative control. One real test-authoring bug caught and fixed on the first run: the stats-don't-retroactively-change discriminator's original level-10/4-EV fixture was too small to move `_stat_formula`'s own floored result, making the proof vacuous — fixed with a level-50/20-EV fixture large enough to guarantee a visible shift. All 30 passed clean after the fix. Full regression: two sweeps via the hardened absolute-path invocation, 125 files each, GRAND TOTAL 13175 then 13174 against a clean baseline of 13177 (13147 prior + 30 new) — a line-by-line diff found exactly two differing suites in total across both runs, `m19a_gen1_test.tscn` and `m18_5g_test.tscn`, both confirmed by name against CLAUDE.md's own documented flaky-suite list (both from the `[D4 CHEAP bundle]` statistical-flakiness class), not new or unexplained findings. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[M20c]` entry and `docs/m20_recon.md`'s Section E for full detail. **M20 (Experience & Leveling) is now genuinely fully complete** — every proposed sub-tier (M20a data pipeline, M20b core dispatch + level-up + move-learning, M20c EV-gain grant logic) has shipped. Only the explicitly-deferred I.3 (automatic 20% non-participant bonus, `[M20 EXP design]`) remains unbuilt, by design, not by omission.
- M21 (Doubles interaction cleanup — bundle-safe group): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-15, same day. Report-only recon first (exhaustive grep inventory of every flagged/deferred doubles gap across the project's history), then a Parabolic-Charge-drain-rounding-only recon (confirmed non-issue), then approved implementation of the bundle-safe group: items 1, 2, 3, 4, 7, 8 (test-only), 9 (test-only), 10 — **item 6 (Guard Dog + Flower Veil ally tie-break) explicitly EXCLUDED per Rob's own decision, dropped as low-value/niche, not an oversight**; items 5 (Dragon Darts smart-redirect) and 8's original scope (Trick Room × Pursuit doubles turn-order) were BOTH escalated to Rob mid-session via `AskUserQuestion` once Step 0 found each was riskier than its "bundle-safe" classification — both deferred to a future dedicated turn-order-splice session, per Rob's own choice. **Item 7 (TrainerAI doubles bug, a live correctness bug, done FIRST)**: `TrainerAI.choose_replacement`/`_best_switch_target` both still used the old singular `i == my_party.active_index` check (only excludes slot 0 of the active pair), unlike `get_first_non_fainted_not_active`'s already-fixed `not active_indices.has(i)` — in a doubles battle with BOTH slots alive, this let the AI recommend "switching in" a mon already active in the OTHER slot; fixed identically in both functions. **Item 3 (Red Card double-trigger guard)**: re-derived source's TWO distinct flags rather than assuming symmetry with Snatch's own turn-scoped guard — `_red_card_activated_this_move` (broad, set the moment a valid switch slot exists even if Guard Dog then blocks the actual switch, prevents a SECOND Red Card holder from also triggering) vs. `_red_card_switched_this_move` (narrow, set ONLY when the attacker actually leaves the field, gates Shell Bell AND Life Orb specifically) — both reset at the top of `_phase_move_execution`. **Item 1 (Shell Bell + Red Card interaction)**: confirmed source's real `sMoveEndScriptFuncs` dispatch order (`MOVEEND_CARD_BUTTON` precedes `MOVEEND_LIFE_ORB_SHELL_BELL`) — Shell Bell's heal AND Life Orb's recoil (a related, not-originally-flagged bug found via the same investigation) were both relocated from their original earlier positions in `_do_damaging_hit` to the tail of the function, both now additionally gated on `not _red_card_switched_this_move`. **Item 4 (Self-Destruct/Explosion ally-hit)**: confirmed `TARGET_FOES_AND_ALLY` (`CancelerSetTargets`) hits every OTHER battler in doubles including the user's own ally, with `GetTargetDamageModifier` using the same flat 0.75x for both 2- and 3-target cases at this project's config — new `MoveData.target_includes_ally` flag (set on Self-Destruct(120)/Explosion(153) only) wired into the spread-move dispatch branch; a full `moves_info.h` grep found ~18 OTHER already-implemented moves (Surf, Earthquake, Magnitude, Discharge, etc.) share this exact target type and the identical ally-hit gap, **deliberately NOT retroactively fixed this session** — flagged for a dedicated future sweep. **Item 2 (Shell Bell spread-accumulation, done LAST per its own dedicated test pass)**: the spread-move dispatch branch was restructured to accumulate damage/hit-count across ALL targets hit (each per-target `_do_damaging_hit` call now suppresses its own heal/recoil) and apply Shell Bell's heal + Life Orb's recoil exactly ONCE off the combined total — closes the real under-count (Shell Bell, floor-division truncation per-hit-and-summed) AND a separately-discovered, opposite-direction Life Orb bug (over-counting via its flat maxHP/10 recoil repeating once per target/hit instead of once per whole move) — the same fix also closes a third, pre-existing Life Orb bug in `_do_multi_hit_sequence` (repeating the flat recoil once per hit rather than once per whole multi-hit move), found only as a side effect of this session's own investigation. **Items 8/9 (test-only, no implementation expected)**: item 9 (Snatch vs Magic Coat/Bounce doubles ordering) shipped as a synthetic-`MoveData` test, matching the project's own `[M17n-5]` precedent for exercising a flag combination no real move carries (a full 717-move scan confirmed `snatch_affected` and `bounceable` are mutually exclusive categories with zero real-move overlap). **Item 8 escalated and deferred**: Step 0 found a genuine, previously-undocumented significant finding — Godot's `Array.sort_custom` is an UNSTABLE sort with no transitivity guarantee, so a same-side-speed-tie scenario made the Pursuit-interception turn-order test non-deterministically pass/fail across reruns with IDENTICAL code and inputs (confirmed via repeated debug-printed `_turn_order` state) — this is a real, deeper bug than "an untested-but-correct scenario," folded into the same future turn-order-splice session as item 5. **Item 10 (stale Infiltrator/screens doc comment, zero functional risk)**: corrected `damage_calculator.gd`'s `GetScreensModifier`-citing comment, which predated `[M17n-9]`'s Infiltrator implementation and incorrectly implied this stateless utility function had no Infiltrator awareness by design gap rather than by correct architecture (the bypass is actually handled at the `BattleManager._do_damaging_hit` caller level). New `scenes/battle/m21_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 33/33 assertions, stable across reruns — caught and fixed 3 separate whole-battle-aggregation test-authoring bugs along the way (item 3's second Red-Card-holder contamination via an independently-triggering Tackle-user, fixed with a synthetic 0-power STATUS move for the non-primary attacker; item 1's Shell-Bell/Life-Orb "did it ever fire" checks contaminated by a legitimate LATER re-trigger after faint-replacement, fixed via a new timeline-adjacency testing pattern — a combined ordered event array restricting the check to strictly between the attacker's own switch-out and its own next switch-in; item 2's initial full-multi-turn-battle test drafts re-casting the spread move every turn, fixed by rewriting all 6 tests to use a new `_dispatch_doubles_spread_with_signals` direct single-dispatch helper matching `ban_flag_audit_test.gd`/`d4_bundle9_test.gd`'s established precedent). Targeted regression per Rob's own instruction (tier-specific/doubles suites only, not a full sweep): `m18n_test` 22/22, `m18q_test` 16/16, `item_test` 77/77, `m18_5g_test` 315/315, `doubles_test` 54/54, `m19_bucket4_pairs_test` 52/52 — all clean. **Move-count/exclusion accounting unaffected (M21 is a bugfix/cleanup pass, not an M19 move tier)**. - NEW ITEM B (Status-move spread-targeting dispatch — structural gap): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-15, same day. Closes the highest-priority open item from the full-roster audit above. Step 0 re-derived the real per-target mechanism from source rather than assuming symmetry with the damage-move spread loop: `StatChangeSubstitute` (`battle_move_resolution.c` L4475-4490) loops over every battler independently BEFORE any stat applies; `MoveEndBouncedMove` (L3141-3202) tracks Magic Bounce/Coat as a PER-BATTLER BITMASK, resolving each pending bounce with its own full script re-execution and clearing only that one battler's bit — confirming a bounce by one target does NOT cancel the move's resolution against any OTHER target, which still proceeds normally (the key cross-target-independence question the task asked to resolve before writing any loop). **Real correction to the original recon's framing**: Teeter Dance(298) is `EFFECT_CONFUSE`, not `EFFECT_STAT_CHANGE` — its real mechanism dispatches through `try_apply_confusion`/`try_secondary_effect`, not `_apply_stat_change_effect`, and it does not carry `.magicCoatAffected` in source (correctly not bounceable). Design: extracted the existing single-target status dispatch's gate sequence (Magic Bounce/Coat → Substitute → type-immunity → Prankster-vs-Dark → the actual effect) into a new reusable `BattleManager._apply_status_move_to_target()`, called once per live opposing combatant (+ally if `target_includes_ally`) from a new early branch in `_phase_move_execution`, gated on `foe_targeting and move.is_spread and _active_per_side > 1` — a deliberate choice NOT to refactor the existing ~750-line single-target function (which contains many unrelated move-specific branches this fix doesn't touch). **A real conflict caught only by this session's own first test run, not by static Step 0 reading**: Venom Drench(599) — also `TARGET_BOTH`/`is_spread=True` — has its OWN pre-existing `is_venom_drench` dispatch branch that already loops `_get_live_opponents(attacker)` directly, confirmed (`_get_live_opponents`, `battle_manager.gd:6590-6601`) to already return every live opponent regardless of `_active_per_side` — **Venom Drench was ALREADY correctly hitting both opponents in doubles before this session**, via a completely separate, already-correct mechanism; the new generic branch was incorrectly intercepting it (its own data has no `stat_change_stat`/relevant `secondary_effect` for the generic dispatch to read) — fixed by excluding `not move.is_venom_drench` from the new branch's gate, letting it fall through unchanged to its own pre-existing branch. **NEW ITEM B's real scope is 8 moves, not 9** — Tail Whip(39)/Leer(43)/Growl(45) (gained `is_spread=True`, were missing it entirely), String Shot(81)/Cotton Spore(178)/Poison Gas(139)/Sweet Scent(230) (already had `is_spread=True`, now finally live), and Teeter Dance(298) (gained `target_includes_ally=True`). New `scenes/battle/new_item_b_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 29/29 assertions, stable across 4 reruns — Growl hitting both opponents (the core fix); Venom Drench's per-target-independent poison condition (one poisoned target gets all 3 drops, one non-poisoned gets none); Teeter Dance confusing both opponents AND the ally; Substitute blocking one target while the OTHER target in the same spread use is still hit normally; a Magic Bounce holder reflecting Growl back at the attacker while the OTHER target is STILL hit normally in the same spread use (the key cross-target-independence proof); singles and single-target-move-in-doubles negative controls. Two real test-authoring bugs caught and fixed on the first run (27/29): the Venom Drench interception above (a production bug, not a test bug); and the singles negative control's own whole-battle-aggregation instance (Growl has no fallback move, so a plain `start_battle` runs many turns re-casting it past -1 — fixed via a first-occurrence signal snapshot). A real, out-of-scope aside flagged not fixed: `_apply_one_stat_change_pair` (which Venom Drench's own branch calls) doesn't itself check Substitute/Magic-Bounce/type-immunity — a separate, pre-existing gap in Venom Drench's own implementation. - NEW ITEM C (`TARGET_FOES_AND_ALLY` full-roster ally-hit sweep): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-16. Step 0 re-derived the full 20-move `TARGET_FOES_AND_ALLY` list fresh via a from-scratch `moves_info.h` parse (not copied from prior counts), cross-checked each against CURRENT `gen_moves.py` state, and produced a corrected worklist: **13 confirmed still open** (Magnitude(222), Discharge(435), Lava Plume(436), Sludge Wave(482), Bulldoze(523), Searing Shot(545), Parabolic Charge(570), Petal Blizzard(572), Boomburst(586), Sparkling Aria(627), Brutal Swing(656), plus Surf(57)/Earthquake(89) — the latter two deliberately left without `target_includes_ally` by NEW ITEM A this same arc, confirmed still missing it), **3 already fully correct** (Self-Destruct(120)/Explosion(153) from M21's own bundle-safe session, Teeter Dance(298) from NEW ITEM B this same arc — verified, not assumed, that Teeter Dance needed zero further work), **4 not yet implemented** (Synchronoise/Mind Blown/Misty Explosion/Corrosive Gas, noted only). Per-move safety check on all 11 damage moves: Magnitude's own `is_magnitude` power-roll is computed once via `_dmg_power_override` before the spread/single split (same shape already proven safe for Eruption); Sparkling Aria's own `is_sparkling_aria` burn-cure reads the per-target parameter inside `_do_damaging_hit` (called once per target), confirming it correctly extends to cure the ally's own burn too — a genuine win, not just "no conflict." **A real, specifically-checked interaction, not assumed safe**: `AbilityManager.pressure_pp_cost`'s own spread-move branch loops ONLY over the opposing side's combatants and never reads `target_includes_ally` — structurally cannot count the ally regardless of this session's changes, confirmed via source that Pressure's PP surcharge is genuinely opponent-only by design even for a `TARGET_FOES_AND_ALLY` move; `m17n10_test.gd`'s own Magnitude-vs-two-Pressure-holders doubles test reconfirmed unaffected. **Parabolic Charge's drain guardrail explicitly re-confirmed per instruction**: the drain is computed inside `_do_damaging_hit`, called once per target — the ally is simply one more target in the SAME existing loop, healing the attacker off the ally's own hit independently, exactly matching source's real per-hit (not accumulate-then-heal-once, explicitly NOT the Shell-Bell pattern) drain behavior; no change to the drain mechanism itself was needed. `gen_moves.py`: added `target_includes_ally=True` to all 13 confirmed-open moves; Teeter Dance untouched.
