- NEW ITEM D scoping (Shared Accuracy Roll Architecture Gap — recon only, no code/tests): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-16. Re-derives from source, corrects and RAISES the severity of NEW ITEM A's own original framing (which had assumed, without verifying, that source might share this project's single-shared-accuracy-roll simplification — it does not). Confirmed via direct citation that source resolves BOTH ordinary accuracy (`CancelerAccuracyCheck`, `battle_move_resolution.c:2174-2260`, its own explicit per-battler loop calling `DoesMoveMissTarget` independently, reading each target's own evasion stage via `GetTotalAccuracy`) AND the semi-invulnerable bypass (a separate, structurally identical per-target canceler loop, `battle_move_resolution.c:1960-2010`, `CanBreakThroughSemiInvulnerablity` called independently per target) via DEDICATED PER-TARGET LOOPS — this project's own single shared `StatusManager.check_accuracy` call (`battle_manager.gd:2658`, before the spread/single split) is a confirmed, genuine divergence, not shared upstream behavior. Traced current behavior precisely: a miss on the single shared roll aborts the WHOLE move (zero targets hit); a hit unconditionally passes EVERY live target to `_do_damaging_hit()` with no further per-target accuracy/semi-invulnerable check at all (confirmed via its full body) — a strict all-or-nothing binary, no partial-hit outcome is currently possible. Neither `check_accuracy` nor `_can_hit_semi_invulnerable` need logic changes (both already stateless and per-target-capable) — the gap is purely a call-site scoping issue. Exact affected-move count queried directly (not estimated): **59 currently-implemented `is_spread=True` damage-category moves** (not the "~37" originally estimated — that predated NEW ITEM A/C's own pool growth). Two concrete player-visible impact classes identified: a high-frequency case (any two opposing targets with different evasion/accuracy-modifying state get an architecturally-impossible-to-diverge shared outcome) and a lower-frequency, higher-severity case (a spread move vs. one semi-invulnerable + one grounded target can wrongly hit the semi-invulnerable one OR wrongly block the grounded one, depending on which the project's own default-target logic happens to check) — not empirically reproduced this session (recon-only), but a direct conclusion from the traced code paths. Blast-radius assessed as a contained core fix (wrap the existing, unchanged per-target-capable checks in a loop) with real surrounding bookkeeping needing its own design pass first (`move_missed`'s per-move signal shape, `crashes_on_miss`'s unresolved partial-spread-miss semantics, Blunder Policy's per-target trigger point) — secondary effects (flinch/stat-lowering/status) confirmed unaffected, already correctly per-target. Cross-referenced against the turn-order-splice trio/Acupressure/Lightning-Rod-Storm-Drain-redirect: independent, only a soft thematic overlap with Dragon Darts' own per-hit-miss concept. **Per explicit instruction, this session stops short of a firm priority recommendation and flags the raised severity for Rob's own input** before any future session scopes implementation — three candidate placements identified (own dedicated session; folded into the turn-order-splice session; deprioritized), no default chosen. Findings written to `docs/m21_recon.md`'s new "NEW ITEM D" section and `docs/decisions.md`'s `[NEW ITEM D scoping]` entry. No commit made this session — per standing instruction, Rob commits.
- NEW ITEM D implementation (Shared Accuracy Roll Architecture Gap — Step 0 + implementation): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-16, same-day follow-up to the scoping session above. Step 0 re-verified fresh (not trusted from the scoping session) and resolved all 6 open design questions cleanly, no genuine tangle: `crashes_on_miss` (Jump Kick/High Jump Kick/Axe Kick/Supercell Slam) confirmed via direct source read to be `.target=TARGET_SELECTED` for all 4 — never co-occurs with `is_spread`, a non-issue; `recoil_percent`/`drain_percent`/`is_rage`/`is_recharge` are all already gated on `damage > 0` inside `_do_damaging_hit` (called once per target), composing correctly for free once a missed target is simply skipped; `is_rollout`/`is_fury_cutter`/`is_steel_beam`/`is_rampage`/`is_uproar` also confirmed via `gen_moves.py` grep to never co-occur with `is_spread`, so the pre-existing shared miss-handling block is simply and safely skipped for spread moves; Dragon Darts' smart-target mechanism dispatches through the separate `multi_hit`/`strike_count` branch, confirmed untouched; `StatusManager.check_accuracy` (already calling its own internal `_can_hit_semi_invulnerable` per its `defender` param) needed zero logic changes — a pure call-site scoping fix; Blunder Policy resolved as a disclosed simplification (fires only when a spread move's accuracy roll misses EVERY live target, matching `move_missed`'s own new single-shot threshold), via a new shared `_apply_blunder_policy_on_miss` helper reused by both the pre-existing single-target path and the new spread path. Implementation: the old single shared accuracy-check block is now guarded to skip spread moves entirely (`if not (move.is_spread and _active_per_side > 1):`); each live target (opponents + ally, if `target_includes_ally`) now gets its own independent `StatusManager.check_accuracy` call inside the spread-dispatch loop before `_do_damaging_hit` runs for it, mirroring source's real per-battler `CancelerAccuracyCheck` loop — a miss excludes only that one target, others in the same use resolve normally. New `move_missed_target(attacker, target, reason)` signal fires per individual miss; the existing `move_missed` signal stays single-shot, firing only on a full "every target missed" spread use (preserving `_current_action_failed`'s Stomping-Tantrum-timer semantics). Confirmed composes correctly with `[M21]`'s own Shell Bell/Life Orb spread-accumulation fix — a missed target simply never reaches `_do_damaging_hit`, contributing 0 to the accumulated total by construction. Test-audit-first pass found zero existing assertions needed fixing (every spread-move test in this codebase already used `_force_hit` or a hardcoded `accuracy=100`, both behaviorally identical whether accuracy is checked once or once-per-target). New `scenes/battle/new_item_d_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 18/18 assertions, stable across 5 reruns — a fully-deterministic semi-invulnerable+grounded independence proof (Earthquake hits both a grounded and a mid-Dig target in one spread use; Rock Slide, lacking `damages_underground`, hits only the grounded one), partial-miss-vs-full-miss signal-shape discriminators, Blunder Policy's full-miss-only threshold, a 60-trial statistical evasion-divergence proof (0-evasion target hits 100% of trials independent of a +6-evasion target's own ~33% rate), Shell Bell accumulation excluding a missed target's contribution, and a singles negative control. Targeted regression (14 suites) plus two full regression sweeps (130 files, GRAND TOTAL 13317 both times) all clean except the already-documented pre-existing `m19a_gen1_test.tscn` flake (unrelated, reconfirmed via standalone rerun). **This closes the full NEW ITEM A/B/C/D arc** — remaining open items are the turn-order-splice family (items 5/8/11/12/13), Acupressure's ally-choice gap, and Lightning Rod/Storm Drain's attacker-ally redirect, none touched. These moved into Bucket 3 (15→30). [CORRECTED by `[M19-secondary-stat-audit]`, 2026-07-09: the plan's own stale Bucket 3 count was NOT a repeat of this field-naming bug — `[M19-rescope]`'s own classifier never had a stat-field list to omit anything from; its bug was counting `STAT_CHANGE_EFFECT_PLUS/MINUS` token occurrences, not distinct sub-fields per block. Independently re-verified by tracing every `stat_change_stat` reference in `battle_manager.gd`: all live inside the pure-status-move-only branch, never inside `EFFECT_HIT`'s own damage-execution path. The plan's own confident claim (from `[M19-pipeline-fix]`) that these moves' "real mechanics... are the exact same generic dispatch every other Tier 2 stat-change move already uses" was an unverified assumption — the cited examples (Mud-Slap/Icy Wind/Rock Tomb) were never actually implemented. A single new mechanism (extend `EFFECT_HIT` dispatch to roll+apply `stat_change_stat`, mirroring `try_secondary_effect`'s existing chance-roll shape) would unlock all 79 at once — flagged as its own top-priority Bucket 4 sub-group (`M19-secondary-stat-on-hit`), not built here per this tier's explicit no-new-dispatch scope. **(4)** 2 more found via a `.target` field sweep: Howl (`TARGET_USER_AND_ALLY` at GEN8+) and Aromatic Mist (`TARGET_ALLY`, buffs the ally not the user) — this project has no ally-targeting stat-change mechanism in any form. **135 confirmed genuinely single-mechanism reuse and implemented**, across 8 mechanism groups (`EFFECT_HIT`+single-secondary 72, pure `EFFECT_STAT_CHANGE` 30, `EFFECT_NON_VOLATILE_STATUS` 9, `EFFECT_RECOIL` 9, `EFFECT_ABSORB` 8, `EFFECT_CONFUSE` 3, `EFFECT_SEMI_INVULNERABLE` 2 [Dive/Bounce], `EFFECT_TWO_TURNS_ATTACK` 2 [Freeze Shock/Ice Burn]) — zero new dispatch logic added, matching this tier's own scope. - M19-secondary-stat-on-hit (Bucket 4's single highest-leverage sub-group — unlocks all 79 `EFFECT_HIT` + stat-token moves flagged by `[M19-bucket2]`): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Step 0 re-verified everything from scratch (a genuinely different extraction method than whatever produced the original 79-list) rather than trusting `[M19-bucket2]`'s numbers blindly: 92 `EFFECT_HIT`+`MOVE_EFFECT_STAT_PLUS/MINUS` entries found, 10 genuinely multi-stat (Bucket 3, excluded — including Clangorous Soulblaze, a Z-move-exclusive whose auto-incremented enum value never resolves a numeric ID), minus Triple Arrows(771)/Make It Rain(802) (separate mechanisms) = 79, cross-checked byte-for-byte against a raw pre-compaction extraction with zero ID differences. **Count correction: the true, final figure is 79, not 78** — Bleakwind Storm(774) is confirmed double-blocked (carries BOTH the still-unbuilt weather-conditional-accuracy mechanism AND a stat-change token) but was ALREADY excluded from the 79 before this session started, so "79 minus Bleakwind Storm = 78" double-subtracts something never counted; both independent derivations agree on 79 with Bleakwind Storm already outside it. A first-draft extraction script bug was caught and fixed before generating any data: it resolved GEN-conditional ternaries by blindly taking the first branch regardless of comparison operator, misclassifying Crunch/Acid (whose two candidate sub-fields are gated by OPPOSITE-direction comparisons on the same condition) as multi-stat — fixed by resolving each ternary against its actual operator. Self-targeted fraction confirmed much higher than assumed (24/79, 30%, not "almost certainly foe-only") — the existing `stat_change_self` field already generalized correctly. Magnitude spread confirmed NOT uniform ±1 (10 moves are ±2). Guaranteed-vs-explicit-100 chance distinction confirmed to have real behavioral consequences: 10 moves (all self-targeted post-hit drops — Overheat, Draco Meteor, Leaf Storm, Psycho Boost, Fleur Cannon, Ice Hammer, Clanging Scales, Zippy Zap, Spin Out, Hammer Arm) omit `.chance` in source entirely and are encoded `secondary_chance=0` (guaranteed, Sheer-Force-exempt), matching real game behavior, vs. 69 with an explicit value remaining subject to Shield Dust/Covert Cloak/Sheer Force/Serene Grace normally. Design: `StatusManager.try_secondary_effect` gained one new escape hatch (`secondary_effect == SE_NONE and stat_change_stat >= 0 → return true`, same "caller applies it" shape as the pre-existing `SE_FLINCH` case) reusing its existing chance-roll/Serene-Grace/Shield-Dust/Covert-Cloak/Sheer-Force gating for free; its own internal early-return and `battle_manager.gd`'s caller-side gate BOTH needed widening, since these moves have `secondary_effect == SE_NONE` by construction. New `BattleManager._apply_stat_change_effect(attacker, defender, move, ng_active)` — extracted verbatim from the pre-existing pure-status-move `EFFECT_STAT_CHANGE` dispatch (Mirror Armor redirect / Defiant-Competitive / Opportunist / Mirror Herb) so the new damage-move call site reuses it exactly rather than re-deriving any of it; the pure-status-move branch now just calls this function, confirmed behavior-unchanged via regression. New dedicated `elif` branch in `_do_damaging_hit`'s `if effect_hit:` dispatch, same reasoning as the pre-existing `SE_WRAP` carve-out (the general `else` branch's status-cure-berry checks don't apply to a stat change). New `m19_secondary_stat_test.gd`/`.tscn`: one table-driven loop over all 79 moves (core data + every flag, `secondary_effect` confirmed to stay `SE_NONE`) plus 8 functional checks (±1/±2 magnitude, self-vs-foe targeting, the force_secondary=true/false gate — reusing this project's established direct-`try_secondary_effect`-call convention since no full-battle forcing seam exists for the secondary-chance roll specifically — the Sheer-Force-suppresses-and-boosts/guaranteed-chance-exempt pair, and the Mirror-Armor-redirects/self-targeted-bypasses-Mirror-Armor pair reusing `[M17n-11]`'s own full-battle pattern): 1754/1754 assertions, passed clean on the first run. Regression: `item_registry_test.tscn` 309/309, `status_test.tscn` 78/78, `stat_test.tscn` 78/78, `damage_test.tscn` 24/24 (the task's own non-negotiable set) plus a wider safety sweep given how central the extracted function is — `m17b_test.tscn` 109/109 (Defiant/Competitive), `m17n8_test.tscn` 58/58 (Opportunist), `m17n11_test.tscn` 51/51 (Mirror Armor), `m18m_test.tscn` 27/27 (Mirror Herb), `move_test.tscn` 49/49, `tier4_test.tscn` 86/86 — all unchanged. **Total move-implementation count: 351→430.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated: Bucket 4 recomputed (141→62 moves, 28→27 sub-groups), the `M19-weather-conditional-accuracy` sub-group's description corrected to flag Bleakwind Storm's double-block explicitly, both "recommended execution order" lists updated, top summary table and reconciliation formula recomputed (430+109+1+213+181=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[M19-secondary-stat-on-hit]` entry added with full Step 0 citations, including the 78-vs-79 count correction. Next recommended tier: Bucket 3 (30 moves, still open) or any of Bucket 4's remaining 27 sub-groups, per Rob's preference.
- Doc-sync fix + Bucket 3 multi-stat cluster (Ancient Power, Superpower, Silver Wind, Tickle, Cosmic Power, Bulk Up, Calm Mind, Dragon Dance, Close Combat, Ominous Wind, Hone Claws, Quiver Dance, Coil, Shell Smash, Shift Gear, Work Up, Noble Roar, Dragon Ascent, Tearful Look, Decorate, Victory Dance, Headlong Rush, Spicy Extract, Armor Cannon): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Part A (pure doc-sync, no design decision): `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md`'s top summary block had never been updated after `[M19-secondary-stat-on-hit]` shipped — still read 351/583 while Section E's bottom summary already read 430/504; fixed both to agree (454/480 after Part B's own shipment), confirmed via full-document sweep no other stale figure remained. Part B Step 0 re-derived Bucket 3's 25-move multi-stat cluster fresh from source rather than trusting the plan doc's list blindly — found and fixed a real gap in the extraction methodology itself: the first-draft scanner only caught "many stats in ONE block" (Growth/Ancient Power shape) and missed **Spicy Extract(786)**, which uses two SEPARATE single-stat blocks that together touch 2 stats — broadened to union stats across all of a move's blocks. Also needed a proper sequential C-enum walker for ID resolution (Hone Claws' ID is `= MOVES_COUNT_GEN4`, an auto-incremented symbolic constant, the same class of gap `[M19-secondary-stat-on-hit]` hit for Clangorous Soulblaze). After both fixes, the re-derived 25-move list matched the plan doc's own list byte-for-byte. Confirmed the cluster is genuinely non-uniform in three ways: (1) splits 8 `EFFECT_HIT` (damage moves) / 17 `EFFECT_STAT_CHANGE` (pure status) — both dispatch paths needed extending; (2) magnitude/sign not uniform ±1 (Shell Smash mixes +2 with -1 in one move; Shift Gear mixes +1 with +2); (3) **Coaching(739) is genuinely `TARGET_ALLY`** — a third targeting mode `stat_change_self: bool` can't represent, carved out and merged into `M19-ally-targeting-stat-change` (now 3 moves), leaving 24 shipped here. Confirmed Sheer Force/Contrary already fully generic (zero new code), but Mirror Armor and Defiant/Competitive both need PER-PAIR evaluation, not once per move — Spicy Extract's -2 Def redirects via Mirror Armor while its simultaneous +2 Atk does not; a 2-stat-lowering move against a Defiant holder correctly triggers it twice, confirmed as real game behavior via source, not a bug to avoid. Design (confirmed with Rob before implementing, per Step 0's own explicit fork): a generalized array-based mechanism, not a per-move flag matching `is_growth`'s precedent — cheap specifically because `[M19-secondary-stat-on-hit]` had already extracted `BattleManager._apply_stat_change_effect` into one shared function. New `MoveData` fields `extra_stat_change_stats`/`extra_stat_change_amounts` (parallel `Array[int]`, empty for every other move — empirically confirmed a plain bracket literal in a hand-written `.tres` loads correctly into a typed `Array[int]` export). `_apply_stat_change_effect` refactored into a new per-pair private helper (`_apply_one_stat_change_pair`), called once for the primary pair and once per extra pair, running Mirror Armor/Defiant/Opportunist/Mirror Herb independently per pair. Zero changes to either dispatch gate or to Sheer Force. New `m19_bucket3_multistat_test.gd`/`.tscn`: table-driven data-integrity loop over all 24 moves plus 7 functional checks scoped to what's genuinely new (pure-status multi-application, `EFFECT_HIT` guaranteed multi-application with damage-nonzero discriminator, Spicy Extract's per-pair Mirror Armor redirect — the key new-behavior test, Tickle's per-pair Defiant double-fire, Ancient Power's whole-secondary Sheer Force suppression, Bulk Up's per-stat Opportunist copy, Shell Smash's mixed-sign self-application). - Bucket 3 clusters 1-2 (Thunder Fang, Ice Fang, Fire Fang, Glitzy Glow, Baddy Bad): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Closes out Bucket 3 entirely (30/30). Two independent Step 0 investigations, one per cluster, per the task's explicit instruction. **Cluster 1 (combined secondary effects)**: confirmed from source (`Cmd_setadditionaleffects`'s loop, `CalcSecondaryEffectChance`/`MoveIsAffectedBySheerForce` both keyed per-additionalEffect) that Thunder/Ice/Fire Fang's status roll and flinch roll are genuinely TWO INDEPENDENT rolls — own RNG index, own Serene-Grace doubling, own Shield-Dust/Covert-Cloak/Sheer-Force gate each — confirming the historical "10%/10%, independently rolled" framing rather than assuming it. New `secondary_effect_2`/`secondary_chance_2` fields on `MoveData` (status stays in the existing slot 1; flinch moves to the new slot 2), dispatched via a SECOND `try_secondary_effect` call on a shallow-duplicated `MoveData` — the same "duplicate and substitute" pattern `[M17n-6]` established for move-type mutation, reused here instead of changing that function's own signature, composing every existing gate correctly for free. **A real cross-tier gap found and fixed**: `[M18k]`'s King's Rock/Razor Fang mutual-exclusion gate only ever checked slot 1 for native `SE_FLINCH` — latent until this tier, since no prior move had native flinch anywhere but slot 1 — extended to check both slots, verified via a dedicated n=300 statistical rate test (King's Rock's own roll forced true) confirming the observed flinch rate tracks Thunder Fang's native ~10%, not the ~100% a stacked independent roll would produce if the fix were absent. **Cluster 2 (screen+damage)**: confirmed both Glitzy Glow/Baddy Bad are `EFFECT_HIT` (power 80/accuracy 95 at GEN_LATEST) with a guaranteed (no `.chance` field), self-targeted `MOVE_EFFECT_LIGHT_SCREEN`/`MOVE_EFFECT_REFLECT` additional effect, dispatched via the SAME `TrySetReflect`/`TrySetLightScreen` source calls the pure-status Reflect/Light Screen moves already use — confirmed, by actually tracing it rather than assuming either way, that this project's own `is_reflect`/`is_light_screen` dispatch branches return immediately with zero damage dealt, meaning a damaging move genuinely could NOT reach them before this tier — a real gap, not a "verify it's already fine" outcome. New `sets_reflect_on_hit`/`sets_light_screen_on_hit` per-move flags, dispatched inside `_do_damaging_hit` unconditional on `damage > 0` alone (not routed through `try_secondary_effect`, since this is a guaranteed/primary effect), reusing the exact same already-up no-refresh check and Light-Clay-aware duration extension. New `m19_bucket3_cluster12_test.gd`/`.tscn`: data integrity for all 5 moves plus 11 functional checks (Cluster 1: slot 1/slot 2 direct-call firing, cross-slot independence, Sheer Force suppressing both, Shield Dust blocking both, a full-battle synthetic-100%-move integration test proving the REAL dispatch fires both effects together, the King's Rock statistical mutual-exclusion test; Cluster 2: damage+screen together for both moves, a side-index check confirming the screen always lands on side 0 — the attacker's own side, never the target's, and an already-up no-refresh test). 47/47 assertions pass, stable across 3 reruns. - Bucket 4 cheapest singles (Rage, Clear Smog, Incinerate, Sparkling Aria, Throat Chop, Eerie Spell, Blood Moon — 7 of 9 originally-proposed single-move sub-groups): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Secret Power(290) and Uproar(253), the other 2 moves in this batch, were investigated with the same Step 0 rigor but explicitly DEFERRED by Rob via `AskUserQuestion`, not shipped. **Secret Power**: its secondary depends on `gBattleEnvironment`, an overworld map/tile-derived field this project has zero analog for (no map system at all) — confirmed `BATTLE_ENVIRONMENT_PLAIN`'s own GEN_LATEST effect is a trivial 30% Paralysis chance (fully schema-representable, offered as the cheap option), but Rob chose to defer entirely rather than hardcode. **Uproar**: turned out to need the SAME multi-turn forced-move-repeat primitive (`gLockedMoves`) Bucket 4's still-unbuilt `M19-rampage` sub-group (Thrash/Petal Dance/Outrage/Raging Fury) needs — genuinely not "cheap/self-contained" like this session's other 8 moves — plus a field-wide (BOTH sides, a real correction to a plausible "self-team-only" assumption) sleep-infliction block and a one-time wake-everyone-up trigger; Rob chose to defer and bundle with a future M19-rampage tier rather than build the shared lock now. Of the 7 shipped: **Rage** confirmed NOT a rampage-lock either (no `gLockedMoves` in its own case) — a simple `rage_active` volatile set on a successful hit, cleared when a different move is chosen, whose reactive half raises the holder's own Attack +1 on any subsequent damaging hit taken (self/ally-hit excluded). **Clear Smog** resets all 7 stat stages to exactly 0 (an absolute reset the existing relative-delta schema can't represent — no Haze precedent exists to reuse, since Haze itself remains unimplemented). **Incinerate** destroys (not consumes) the target's held Berry, deliberately bypassing this project's `_consume_item` (which would incorrectly also trigger Cheek Pouch/register `last_consumed_berry`) while still correctly triggering Unburden via a small dedicated destroy-path; Gems are permanently moot (none exist in this project). **Sparkling Aria** cures the TARGET's own burn, the inverse of every existing self-cure precedent. **Throat Chop** and **Eerie Spell** are both explicit chance=100 true secondaries needing their own new `SE_THROAT_CHOP`/`SE_EERIE_SPELL` constants; Eerie Spell resolved the task's own "does per-Pokémon last-move tracking exist" question with a clean yes — this project's pre-existing `last_move_used` field (wired since `[M16e]`'s Conversion 2) already answers it, zero new state needed. **Blood Moon** reuses that SAME `last_move_used` field for its own "can't use twice in a row" check (reference-equality, the same pattern the existing Disable check uses) — resolving the task's own "can these two share one mechanism" question with an even cheaper answer than proposed: reuse an existing field, not build a new shared one. New `MoveData` fields (`is_rage`/`is_clear_smog`/`is_incinerate`/`is_sparkling_aria`/`cant_use_twice`, plus the two new `SE_*` constants), new `BattlePokemon.rage_active`/`throat_chop_turns` volatiles (both switch-cleared), new `status_cured` signal. New `m19_bucket4_cheap_singles_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 46/46 assertions, stable across 4 reruns. **A real self-inflicted bug was found and fixed mid-session**: an earlier `Edit` call in this SAME session (adding `rage_active`/`throat_chop_turns` to `battle_pokemon.gd`) had accidentally deleted the pre-existing `last_consumed_berry` field declaration instead of preserving it alongside the new fields — silently breaking `_consume_item`'s Harvest/Cud-Chew tracker assignment, surfaced by this tier's own Sticky Hold discriminator test crashing with a spurious type-mismatch error. Root-caused via a plain Tackle-vs-Tackle repro with zero Incinerate/Sticky-Hold involvement (both were red herrings), fixed by restoring the missing declaration, and reverified via a regression sweep including `m17n7_test` (Harvest/Cud Chew's own origin suite). - M19-rampage (Thrash, Petal Dance, Outrage, Raging Fury, Uproar merged in): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Closes Bucket 4's core rampage-lock sub-group, resolving `[Bucket 4 cheapest singles]`'s own Uproar deferral by merging it in here per Rob's confirmation (`AskUserQuestion`), matching the Spirit Shackle/M19f precedent rather than tracking it as a separate closed sub-group. Step 0 confirmed all 4 "true" rampage moves are structurally IDENTICAL in source (same `MOVE_EFFECT_THRASH` additionalEffect, same 2-3 turn range, no per-move behavior difference — Raging Fury deliberately has no `makes_contact`, confirmed not assumed) and that the lock is a genuine FORCED REPEAT (`HandleAction_UseMove` overrides the chosen move unconditionally, bypassing selection entirely — not "user-selected-but-can't-switch"). Uproar shares the same `gLockedMoves` primitive but its own counter (flat 3 at this project's Gen5+ config) and a genuinely different end-of-lock behavior: no self-confuse. Confirmed via source: a miss does NOT cancel a continuing lock (still decrements, still confuses on schedule); a type-IMMUNE hit against a continuing lock cancels it WITHOUT confuse (a real, distinct rule from a miss); a first-use immune hit never sets the lock at all; target-faints-mid-rampage and attacker-faints/switches-mid-lock both need zero special-case code (confirmed free from this project's existing `_default_target`, recomputed fresh every turn, and `_clear_volatiles`, already called at every faint/switch site). Uproar's sleep-block is FIELD-WIDE (both sides, not just the user's own team — confirming the correction already flagged in the prior session's deferred entry) and only blocks NEW sleep at this project's Gen5+ config (does not wake already-sleeping mons). Design fork confirmed with Rob before implementing: a NEW dedicated `BattlePokemon.locked_move` field, kept SEPARATE from the pre-existing `charging_move` field (matches this project's own one-field-per-lock convention — `disabled_move`/`encored_move`/`choice_locked_move` are all separate too — and avoids interference with `charging_move`'s own two-turn/Bide-specific dispatch gates). Both `is_rampage` and `is_uproar` share `locked_move` but use distinct counters (`rampage_turns`/`uproar_turns`) to tell the end-of-lock behavior apart. New `BattleManager._is_uproar_active()` (field-wide scan, same shape as `_is_neutralizing_gas_active()`) threaded as a new `uproar_active` param into `StatusManager.try_apply_status`/`try_secondary_effect` and `AbilityManager.try_contact_effects` (Effect Spore's own sleep roll). Two new signals (`rampage_lock_started`/`rampage_lock_ended`) make every lock-ending scenario cleanly observable for testing. New `m19_rampage_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 33/33 assertions, stable across 4 reruns — every multi-turn/lock-ending assertion snapshotted via signal handlers guarded to the first occurrence rather than reading state after `start_battle()` returns, since every fixture's attacker has the rampage/Uproar move as its only move (a new cycle can legitimately restart later in the same battle); a first draft of the Uproar field-wide-block test read state post-battle and would have been genuinely wrong (Uproar's lock has a one-turn gap every cycle where `_is_uproar_active()` legitimately returns false), fixed by snapshotting at the opponent's first Sleep Powder attempt only. - M19-recharge (Hyper Beam, Blast Burn, Hydro Cannon, Frenzy Plant, Giga Impact, Rock Wrecker, Roar of Time, Prismatic Laser, Meteor Assault, Eternabeam): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Bucket 4's largest remaining sub-group. Step 0 found the 10 are NOT mechanically uniform (Prismatic Laser is 160/100/10, not the 150/90/5 norm; Meteor Assault is 150/100/5; Giga Impact/Rock Wrecker/Meteor Assault are Physical, the rest Special; only Giga Impact makes contact — Rock Wrecker is ballistic but non-contact, Meteor Assault is physical but non-contact). A genuine, source-confirmed CORRECTION to the commonly-assumed "recharges even on a miss" folklore, stopped-and-confirmed with Rob via `AskUserQuestion` before implementing: none of the 10 moves set `.preAttackEffect = TRUE` on their `MOVE_EFFECT_RECHARGE` additionalEffect, so it dispatches ONLY via `Cmd_setadditionaleffects`, itself only reachable via the successful-hit script path — a miss never sets the recharge lock in this reference engine, the opposite of "real games: regardless of hit/miss." Also confirmed a genuinely different mechanism SHAPE from `[M19-rampage]`'s `locked_move` forced-repeat lock: recharge is a PRE-MOVE canceler (source: `CancelerRecharge`, confirmed to run BEFORE Sleep/Truant in the real canceler chain), reusing this project's existing `StatusManager.pre_move_check` chokepoint (where Truant already lives) via one new `BattlePokemon.must_recharge: bool` rather than a forced-move-repeat lock, since there's no move to force — the Pokémon does nothing at all on the recharge turn. Switch-out/faint clears it for free (source's `rechargeTimer` lives in the same bulk-memset `Volatiles` struct every other switch-cleared field does), mirrored by the existing `_clear_volatiles`. New `m19_recharge_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 39/39 assertions, stable across 4 reruns after fixing two real test-authoring bugs, both fresh recurrences of already-documented CLAUDE.md pitfalls: a `%`-after-`+`-concatenation precedence bug (a `_chk` label's trailing `% [events]` bound only to the last string literal, which had no `%s` placeholder at all, producing a consistent non-fatal runtime error every run) fixed by parenthesizing the full concatenation; and a whole-battle-aggregation bug in the switch-out test (post-battle state read on `atk.must_recharge`, but `atk`'s own move is Hyper Beam — if its bench-mate later fainted, faint-replacement would force `atk` back in, where a later legitimate Hyper Beam use could re-set `must_recharge`, reproduced flaking 2 fails/5 runs) fixed by snapshotting inside the `pokemon_switched_out` signal handler instead. - M19-break-protect (Feint, Shadow Force, Phantom Force, Hyperspace Hole): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Step 0 found all 4 moves share the LITERAL SAME `MOVE_EFFECT_FEINT` additionalEffect — a genuinely uniform mechanism, directly contradicting the task's own suspicion that Feint (historically lower-power, a simple attack) might be structurally distinct from the other 3 (two-turn semi-invulnerable attacks). Confirmed `breaks_protect` is a real, ADDITIONAL mechanism beyond this project's pre-existing `ignores_protect` field: `ignores_protect` only lets a move's own hit bypass an already-up Protect check; `breaks_protect` is a separate POST-HIT mutation (source: `battle_script_commands.c`'s `MOVE_EFFECT_FEINT` case, L2584-2606) that clears the target's `protect_active` AND resets `protect_consecutive` (the Gen5+ 1/3^n fail-chance ramp `_roll_protect_success` reads) — confirming the task's own suspicion of a genuine unbuilt distinction, not a simple bypass flag covering everything. Confirmed POST-HIT ONLY (none of the 4 set `.preAttackEffect`) — a miss never breaks Protect, the same shape `[M19-recharge]` already established. Confirmed single-target scope only: source's side-wide-Protect-on-the-partner half (Wide Guard/Quick Guard/Crafty Shield) has nothing to act on since this project has zero side-wide protect moves implemented — not a gap, explicitly not built. Shadow Force/Phantom Force needed a genuinely NEW semi-invulnerable state (new `MoveData.SEMI_INV_VANISH`) — source's `STATE_PHANTOM_FORCE` explicitly returns FALSE from `CanBreakThroughSemiInvulnerablityInternal` (nothing hits through it, unlike Fly/Dig/Dive's own move-flag exceptions), a DIFFERENT branch from that function's own default (`STATE_NONE`/unknown → TRUE) — and this project's own `StatusManager._can_hit_semi_invulnerable` helper defaulted an unrecognized state to `true` too (the opposite of what's needed), so an explicit `match` case was required; caught and fixed BEFORE implementing by reading the helper's actual default, not discovered via a failing test. New `BattleManager.protect_broken` signal (mirrors the existing `protected` signal). New `m19_break_protect_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 26/26 assertions, stable across 4 reruns after fixing two test-authoring bugs on the first run — a `defender`-vs-`target` parameter-name mismatch (hard parse error, caught immediately) and a pre-set-before-`start_battle()` bug (`protect_active` is unconditionally cleared at the start of every turn, so 2 tests had to be restructured to have the defender genuinely USE Protect within the battle rather than pre-setting the post-reset field directly). - M19-recoil-on-miss (Jump Kick, High Jump Kick, Axe Kick, Supercell Slam): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Step 0 found all 4 moves share the LITERAL SAME `.effect = EFFECT_RECOIL_IF_MISS` — a genuinely uniform mechanism, directly contradicting the possibility that the two newer-gen additions (Axe Kick/Supercell Slam) might use a different crash formula. Confirmed the crash formula at this project's GEN_LATEST config is a FLAT 50% of the ATTACKER'S OWN max HP — NOT damage-scaled (source: `battle_move_resolution.c :: MoveEndMoveBlockRecoil`, `B_RECOIL_IF_MISS_DMG >= GEN_5` branch, an unconditional `if` that always overwrites the older defender's-HP-based `B_CRASH_IF_TARGET_IMMUNE == GEN_4` branch, which is dead code at this project's config anyway). Confirmed the miss-scope is genuinely BROADER than accuracy-only — source's `IsBattlerUnaffectedByMove` gate (`MOVE_RESULT_MISSED | MOVE_RESULT_FAILED | MOVE_RESULT_PROTECTED | MOVE_RESULT_DOESNT_AFFECT_FOE`) means crash also fires on a Protect block and ordinary type immunity — but EXCLUDES every pre-move-cancel failure (sleep/paralysis/Truant/etc., via the `!unableToUseMove` condition), since the attacker never attempted the move in those cases; this project's existing `pre_move_check` already gates all of those upstream, so nothing extra needed excluding. Also fixed a directly-adjacent, already-anticipated gap: Reckless's own power-boost check in source is gated on `{EFFECT_RECOIL, EFFECT_RECOIL_IF_MISS}` together, and this project's prior implementation only checked `recoil_percent > 0` — its own doc comment had explicitly flagged this exact re-check as needed once a crash-on-miss move existed. - M19-weather-conditional-accuracy (Thunder, Hurricane, Bleakwind Storm, Wildbolt Storm, Sandsear Storm): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-09. Step 0 confirmed exactly the task's own hypothesis: 2 genuinely separate flags, not 1 — `always_hits_in_rain` (all 5 moves, a FULL BYPASS of the entire accuracy chain, dispatched in the same early-exit function as No Guard/accuracy==0, source: `CanMoveSkipAccuracyCalc`) and `accuracy_halved_in_sun` (Thunder/Hurricane ONLY, a literal override to a flat 50 — not a ×0.5 multiply — applied at the exact insertion point `[M17n-11]`'s Wonder Skin already established, composing with rather than bypassing the rest of the modifier chain). Both gated on the ATTACKER's own effective weather, reusing the existing `ItemManager.blocks_weather_modifier` (Utility Umbrella) directly — no new item-check function needed. **A real correction beyond the task's own stated premise**: Bleakwind Storm was NEVER actually implemented before this session (re-verified via direct grep — no `.tres`/`gen_moves.py` entry existed for any of the 5 IDs) — it was correctly excluded from `[M19-secondary-stat-on-hit]`'s 79-move batch specifically because of this double-block, so its stat-on-hit half was never shipped either; this session built both halves together in one entry. Also confirmed `.windMove` (Hurricane + the Storm trio) has zero consumers anywhere in this project (no Wind Rider/Wind Power-style ability) — deliberately not modeled. - D3 turn-order/event-tracker batch (D2's turn-order-manipulation family [After You(495)/Quash(511)/Upper Hand(846)/Instruct(652)] + "stat/event happened this turn" tracker family [Lash Out(736)/Retaliate(514)/Rage Fist(815)/Echoed Voice(497)]): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. Both difficulty tags (MODERATE/CHEAP) re-verified rather than trusted, per this arc's own standing discipline — Part A's real findings landed almost entirely on Instruct (a genuinely new fall-through shape) and Upper Hand (a precise ability-boosted-priority re-check), Part B confirmed CHEAP as tagged except for one real empirically-discovered Retaliate timing nuance. After You(495)/Quash(511) both confirmed to read/write only the pre-existing `_turn_order`/`_current_actor_index` state `[M18j]`'s Zoom Lens/`[M17n-3]`'s Quick Draw already established as directly accessible — After You pushes the target to `_current_actor_index+1` (a no-op success when already there, matching this project's GEN_LATEST `B_AFTER_YOU_TURN_ORDER>=GEN_8` config), Quash pushes to the absolute end (a deliberate simplification of source's speed-order-preserving doubles-only branch, observably identical to source in singles). Upper Hand(846) re-derived fresh from source rather than assumed: connects only if the target's own CHOSEN move has an ability-boosted priority in [1,3] (via the exact same `AbilityManager.move_priority_bonus` function real turn-order sorting uses, not raw `move.priority`), target hasn't acted, and that move isn't status — on failure the whole move fails, matching the existing Sucker Punch "ButItFailed" shape. **Instruct(652) — the one genuinely new mechanism shape this session**: unlike Mirror Move/Metronome (which only reassign `defender`/`move`), Instruct reassigns `attacker` itself (the instructed Pokémon becomes the one actually executing), requiring `attacker_idx`/`attacker_side` to be recomputed too; the instructed move costs no PP (positioned after the existing PP-deduction block, the same "called move" shape Mirror Move/Metronome already establish); its exclusion list was re-derived against this project's own 23 currently-implemented `instructBanned` moves (21 already covered by pre-existing `two_turn`/`is_recharge`/`is_rollout`/`is_metronome`/`is_mirror_move`/`is_rampage`/`is_uproar` flags, Obstruct via `protect_method==PROTECT_METHOD_OBSTRUCT` specifically — source flags ONLY Obstruct+King's Shield among the whole Protect family, not a general rule — and Bide via a new `is_bide` check, the one real gap found). Lash Out(736) confirmed the exact decrease-side mirror of the already-shipped `stat_raised_this_turn` (new `BattlePokemon.stat_lowered_this_turn`, same chokepoint in `StatusManager.apply_stat_change`, same per-turn reset cadence). Retaliate(514) confirmed side-wide via a new `BattleManager._retaliate_timer` 2-element array, set to 2 on any faint on that side, decremented once per turn boundary — **a real, empirically-discovered timing nuance**: this project's own `_phase_end_of_turn` is SKIPPED for the turn a faint/replacement occurs in (pre-existing architecture), so the timer stays at 2 (undoubled) through the replacement mon's entire FIRST turn back, only reaching 1 (doubled) on its SECOND turn — caught via direct debug tracing after the test's first (intuitive but wrong) assumption failed. Rage Fist(815) confirmed a genuine BATTLE-LIFETIME counter (new `BattlePokemon.times_hit`, incremented in `_do_damaging_hit`'s existing `if damage > 0:` block, deliberately excluded from `_clear_volatiles` and confirmed via a dedicated unit test that it survives switch-outs, the same precedent as `[M17n-7]`'s Harvest). Echoed Voice(497) confirmed FIELD-WIDE (not per-mon/per-side) via new `BattleManager._echoed_voice_counter`/`_echoed_voice_used_this_turn`, incremented once per turn boundary if attempted (not gated on hit success), reset to 0 the instant a turn passes without use. New `d3_batch_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 48/48 assertions across 9 sections, stable across 4 reruns — 4 real test-authoring bugs fixed along the way (doubles party setup used the singular `active_index` instead of the required `active_indices`; a confounded Lash Out pairwise comparison using Growl, which also lowers the move's own damage-relevant Attack stat, fixed by switching to Scary Face's Speed-lowering instead; a fresh 4-way recurrence of the whole-battle-aggregation pitfall across all of Part B's pairwise comparisons, fixed with first-occurrence-only capture guards; an over-precise exact-equality assertion for doubled/tripled power — the same class CLAUDE.md's own `[D2 batch]` entry documents for Solar Beam — fixed with a new tolerance-based `_approx_scaled` helper) plus one real type-immunity confound (Rage Fist is Ghost-type, tested by default against a Normal-type opponent — flatly immune — fixed by adding an optional type parameter to the fixture helper). 19-suite targeted regression clean (`damage_test`/`move_test`/`stat_test`/`status_test` plus `m17k_test`/`m17n3_test`/`m17b_test`/`switch_test`/`tier4_test`/`doubles_test`/`item_registry_test`/`m18j_test`/`m19_bucket4_pairs_test`/`m19_rampage_test`/`m19_recharge_test`/`m17c_test`/`m19ef_test`/`m19_bucket3_multistat_test`/`m19_secondary_stat_test`; the full ~80-file automated sweep repeatedly failed to complete within this session's tooling constraints, so this targeted set — chosen to cover every directly and indirectly touched function — stood in for it). **Total move count: 588→596.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: both D2 families marked CLOSED with full findings, D5's recommendation updated (flagging the delayed-effect family as D2's last remaining cross-cutting family), Section E's two summary tables and top reconciliation recomputed (596+1+1+213+123=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[D3 turn-order/event-tracker batch]` entry with full Step 0 citations. **Section D's residual: 131→123.**
- Delayed-effect family + Psyshock/Psystrike (Future Sight(248)/Doom Desire(353)/Wish(273)/Yawn(281)/Healing Wish(361)/Lunar Dance(461) + Psyshock(473)/Psystrike(540)): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. Two independent pieces; closes D2 entirely (every cross-cutting family surfaced by `[M19-section-d-cluster]`'s original sweep has now shipped). **Part A — real correction to the task's own two-way framing: genuinely THREE mechanism shapes, not two.** (1) Per-slot delayed scheduler — Future Sight/Doom Desire (share `EFFECT_FUTURE_SIGHT`) and Wish — new `BattleManager` dictionaries keyed by combatant SLOT INDEX (mirroring source's own per-slot `gBattleStruct` storage, whose own code comment flags this as a deliberate simplification). Future Sight/Doom Desire resolve 2 turns later against whoever OCCUPIES the target's slot then (confirmed via a dedicated switch-survival test: the original target switches out, the replacement takes the hit instead), no accuracy roll ever, resolution routed through the EXISTING `_do_damaging_hit` chokepoint (screens/Substitute/Sturdy-chain/times_hit/Air Balloon all apply for free). Confirmed source ALWAYS resolves fresh at that later turn, never freezing cast-time snapshots — the caster's `stat_stages` are already correctly zeroed by the pre-existing `_switch_out_clear` if it switched away in the meantime, reproducing most of source's own "caster no longer present" fallback for free; the one disclosed gap is this project doesn't additionally null a benched caster's ability/item the way source's own struct-swap does. Wish resolves 1 turn later against whoever occupies the CASTER'S OWN slot, healing `caster's own max HP / 2` — fixed at cast time, confirmed via a dedicated discriminator NOT the eventual recipient's own max HP. (2) Per-mon volatile counter — Yawn — confirmed genuinely NOT part of the scheduler family despite the shared framing: mechanically IDENTICAL to the already-shipped `disable_turns`/`encore_turns`/`throat_chop_turns` pattern, zero new switch/faint infrastructure, already correctly cleared by `_clear_volatiles`; resolution fires a completely fresh sleep-infliction attempt via the existing `try_apply_status` pipeline (all immunities re-derived at that moment). (3) Switch-in-triggered one-shot — Healing Wish/Lunar Dance — a single per-slot flag with no counter, consumed by the slot's next switch-in by any method; unlike Explosion/Self-Destruct, FAILS OUTRIGHT (no faint) if no valid switch target exists (new `has_valid_switch_target()`-gated check). **A real finding surfaced only while writing tests, not from source reading alone**: "any switch method" isn't independently testable as a scenario different from plain faint-replacement for this move family specifically — the stored effect is created BY the caster's own faint, and faint-replacement for that exact slot follows immediately and unconditionally, so no other switch method can ever reach the slot first; an initial "test via forced Roar" design was scrapped once this was traced through. Both moves heal to full AND cure status; Lunar Dance additionally restores full PP on all 4 moves. **The one genuine judgment call, confirmed with Rob via AskUserQuestion before implementing**: real source's Gen8+ config lets the stored effect persist across multiple switch-ins until one actually benefits — simplified to always-consume-next-switch-in per Rob's choice. **Part B (Psyshock/Psystrike)** confirmed small and clean exactly as expected: `CalcDefenseStat`'s existing category-based branch gets one added OR condition reading the DEFENDER's Defense instead of Sp. Defense, no category swap, genuinely simpler in shape than Foul Play/Body Press (same battler, just a different stat column, not a cross-battler swap) — a third override alongside the two already-shipped ones in `DamageCalculator`, same insertion point. New `delayed_effect_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 41/41 assertions across 6 sections, stable across 5 reruns after fixing 3 real test-authoring bugs (a scrapped "via forced switch" test design, caught during Step-0-style tracing before it was ever run; a heal-amount assertion that didn't account for Wish's own missing-HP cap; a fresh whole-battle-aggregation recurrence where an unrelated later faint was misread as the move's own self-faint). 17-suite targeted regression clean (`damage_test`/`move_test`/`stat_test`/`status_test`/`switch_test`/`two_turn_test`/`m19_recharge_test`/`m19_rampage_test`/`d2_batch2_test`/`m17c_test`/`tier4_test`/`item_registry_test`/`d3_batch_test`/`doubles_test`/`m17n8_test`/`m17f_test`/`m17n9_test`). **Total move count: 596→604.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: D1's `EFFECT_FUTURE_SIGHT`/`EFFECT_PSYSHOCK` rows and D2's delayed-effect-family item all marked CLOSED with full findings (D1's own header corrected to 7 clusters/18 moves, folding in the earlier `EFFECT_FORESIGHT` closure its header had never been updated for), Section E's two summary tables and top reconciliation recomputed (604+1+1+213+115=934, reconfirmed). **Perish Song(195) confirmed still unbuilt**, still carrying its own Perish-Body-reconsideration cross-system note forward, unaffected by this session (a different mechanism entirely — a multi-battler delayed-faint countdown). `docs/decisions.md` new `[Delayed-effect family + Psyshock/Psystrike]` entry with full Step 0 citations. **Section D's residual: 123→115. D2 is now fully closed.**
- D1 easy bundle (6 remaining "easy" D1 clusters, 13 moves — EFFECT_HIT_ESCAPE [U-turn(369)/Volt Switch(521)/Flip Turn(740)] + EFFECT_HIT_SWITCH_TARGET [Circle Throw(509)/Dragon Tail(525)] + EFFECT_FIRST_TURN_ONLY [Fake Out(252)/First Impression(623)] + EFFECT_TRICK [Trick(271)/Switcheroo(415)] + EFFECT_REVENGE [Revenge(279)/Avalanche(419)] + EFFECT_STOMPING_TANTRUM [Stomping Tantrum(661)/Temper Flare(843)]; EFFECT_DOUBLE_POWER_ON_ARG_STATUS deliberately left out as the largest remaining cluster, deserving its own session): **COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. Move lists re-verified fresh against Section D before starting — matched exactly (13 moves/6 clusters), no drift this time. All 6 clusters confirmed small and mechanically-contained as tagged, but this session surfaced and fixed **two real bugs in already-shipped code**. Hit Escape (U-turn family): fires on a connecting hit INCLUDING a Substitute absorption, blocked if the attacker dies to recoil/contact-punish first; the player-choice-vs-random fork this cluster's own table entry flagged in advance was resolved by reusing `_get_replacement_slot`'s existing test-queue→AI-choice→deterministic-first-available chain (the same one faint-replacement already uses), NOT Red Card's random pick. Hit Switch Target (Circle Throw family): forces the DEFENDER out, EXCLUDING a Substitute absorption (the opposite scoping from Hit Escape, confirmed via direct source read) — genuine RANDOM replacement via the same Roar/Red-Card machinery, no design fork needed. First Turn Only (Fake Out family): reuses the EXISTING `switched_in_this_turn` flag directly (zero new tracking state) — closes the Instruct-double-fire loophole by adding it to Instruct's own exclusion list. Trick family: bidirectional item swap, a genuinely new 4th direction for the M17j item-transfer family; of source's full unswappable-item list only Multitype's Plate is relevant (everything else — Mail/E-Reader-Berry/Z-Crystals/Booster-Energy-Paradox/Ogerpon-Masks — is permanently moot, items/species never implemented here); Sticky Hold checked only on the target. Revenge family: confirmed the narrow per-(victim,attacker)-PAIR scoping exactly as suspected (genuinely distinct from Lash Out/Retaliate's own D2-tracker shape), verified via a real 2v2 doubles test that a hit from one opponent doesn't double a Revenge aimed at a different one. **Stomping Tantrum family — the highest-yield finding**: tracing its exact decrement site revealed it shares the LITERAL SAME source function as Retaliate's own side-timer (`battle_main.c`'s per-battler action-reset, unconditional every turn) — directly contradicting the already-shipped `[D3 turn-order/event-tracker batch]` Retaliate implementation, which decremented in `_phase_end_of_turn` (a site confirmed via that session's own testing to be SKIPPED on a faint/replacement turn, a project-specific quirk source doesn't share). This meant Retaliate was under-doubling by one full turn boundary after a faint; fixed by moving BOTH timers' decrement to `_phase_priority_resolution` (which runs unconditionally every turn, matching source), with `d3_batch_test.gd`'s own Retaliate assertions rewritten to match the corrected sequence. **A second, independently-discovered bug**, found while writing this tier's own tests (Fake Out failing to connect on ANY turn, including a fresh battle's first one): `switched_in_this_turn` was never set for a battle's own STARTING leads — only the 3 mid-battle switch-in functions ever set it — meaning Stakeout and Speed Boost (its two pre-existing consumers, both shipped in earlier ability tiers) had been silently reading a permanently-false value for every battle's own opening turn since they shipped. Fixed at the root (not a Fake-Out-specific workaround): `_phase_battle_start` sets a new `_pending_initial_switch_in` flag, consumed by `_phase_priority_resolution`'s own per-turn reset to mark turn 1 specifically; verified no regression via `m17a_test`/`ability_test` (Stakeout/Speed Boost's own suites, both clean). New `d1_easy_bundle_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 49/49 assertions across 8 sections, stable across 4 reruns after fixing 4 real test-authoring bugs (a scrapped fragile RNG-choreography design for Stomping Tantrum's own integration test, replaced with a fully deterministic type-immunity failure needing no RNG forcing at all; a fresh 2-site recurrence of the pre-set-state-gets-consumed-before-the-first-turn's-own-check pitfall, discovered independently in both this tier's own Stomping Tantrum tests AND `d3_batch_test.gd`'s pre-existing Retaliate tests once the decrement-site fix was applied; an unreachable pre-set-state scenario for Revenge's own doubles-scope discriminator, rewritten as a genuine 2v2 battle with explicit `queue_move_targeted` calls; a whole-battle-aggregation risk in Hit Escape's own recoil-death discriminator, caught at design time). 23-suite regression clean (`damage_test`/`move_test`/`stat_test`/`status_test`/`switch_test`/`m18j_test`/`m19_bucket4_pairs_test`/`m19_rampage_test`/`m19_recharge_test`/`m17c_test`/`tier4_test`/`item_registry_test`/`m17f_test`/`m17n8_test`/`m17n9_test`/`doubles_test`/`m17a_test`/`ability_test`/`delayed_effect_test`/`m19ef_test`/`m17n10_test`/`m17n1_test`), plus `d3_batch_test` itself corrected and rerun clean (48/48). **Total move count: 604→617.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: all 6 cluster rows marked CLOSED with full findings, D1's own header corrected to just 1 cluster/5 moves remaining (`EFFECT_DOUBLE_POWER_ON_ARG_STATUS` only), Section E's two summary tables and top reconciliation recomputed (617+1+1+213+102=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[D1 easy bundle]` entry with full Step 0 citations and both bug writeups. **Section D's residual: 115→102.**

- **[Multitype-Plate fix] (bugfix to already-shipped M17j/M17n-4/D1-easy-bundle code, NOT new M19 scope): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. A verification-only follow-up to the D1 easy bundle's own Trick/Switcheroo Multitype-Plate exclusion found the fix was scoped narrowly (Trick's own inline dispatch, not a shared gate) while real source's `CanBattlerGetOrLoseItem` is called by far more than Trick — also `CanStealItem` (Pickpocket/Magician/Thief/Covet/Sticky Barb, all via the shared `AbilityManager._try_steal_item`) and `TryTriggerSymbiosis`. Neither `_try_steal_item` nor `try_symbiosis` had this check at all — a real, previously-untested gap (Knock Off/Fling/Bestow confirmed non-issues, not implemented in this project). A second, deeper finding: re-deriving Trick's own condition against source revealed its original 2-check version (`trick_atk_unswappable`/`trick_def_unswappable`) only covered each side losing its own currently-held Plate — real source's `Cmd_tryswapitems` makes 4 `CanBattlerGetOrLoseItem` calls, also blocking a Multitype holder with NO Plate from GAINING a foreign one. New shared `AbilityManager.is_form_locked_by_item(battler, item, ng_active)` (item passed explicitly, not read off `battler.held_item`, since both the "gains foreign" checks and Pickpocket/Symbiosis's receiver-side checks need to test an item the battler doesn't yet hold) now backs Trick's corrected 4-check dispatch, `_try_steal_item` (unconditional, not gated by `bypass_sticky_hold` — confirmed Sticky Barb's own transfer calls the same `CanStealItem`), and `try_symbiosis`. `m17j_test.gd` gained a new Section 10 (12 assertions), `m17n4_test.gd`'s S5.04 was rewritten (its own setup depended on Magician successfully stealing a Multitype holder's Plate, now correctly blocked), `d1_easy_bundle_test.gd` gained E.07-E.10 covering both the original and the deeper case — all three passed clean on the first run (60/60, 44/44, 53/53). 14-suite regression clean. No new moves/abilities/items, zero M19 move-count or Section D changes. See `docs/decisions.md`'s `[Multitype-Plate fix]` entry for full source citations.
- **`EFFECT_DOUBLE_POWER_ON_ARG_STATUS` (the last structured D1 cluster, 5 moves — closes D1 entirely): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. Hex(506)/Venoshock(474)/Smelling Salts(265)/Barb Barrage(767)/Infernal Parade(772), individually re-verified against `moves_info.h` rather than assumed uniform (move IDs also re-derived — Barb Barrage/Infernal Parade are 767/772, not the 838/852 initially assumed). Confirmed genuinely non-uniform: Hex/Infernal Parade double vs ANY non-volatile status; Venoshock/Barb Barrage double vs poison/toxic only; Smelling Salts doubles vs paralysis only. **Three of the five turned out to be two-mechanism composites, not just Smelling Salts as originally flagged**: Barb Barrage/Infernal Parade each ALSO carry a 50%/30% chance to poison/burn the target — pure reuse of the existing generic `secondary_effect`/`SE_POISON`/`SE_BURN` dispatch, zero new code; Smelling Salts ALSO cures the target's paralysis on hit, PLUS carries a genuine second nuance the original flag hadn't anticipated — source's own dispatch (`battle_util.c` L6186-6190) suppresses the power-double ITSELF (not just the cure) if the hit would be blocked by a live, non-ignored Substitute, an asymmetry unique to this one move in the cluster. A real, currently-reachable Comatose interaction confirmed and implemented: source treats a Comatose holder as having STATUS1_SLEEP for this check specifically (`status1 | (STATUS1_SLEEP * isComatose)`), reachable since Comatose already ships (`[M17n-11]`). New `MoveData.is_double_power_on_status`/`double_power_status_arg` (a real status value or one of two new sentinels, `STATUS_ARG_POISON_ANY`/`STATUS_ARG_ANY`, since this project's status field is single-valued not a bitmask)/`is_smelling_salts`; new `BattleManager._status_matches_double_power_arg` static helper; the doubling itself reuses the EXACT existing `_dmg_power_override` pipeline stage Rollout/Magnitude/Stomping Tantrum/Revenge/etc. already occupy — no new mechanism, confirming the D1 table's own prediction. New `d1_double_power_status_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 60/60 assertions, stable across 5 reruns after fixing 3 real test-authoring bugs on the first run (50/57) — a fresh instance of the documented "type immunity precedes ability logic" pitfall (Ghost-type Hex/Infernal Parade tested against a default Normal-type defender, a flat 0× immunity); the actual root cause, more fundamental than the immunity confound: raw `DamageCalculator.calculate()` calls have zero awareness of `_dmg_power_override`, which lives entirely in `BattleManager` — every "doubles vs status" claim needed real full-battle observation instead, matching how every other power-override move is tested elsewhere in this project; and a fresh whole-battle-aggregation instance (a `substitute_hp=50` fixture legitimately broke over a long multi-turn battle, after which a later, unrelated hit correctly cured the paralysis and was misread as the Substitute-exception failing — fixed via `substitute_hp=999999`, the established "effectively unbreakable" precedent). 16-suite regression clean. **Total move count: 617→622.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: the cluster marked CLOSED, D1's own header corrected to **FULLY CLOSED** (all 21 clusters/51 moves), Section E's two summary tables and top reconciliation recomputed (622+1+1+213+97=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[EFFECT_DOUBLE_POWER_ON_ARG_STATUS]` entry with full Step 0 citations; also flags (not fixes) that Section A's own separate Tier-by-Tier table has been stale since `[M19c]`/`[M19d]`, several sessions behind Section E's own up-to-date figures — a pre-existing drift outside this session's own narrow scope. **Section D's residual: 102→97 — D1 is now fully closed, only D4's singleton pool remains.**
