- **[D4 bundle] (Struggle, Helping Hand, Sleep Talk, Taunt, Assurance, Magic Coat — 6 of the D4 recon's 7-move top pick, Nature Power pulled): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. Step 0 independently re-verified all 7 against source rather than trusting the FREE/CHEAP tags, finding real wrinkles on 3. **Struggle confirmed FREE** — the hardcoded `_ready()`-constructed fallback was already fully correct, but source shows it carries nearly every ban flag that exists (meFirst/mimic/metronome/sleepTalk/copycat/instruct/encore/assist/sketch/mirrorMove-banned) — mattered specifically because `_pick_metronome_move()` scans every `.tres` on disk, so a bare data entry would have silently made Struggle Metronome-callable for the first time. **Helping Hand confirmed FREE** (full dispatch — doubles-check, ally-fainted/already-acted fails, signal — already built since `[M14b]`) but a real gap was caught before the first test run: it also needed its own `metronomeBanned`/`copycatBanned`/`assistBanned`/`mirrorMoveBanned` flags, missed on the first data-entry pass. **Nature Power pulled from the bundle**: re-deriving `GetNaturePowerMove()` found the D4 recon's own "reduces to a fixed call" framing was wrong — it falls through to the same `gBattleEnvironment` blocker as Secret Power/Camouflage in the vast majority of cases; deferred alongside them, D4's BLOCKED tier corrected 1→2. **Sleep Talk** confirmed via source (`battle_move_resolution.c` L529-552) that Metronome/Assist/Nature-Power/Sleep-Talk/Copycat/Me-First all share the literal same `calledMove` switch, formalizing the "call-a-different-move" cluster; needed a genuinely new `usable_while_asleep` mechanism (bypasses `pre_move_check`'s sleep block) plus its own explicit "is the attacker actually asleep or Comatose" gate inside the move-picking function itself — NOT implied for free by the `pre_move_check` bypass. **Taunt** confirmed execution-time-checked (a status move already queued this turn IS still blocked if Taunt lands first) with a genuinely conditional duration (4 turns if the target already acted this turn, 3 if not) reusing Helping Hand's own "has this mon acted yet" check. **Assurance** confirmed triggers on "hit by anyone this turn," not "hit by the user" — reuses Revenge's `hit_by_this_turn` directly, zero new state. **Magic Coat** confirmed to share Magic Bounce's exact dispatch chain via direct source read (`battle_move_resolution.c` L5157) — extending the existing swap's condition with an OR inherits its already-proven non-recursive single-bounce guarantee for free; needed its own `BAN_MIRROR_MOVE` flag, the same class of gap as Helping Hand's. New `d4_bundle_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 39/39 assertions, stable across 5 reruns after fixing 3 real test-authoring bugs on the first run (36/39) — two fresh recurrences of "assumed turn order backwards" (Helping Hand's own +5 priority means it always resolves before an ordinary ally move regardless of speed; fixed C.04 by having both allies use Helping Hand instead) and a fresh whole-battle-aggregation instance (Growl/Magic Coat never deal damage, so the test battle runs many turns, each producing a legitimate bounce — fixed by isolating the first action via an ordered timeline). 15-suite regression clean, including `tier4_test` (Metronome's own origin suite, critical since 4 of these 6 moves now enter its pool for the first time). **Total move count: 622→628.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: Nature Power's cluster entry and D4's BLOCKED/CHEAP tier counts corrected, Section E's summary table and top reconciliation recomputed (628+0+0+215+91=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[D4 bundle]` entry with full Step 0 citations and both fixed gaps. **Section D's residual: 97→91.**
- **[D4 CHEAP bundle] (Dream Eater, Torment, Gyro Ball, Electro Ball, Snore, Endure, Fell Stinger, Magnet Rise, Smack Down, Ingrain, Aqua Ring, Payback — 12 moves, the 4 confirmed standouts + 8 additional CHEAP picks): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. Step 0 individually re-verified all 12 against source, finding real corrections on several: Dream Eater's drain reuses the generic `EFFECT_ABSORB`/`EFFECT_DREAM_EATER` `drain_percent` chokepoint (Giga Drain's family), NOT the Volt Absorb/Water Absorb ABILITY family the prompt itself suggested checking, and fails OUTRIGHT (0 damage, confirmed via `BattleScript_DreamEaterSleepCheck`) against a non-sleeping/non-Comatose target, checked before the accuracy roll. Torment is a PERMANENT (never-naturally-expiring) target-side volatile — `Cmd_settorment` sets a plain bool with no timer at all, confirmed distinct from the decoy `tormentTimer`/`Cmd_TrySetTormentSide` path (an unimplemented side-wide variant) — reusing Blood Moon's `cant_use_twice` SHAPE but target- rather than self-inflicted; this project has no Struggle-fallback/menu-legality architecture for ANY execution-time move restriction (Disable/Taunt/Assault Vest/Blood Moon included), so Torment doesn't interact with Struggle specially either, matching that established precedent. Gyro Ball's power is `((25 * target_speed) / user_speed) + 1`, capped at 150, continuous; Electro Ball is CONFIRMED genuinely different — a stepped/banded 5-entry table keyed on the INVERSE ratio (user-to-target), not a mirrored version of Gyro Ball's formula. Snore reuses Sleep Talk's own `usable_while_asleep` mechanism directly (no fail-if-awake gate, unlike Dream Eater — confirmed no dedicated battle script exists for it at all). Endure shares Protect/Detect's `Cmd_setprotectlike` dispatch, but that command itself branches internally to a SEPARATE `endure_active` field, never touching `protect_active` — a real correction to this move's own first-draft plan (reuse `protect_active` with an `_is_protected_from` bypass case), abandoned before any code was written once source was read carefully; the survive-lethal-hit chain checks `endure_active` FIRST, before Sturdy. Fell Stinger raises Attack +3 (not +2) at this project's GEN_LATEST config, mirroring Moxie's own killer-lookup shape via `_last_attacker_move`. Magnet Rise/Smack Down/Ingrain all extend `AbilityManager.is_grounded`'s existing priority-tier ordering (Iron Ball > Smack Down/Ingrain forced-grounded > Magnet Rise/Levitate/Air Balloon ungrounded > Flying-type ungrounded > grounded-default, already confirmed correct in `[M18t]`). **Ingrain's own scope turned out FULLY buildable**, not the partial "flag but don't build the Roar-block" scope originally proposed: self-heal (maxHP/16, shared formula/helper with Aqua Ring, Big-Root-boosted) + self-grounding + BOTH voluntary-switch-block (`AbilityManager.is_trapped`) AND forced-switch-block against Roar/Whirlwind/Circle Throw/Dragon Tail/Red Card (`AbilityManager.blocks_forced_switch`, confirmed from source that Roar's own script checks `VOLATILE_ROOT` directly, `data/battle_scripts_1.s` L1656) — achieved via pure reuse of existing infrastructure once Step 0 found the real cost was lower than expected; confirmed via source that Baton Pass explicitly bypasses this (`SWITCH_IGNORE_ESCAPE_PREVENTION`), matching every other trapping source's already-established exemption. Payback doubles power only if the target already acted this turn AND did NOT just switch in (`B_PAYBACK_SWITCH_BOOST >= GEN_5` at this project's config), reusing `_has_target_already_acted` (`[M18j]`) and `switched_in_this_turn` (`[D1 easy bundle]`) directly. **A real, pre-existing gap was found and fixed as a byproduct of Smack Down/Ingrain's own grounding work**, unrelated to any single move in this bundle: `TypeChart.get_uq412` never had a `grounded_override` parameter at all (unlike `get_effectiveness`, built for Iron Ball in `[M18t]`), meaning `DamageCalculator.calculate`'s own SECOND, independent UQ4.12 damage computation would silently re-immune a Ground-type move against ANY forced-grounded target — Iron Ball holders included, not just this bundle's new moves — even after the FIRST immunity gate already passed it through; fixed by adding the identical parameter/check to `get_uq412` and threading it through both of `calculate`'s own call sites. New `d4_bundle2_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 66/66 assertions, stable across 8 reruns after fixing 4 real test-authoring bugs (a whole-battle-aggregation instance in the Torment discriminator; two missing `queue_move` calls that let auto-select silently re-pick a move's own first slot instead of exercising the intended second move; an exact-equality pairwise-damage assertion that didn't account for integer-division rounding). **A real regression was caught and fixed during this session's own regression sweep, not by the new test suite**: the `is_protect` dispatch's new Endure branch had moved `protect_consecutive`'s increment to AFTER the `protected` signal's emit, changing the order relative to `tier4_test.gd`'s own pre-existing S4.04 (which reads `protect_consecutive` at the moment the signal fires) — fixed by incrementing before the emit in both branches, restoring the original ordering exactly; `tier4_test` confirmed 86/86 stable across reruns after the fix. One additional flaky test was found, root-caused, and confirmed PRE-EXISTING and unrelated via `git stash`: `m19a_gen1_test.gd`'s own "Hydro Pump does NOT trigger Rough Skin" discriminator (a whole-battle-aggregation bug in a much older, untouched test file) reproduces identically with or without this session's changes — flagged, not fixed, out of scope. Regression: the 4 required suites plus 17 suites covering every piece of reused infrastructure, and — given this session's changes touch `DamageCalculator`/`TypeChart`, used by every damaging move in the roster — a full 106-file sweep run twice from independent process states, 0 real failures either time (the one pre-existing flake above excepted). **Total move-implementation count: 628→640.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: the new `[D4 CHEAP bundle]` entry added under D4, D4's own remaining-pool note and Section E's summary table/reconciliation recomputed (640+0+0+215+79=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[D4 CHEAP bundle]` entry with full Step 0 citations. **Section D's residual: 91→79.**
- **[D4 bundle 3] (Splash, Refresh, Purify, Memento, Belly Drum, Fillet Away, Clangorous Soul, Nightmare, Spite, Recycle, Facade, Take Heart — 12 moves, self-selected from Section D's residual): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-10. Step 0 individually re-verified all 12 against source, finding real corrections on several. **Refresh** cures Burn/Poison/Toxic/Paralysis ONLY — confirmed via source's own `STATUS1_CAN_MOVE` bitmask that Sleep/Freeze are explicitly excluded, matching the move's literal flavor text rather than a "cures anything" assumption. **Take Heart** raises Attack + Sp.Atk (source's own data table), NOT Sp.Atk/Sp.Def as general series knowledge would suggest; its own gate is an OR (`WillAnyStatChange() || status1 != 0`), so it still cures status even with both stages already maxed. **Purify** confirmed exactly as proposed: fails outright with no cure attempt if the target has no status; only cures, THEN conditionally self-heals half HP. **Memento**'s stat-drop applies before the self-faint, and only the stat-drop is Substitute-gated — the self-faint is unconditional, since Substitute protects the target, not the attacker's own move-consequence. **Belly Drum/Fillet Away/Clangorous Soul** all hard-fail with ZERO HP cost unless the stat change would genuinely do something AND the HP payment can be made (`WillAnyStatChange() && Try*Hp(...)`, an AND gate — confirmed NOT "always pay, sometimes no boost"), with Clangorous Soul's own divisor (a third of max HP) genuinely different from the other two's half; Belly Drum's own delta is `STAT_CHANGE_FORCE_MAX` (encoded as +12, not a literal "set to +6"), composing correctly with Contrary via the existing generic stage-modifier pipeline for free. **Recycle** restores a NEW, genuinely BROADER `BattlePokemon.last_used_item` field (any item, not just berries) — confirmed distinct from Harvest/Cud Chew's own berry-only `last_consumed_berry` tracker via direct source read of `Cmd_removeitem`/`usedHeldItem`, with an explicit Air-Balloon-pop exclusion mirroring source's own "cannot be restored by any means" carve-out. **Facade**'s burn-halving bypass is confirmed a separate, independent mechanism from Guts', not conditioned on it. **A real, previously-flagged-open bug was resolved**: `[D2 batch 2]`'s own Foresight entry had explicitly flagged "whether any OTHER move shares this gap [a script that never calls `typecalc`] is an open question" — this session found **Purify, Nightmare, and Spite** all share it, confirmed via direct source read; most consequentially for **Nightmare** (Ghost-type), whose own primary use case (an asleep Normal-type target) is the exact Ghost-vs-Normal-immunity shape Foresight's own bug already demonstrated — this project's general type-immunity gate was silently blocking Nightmare against its own most common target before this fix (Memento shares the same gap in principle but is provably unreachable — no type in this project's chart is immune to Dark — so left off the exemption list). Nightmare's own recurring end-of-turn tick re-checks sleep status EVERY turn (not just at application) — waking clears it silently with no damage that turn. New `d4_bundle3_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 56/56 assertions, stable across 9 reruns after fixing 6 real test-authoring bugs, all instances of the same whole-battle-aggregation pitfall recurring across independent tests in one session (Splash's own discriminator colliding with the opponent's unrelated Growl eventually hitting its own "stat_limit" failure on the same battler identity; the HP-cost stat-boost family's own assertions reading `current_hp`/`stat_stages` after the full multi-turn battle instead of snapshotting at the moment of interest, in both the success and discriminator-fail directions; two missing first-occurrence guards on `stat_stage_changed` listeners) plus one real test-DESIGN bug (the Memento-vs-Substitute discriminator wrongly expected the self-faint to also be blocked, contradicting the correct implementation — the test's own expectation was fixed, not the code). Regression: the 4 required suites plus a full 107-file sweep run twice from independent process states (this session touches `_consume_item`, the shared type-immunity gate, and `DamageCalculator`'s burn modifier — all central chokepoints) — 0 real failures either time (the same pre-existing `m19a_gen1_test` flake from the prior session reproduces identically, reconfirmed unrelated). **Total move-implementation count: 640→652.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: new `[D4 bundle 3]` subsection added under D4, Section E's summary table/reconciliation recomputed (652+0+0+215+67=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[D4 bundle 3]` entry with full Step 0 citations. **Section D's residual: 79→67.**
- **[D4 Bundle 4] (Tailwind, Sticky Web, Safeguard, Mist, Copycat, Me First, Assist, Heal Pulse, Life Dew, Stockpile, Spit Up, Swallow — 12 moves, 4 clusters): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-13. Assistant-proposed bundle, confirmed by Rob before Step 0. **Cluster 1 (side-condition timers)**: Tailwind/Sticky Web/Safeguard/Mist all set a per-side `_side_conditions` timer, but are NOT one shared mechanism. Tailwind's own actual ×2 Speed doubling had never been wired by the original proposal — added a new `tailwind_active` param to `StatusManager.effective_speed`, threaded into turn-order sort + Gyro Ball/Electro Ball. Sticky Web's own -1 Speed switch-in effect (confirmed via source, `battle_stat_change.c` L481-491) dispatches through the FULL generic stat-change pipeline — NOT a raw hazard tick like Spikes/Toxic Spikes/Stealth Rock — so Defiant/Competitive/Mirror Armor/Opportunist/Mirror Herb all react to it; `_apply_one_stat_change_pair` extended to return `int` (was void) and called directly from `_apply_switch_in_hazards` via a throwaway `MoveData`, with a new `sticky_web_setter` side-condition key for Mirror-Armor/Defiant attribution. Safeguard blocks non-volatile status AND confusion via a new `safeguard_active` param threaded through `try_apply_status`/`try_apply_confusion`/`try_secondary_effect` (the one chokepoint essentially all move-based status infliction already routes through), bypassed only by an opposing Infiltrator holder (a self-inflicted status is still blocked, matching source's own ally-check-short-circuits-first ordering). Mist blocks a stat DECREASE, added inside `_apply_one_stat_change_pair` checked on the post-Contrary sign BEFORE Mirror Armor/the ability-block chain, matching source's own `CanDecreaseStat` ordering — also Infiltrator-bypassed; `AbilityManager.bypasses_infiltrator_barriers`'s own doc comment had explicitly anticipated this exact addition since `[M17n-9]`. **Cluster 2 (call-a-different-move family)**: Copycat/Me First/Assist confirmed to share the exact same `CancelerCallSubmove` chokepoint Mirror Move/Metronome/Sleep Talk already use. Me First — the bundle's own flagged HIGH-SCRUTINY item — resolved in the good direction: needs NO turn-order pre-emption at all, just a passive "has the target already acted" check reusing the existing `_has_target_already_acted` (Zoom Lens/Upper Hand); its ×1.5 power boost is a flat multiplier at the same pipeline stage as Helping Hand. Copycat needed genuinely NEW state, `_last_landed_move_anyone` (distinct from the existing per-mon `last_move_used`, which is set on nearly every dispatch path regardless of hit/miss) — updated at the same `damage > 0` gate Rapid Spin/Air Balloon use; a disclosed simplification: only ordinary damaging hits update it, since this project has no chokepoint every status-move effect passes through. Assist scans the user's own bench, excluding `assistBanned` moves. All three reuse the pre-existing but previously-dormant `BAN_COPYCAT`/`BAN_ME_FIRST`/`BAN_ASSIST` bitmask constants. **Cluster 3 (target-heal variants)**: Heal Pulse heals the TARGET (not the user) 50%, or 75% if the attacker holds Mega Launcher AND the move is `pulse_move` — a hardcoded special case inside the heal calc itself, not the generic pulse-move damage multiplier. Life Dew heals the user AND ally (if present) 25% each independently, failing only if neither has anything to heal. **Cluster 4 (Stockpile family)** — the interaction-bug-risk check paid off with two real forks: `stockpile_count` (the scaling counter, always increments) and `stockpile_def_added`/`stockpile_spdef_added` (only the ACTUAL stat rise, 0 if capped or Contrary-inverted) are genuinely SEPARATE trackers, confirmed via source (`st->stage > 0` gate); and the stack-consume-and-boost-removal fires even when Spit Up/Swallow's own script "fails" (`MoveEndMoveBlock` is gated only on the move being attempted). A real dispatch-ORDER bug was caught by this bundle's own first test run: Spit Up's `power=1` placeholder (real power = `100 * stockpile_count`) was originally dispatched AFTER the generic `move.power > 0` branch, which silently claimed it first and dealt a flat power=1 hit — fixed by moving Stockpile/Spit Up/Swallow's dispatch earlier, alongside OHKO/Counter/Mirror Coat/Metal Burst (the same "real nonzero placeholder power" class). Both required discriminators resolved cleanly: Me First calling Metronome/Sleep Talk is genuinely IMPOSSIBLE (both are `category == STAT`, excluded by Me First's own category gate before reassignment is ever reached — closing the flagged Step 0 edge case); a Contrary-holding Pokémon using Stockpile has Def/SpDef LOWERED with `stockpile_count` still incrementing but `stockpile_def_added`/`stockpile_spdef_added` staying at 0. Populated `BAN_COPYCAT`/`BAN_ME_FIRST`/`BAN_ASSIST` across 22 already-implemented moves needing them per source (9 of 31 candidates — Struggle/Sleep Talk/Helping Hand/Feint/Shadow Force/Phantom Force/Follow Me/Rage Powder/Thief/Covet — already had them correctly from earlier tiers). New `d4_bundle4_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 89/89 assertions, stable across 5 reruns after fixing 6 real test-authoring bugs on the first run (80/90) — 4 fresh whole-battle-aggregation instances (Stockpile/Contrary-Stockpile/Spit-Up-release/Life-Dew-heal all read state post-battle instead of snapshotting via signal at the first occurrence), an unguarded "did move_called ever fire" check that incorrectly caught a later Struggle fallback once Me First's own PP ran out, a speed-value tuning bug, and a shared-cached-Resource-mutation bug (a Mist unit test mutated Growl directly instead of via `.duplicate()`). Regression: given how many central chokepoints this bundle touches, ran the FULL `scripts/count_assertions.sh` sweep (108 files) twice from independent process states — **11407 total assertions, 0 failures, identical GRAND TOTAL both runs**. **Total move-implementation count: 652→664.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: new `[D4 Bundle 4]` subsection added under D4, Section E's summary table/reconciliation recomputed (664+0+0+215+55=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[D4 Bundle 4]` entry with full Step 0 citations. **Section D's residual: 67→55.**
- **[D4 Bundle 5] (Mud Sport, Water Sport, Weather Ball, Reflect Type, Roost, Strength Sap, Steel Beam, Chloroblast, Charge, Laser Focus, Topsy-Turvy, Autotomize, Fury Cutter — 13 moves, 7 clusters): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14. Assistant-proposed bundle, confirmed by Rob before Step 0; Autotomize explicitly SCOPE-LIMITED by Rob to just its +2 Speed half (the weight-reduction half was never attempted). **Cluster 1 (field-wide side conditions)**: Mud Sport/Water Sport confirmed genuinely FIELD-WIDE (`.target = TARGET_FIELD`), not per-side like Tailwind/Safeguard/Mist — two standalone `_mud_sport_turns`/`_water_sport_turns` battle-wide ints, mirroring `_echoed_voice_counter`'s own shape. Damage reduction is **x0.33, not x0.5** (the pre-Gen-5 value) at this project's config, computed precisely via `fpmath.h`'s own rounding macro (`UQ_4_12(0.33) = 1352`, not a naive truncation to 1351). **Cluster 2 (type-mutation family)**: Weather Ball bundles a type mutation (Sun→Fire/Rain→Water/Sandstorm→Rock/Hail→Ice) AND a SEPARATE x2 power multiplier under one effect ID — two independent hookups in `DamageCalculator.calculate`, not one shared function; gained a matching `is_weather_ball` exclusion in `AbilityManager.effective_move_type` (same shape Hidden Power already uses). Reflect Type needed a genuinely NEW `_set_mon_type_array` sibling function — `_set_mon_type` (backing Conversion/Conversion 2/Protean/Libero/Multitype/Forecast) always forces mono-type and can't represent a dual-type copy; excludes a Multitype-holding target via an ABILITY-keyed check (not species-keyed like source — this project has no species-check pattern anywhere, and Multitype is itself ability+Plate-based); exempted from the general type-immunity gate since its own script never calls `typecalc` (same precedent as Foresight/Purify/Nightmare/Spite). **Cluster 3 (heal-and-drain family)**: Roost's type removal is a query-time overlay in real source (no funneled type-getter exists in this project), so it instead mutates-and-restores via a NEW end-of-turn trigger, snapshotting the EXACT pre-mutation state (`roost_pre_types`, not `original_types`, so an already-Converted mon restores correctly) — a mono-Flying user becomes pure Normal (not typeless) at this project's config. Strength Sap's heal and stat-lower are NOT independent — if the target's Attack is already at -6, NEITHER happens. **Cluster 4 (HP-cost-attached-to-damage family)** — the "same family" framing hid a real divergence: Steel Beam applies ceil(maxHP/2) self-recoil UNCONDITIONALLY (hit, miss, OR Protect-blocked), Magic-Guard-only, via a new `_apply_max_hp_50_recoil` helper called from 3 separate dispatch sites; Chloroblast shares the identical formula but requires a CONNECTING hit and is blocked by BOTH Rock Head and Magic Guard, reusing the existing ordinary-recoil gate. **Cluster 5 (persistent-flag family)**: Charge's `charged` flag is consumed only by a genuinely LATER Electric-type move, per the ACTUAL executable source — its own inline comment claims "regardless of typing," directly contradicting its own code; the comment is deliberately not trusted, preserved via an explanatory code comment so a future session doesn't "fix" it backward. Laser Focus is a flat, UNCONDITIONAL 2-turn guaranteed-crit window (not consumed by use), reusing the SAME `merciless_guaranteed`-shaped pre-check in `DamageCalculator`; found the pre-existing `MoveData.always_critical_hit` field is completely DORMANT (zero consumers anywhere — Storm Throw/Frost Breath/Zippy Zap actually use `critical_hit_stage=3` instead), flagged not fixed. **Cluster 6 (stat-array manipulation)**: Topsy-Turvy inverts stage SIGN (not reset-to-0 like Haze), failing only if all 7 stats are neutral. Autotomize ships ONLY the +2 Speed self-raise (pure generic-dispatch reuse) — the weight-reduction half needs a new mutable per-instance weight field this project doesn't have, and would require editing the already-shipped Low Kick/Grass Knot/Heavy Slam/Heat Crash formulas, both out of scope. **Cluster 7 (escalating power)**: Fury Cutter's counter caps at 5 then WRAPS to 0 on the next successful use (not plateaus), confirmed via a 7-use test reading the counter at each hit (0,1,2,3,4,5,0). **A real production bug was found and fixed mid-session**: Charge's own consumption-clearing was originally placed BEFORE the damage-dispatch branch, meaning the very Electric-type move meant to consume the flag would read it as already-cleared and never get its own boost — fixed by moving the clear to the shared post-dispatch tail, after `_do_damaging_hit` has already read it. New `d4_bundle5_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 85/85 assertions, stable across 5 reruns after fixing 8 real test-authoring bugs on the first run (75/85) — a dual-type-mon construction bug (reassigning `species.types` post-construction doesn't stick, since every switch-in restores from `original_types` captured at construction time — fixed with a new `_make_dual_type_mon` helper), 3 Conversion/Protean/Multitype regression tests with a wrong expected mono-type length (missed `_set_mon_type`'s own `[X, TYPE_NONE]` padding convention), 2 fresh whole-battle-aggregation recurrences (Steel-Beam/Chloroblast ability-block tests incorrectly caught an unrelated later Struggle-fallback recoil; Topsy-Turvy's post-battle stage read was turn-parity-dependent since the mon keeps re-inverting every turn), a speed-tie bug in the Strength Sap tests, and 2 signal-ordering snapshot bugs matching the same root cause as the production bug above (`move_executed` fires before the post-dispatch state settles). Regression: given how many central chokepoints this bundle touches (`DamageCalculator.calculate`'s signature, `AbilityManager.effective_move_type`, several shared `BattleManager` dispatch chokepoints), ran the FULL `scripts/count_assertions.sh` sweep (109 files) twice from independent process states — **11492 total assertions, 0 failures, identical GRAND TOTAL both runs**; special attention paid to `m19_pre1_test.tscn` (Low Kick/Grass Knot/Heavy Slam/Heat Crash/Return/Frustration) given Autotomize's scope-limitation claim — confirmed unchanged at 48/48. **Total move-implementation count: 664→677.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout: new `[D4 Bundle 5]` subsection added under D4, Section E's summary table/reconciliation recomputed (677+0+0+215+42=934, reconfirmed). `docs/decisions.md` new `[D4 Bundle 5]` entry with full Step 0 citations. **Section D's residual: 55→42.**
- **[D4 Bundle 6] (Teleport, Rest, False Swipe, Present, Knock Off, Endeavor, Brine, Acupressure, Psycho Shift, Punishment, Telekinesis, Acrobatics, Bulldoze, Belch, Parting Shot, Venom Drench, Geomancy, Toxic Thread, Stuff Cheeks, No Retreat, Octolock, Poltergeist, Chilly Reception — 23 moves, all REUSE-LIKELY from the preceding verification pass): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14. Step 0 re-derived all 23 fresh from source rather than trusting the recon's own infra-reuse claims, per explicit instruction — 8 real forks confirmed load-bearing. **Octolock does NOT actually trap** in this reference source (`CanBattlerEscape` never checks its volatile) — implemented faithfully as stat-lower-only, deliberately NOT wired into `is_trapped`. **No Retreat's self-trap needed its own dedicated bool** (`no_retreat_active`), not a reuse of `escape_prevented_by` — that field's reciprocal-clear-when-the-source-leaves shape is wrong for a self-inflicted trap. **Telekinesis is two independent halves**: ungrounding (a clean peer addition to `is_grounded`'s existing tier) and a separate guaranteed-hit mechanic (bypasses accuracy except for OHKO moves and while semi-invulnerable, inserted AFTER the semi-invulnerable gate — the opposite ordering from Lock-On). **Parting Shot's switch is GATED ON the stat-lower landing** (Gen7+) — the OPPOSITE of Memento's independence; **Chilly Reception's switch is UNCONDITIONAL** regardless of the weather-set's own success — the opposite gating from Parting Shot despite both being "effect then switch" moves. **Toxic Thread/Venom Drench both needed a type-immunity-gate exemption** (their shared `BattleScript_EffectStatChange` never calls `typecalc`, confirmed via source's own test suite) — flagged, not fixed, that this may be a pre-existing gap for other already-shipped stat-change moves (Growl/Leer/etc.) too. **Knock Off's power boost and removal share one new `AbilityManager.can_remove_item` gate** (Sticky Hold + form-lock, reusing `[M17j]`/`[Multitype-Plate fix]`'s existing checks) — deliberately does NOT route through `_consume_item` (Knock Off never triggers Cheek Pouch or `last_consumed_berry`, since the item is knocked away, not eaten). **Present is a flat 0-255 uniform roll** (102/76/26/51 bands → 40/80/120/heal), confirmed NOT Magnitude's weighted-table shape. - **[D4 Bundle 9] (Flying Press, Sky Drop — the LAST 2 of D4's 6 confirmed NOVEL-MECHANISM moves): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14. Report-only Step 0 requested first ("DO NOT IMPLEMENT YET"), re-deriving both moves fresh from source rather than trusting the prior recon's own complexity estimate; findings reported, then Rob made 3 explicit decisions and authorized implementation in the same session. **Flying Press(560)**: `EFFECT_TWO_TYPED_MOVE` runs TWO independent type-effectiveness computations (Fighting vs. defender, Flying vs. defender, each already correctly combining a dual-typed defender's own two types) multiplied together — every existing type-override (Scrappy/Iron-Ball/Delta-Stream/Freeze-Dry) applies to BOTH components independently, confirmed via source since the underlying function is the FULL modifier pipeline, not a bare lookup. **Real surprising finding, correctly NOT ported**: source's own `ctx->moveType` is a single mutable field left at Flying by the type-effectiveness pass, so the literal current C code grants STAB for Flying-type attackers — but the dev team's own unimplemented test placeholder names the OPPOSITE as intended ("Flying-type Pokémon don't receive STAB on Flying Press"); Rob's decision: port the documented intended behavior (Fighting-only STAB), which falls out for free from this project's own pre-existing STAB code (never mutates `move.type`, unlike source's shared `ctx`). **Sky Drop(507)**: confirmed BOTH combatants become semi-invulnerable during the charge (a real finding beyond the recon's target-only framing) via `HandleSkyDropResult`; the target's own action is skipped every held turn via the EARLIEST canceler in the whole chain (before sleep/freeze even); the anti-air bypass shares Fly's exact `STATE_ON_AIR` rule, zero new logic needed. **Re-verified and corrected the task's own premise**: no Flying-type-target restriction exists anywhere in this reference source (checked in full) — only ally/already-semi-invulnerable/Substitute/weight-≥200kg hard fails. **Found the attacker-faints-while-holding case is NOT auto-handled** by the generic `CancelMultiTurnMoves` (which explicitly PROTECTS the target's own state from being cleared that way) — the real release lives in a dedicated battle-script command, `Cmd_tryconfusionafterskydrop`; Rob's decision: build this for real (reciprocal release + conditional confuse-on-drop), judged a genuine player-facing bug risk if skipped. **Found and precisely characterized a freeze/paralysis asymmetry in source itself**: paralysis explicitly cancels a 2-turn move's charge via `CancelMultiTurnMoves`, but freeze does not; for Sky Drop specifically this leaves the TARGET stuck forever in source (a latent engine gap, flagged not fixed) since `CancelMultiTurnMoves` only touches the one battler passed in. Rob's decision: do NOT build bespoke handling for this — verify and document whichever behavior this project's own pre-move-check ordering naturally produces. Verified via a direct unit-level call: this project's `StatusManager.pre_move_check` never touches `charging_move`/`semi_invulnerable` on ANY failure path, so the natural (and correctly undisturbed) behavior is uniformly "stuck an extra turn" for every pre-move-check failure reason, not just freeze — a real, disclosed divergence from source's own asymmetric behavior, documented rather than silently ported. New `MoveData.two_typed_move`/`second_type` fields; new `DamageCalculator._type_mod_for_attacking_type` extracted from the pre-existing inline UQ4.12 block (behavior-preserving for every other move), called twice and multiplied for Flying Press; confirmed via `Resource.duplicate()`'s default field-copying behavior that the Normalize/Pixilate type-mutation pipeline correctly preserves `second_type` across the duplication, matching the dev team's own Normalize+Flying-Press test-name expectation with zero dedicated code. New `MoveData.is_sky_drop` flag; two new semi-invulnerable state constants routed through the existing bypass-check helper; new `BattlePokemon.sky_drop_target` (source-side reciprocal reference, mirroring `sure_hit_target`'s direction) and `confuse_after_drop`; a dedicated two-phase dispatch block (not the generic two-turn block); a new early check in `_phase_pre_move_checks` for the held-target's-own-action-skipped case; a new reciprocal-release scan in `_clear_volatiles` (the seventh move-based volatile using this shape, in the source-not-victim direction) implementing Rob's decision 2 directly. - **[Charge-cancellation fix] (bugfix, not a move-shipping tier — corrects `[D4 Bundle 9]`'s own "uniformly stuck an extra turn" framing): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14, same day. A dedicated recon first enumerated every `pre_move_check`/`_phase_pre_move_checks` fail branch this project implements (Recharge/Sleep/Freeze/Truant/Flinch/Confusion-self-hit/Paralysis/Infatuation, plus Sky Drop's own target-held check) and checked each independently against source's real canceler chain — all 9 sit well before `CANCELER_CHARGING`, so nothing to fix there, but 4 of them (`CancelerTruant`/`CancelerFlinch`/`CancelerParalyzed`/`CancelerInfatuation`) call `CancelMultiTurnMoves(battlerAtk)` in source, canceling an in-progress charge outright, while Sleep/Frozen/Confusion's own cancelers never do — this project previously never cleared `charging_move`/`semi_invulnerable` on ANY of the 8, correct for 3 but wrong for 4. A follow-up trace then confirmed (not assumed) that reproducing source's version for Sky Drop specifically — cancel the attacker, leave the target orphaned — is a genuine, non-self-healing SOFT-LOCK in the reference engine: the attacker isn't forced to reselect Sky Drop under free move selection once `multipleTurns` clears; a fresh attempt against the same orphaned target just fails via `HandleSkyDropResult`'s own "first turn" branch without releasing it; no other code path anywhere in the source tree clears a stray `STATE_SKY_DROP_TARGET`; and the target can't even switch out on its own (`CanBattlerEscape` explicitly blocks it, the same gate Shadow Tag/Arena Trap use). A further check (don't assume symmetry) confirmed `HandleSkyDropResult`'s own NORMAL release branch never checks `confuseAfterDrop` either — that flag is consumed only by the attacker-faint-specific `Cmd_tryconfusionafterskydrop` — so this project's fix deliberately does NOT apply confuse-after-drop from the new release path, matching source's real scope rather than the faint case's shape. Implementation: new `BattleManager._cancel_charge_if_needed(actor, reason)`, called from `_phase_pre_move_checks` right after `reason` is computed — a plain 2-field clear for ordinary two-turn moves, plus (for Sky Drop, discriminated via `sky_drop_target != null`) a call to a new shared `_release_sky_drop_target(mon, apply_confuse_after_drop)` extracted from `_clear_volatiles`' own pre-existing reciprocal-release block (now just `_release_sky_drop_target(mon, true)`, behavior-preserving), with the new pre-move-check call site passing `false`. Extracted into its own named function specifically so it's directly unit-testable without needing new RNG-forcing seams for the paralysis/infatuation rolls (`_phase_pre_move_checks` has none, unlike the `_force_roll`/`_force_crit`-style seams used elsewhere). `two_turn_test.gd` gained a new T7 section (Truant/Flinch/Paralysis/Infatuation cancel a Fly user's charge; Sleep/Frozen/Confusion negative controls; one full end-to-end check through the real `_phase_pre_move_checks()` dispatch) — 32→46 assertions. `d4_bundle9_test.gd`'s old C.11 series (which asserted the now-superseded "nothing clears" behavior as the expected/passing result) was replaced, not left contradictory: new C.11-C.14 confirm all 4 conditions clear the attacker AND release the held target for Sky Drop specifically; C.15-C.17 are the same 3 negative controls; C.18 confirms confuse-after-drop is deliberately NOT consumed even when the target was mid-rampage when grabbed; C.19 is the same end-to-end wiring check adapted for Sky Drop — 53→77 assertions. Full regression: `scripts/count_assertions.sh` run twice from independent process states — **114 files, GRAND TOTAL 11767, 0 failures both runs** (11729 prior + 38 new). One process-hygiene note: the second sweep attempt initially failed with an empty log, root-caused to the persistent shell's cwd having drifted to the outer `/home/rob/GodotAsImagined` during this session's earlier source investigation — the exact directory-drift pitfall this file's own "never `cd` into the reference checkout" rule warns about; fixed by `cd`-ing to the project root in the same invocation, and the corrected rerun matches the original first sweep exactly. - **[Ability-reset fix] (bugfix to already-shipped code — `[M17h]` 2026-07-03, `[D2 batch]` 2026-07-09 — not new scope): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14, same day. Found while answering a follow-up question during the Mimic/Sketch/Transform/Perish Song Step 0 recon: source's `SwitchInClearSetData` unconditionally re-derives `.ability` from species on every switch-in, but this project's own `_reset_mon_type` (called at every switch-in site) only ever reset `species.types` — `.ability` was never reset anywhere except the one Primal-Reversion switch-in trigger (M18w). This meant Trace/Mummy/Wandering Spirit/Lingering Aroma/Skill Swap/Role Play's ability overwrites persisted PERMANENTLY across switch-outs. **A real architectural gap found at Step 0**: source re-derives ability from `species` + a per-instance `abilityNum` (which of 3 possible slots was rolled) — this project has no equivalent field at all (`ability` defaults to `null` at construction; every test/setup path assigns it externally, exactly once). New `BattlePokemon.ability` setter captures a new `original_ability` field on the FIRST assignment only (considered and rejected capturing lazily at first switch-in instead — confirmed `_phase_battle_start`'s starting-leads loop doesn't go through `_do_switch_in` at all, so that approach would silently miss starting leads; a setter sidesteps this entirely). New `BattleManager._reset_mon_ability(mon)`, a sibling to `_reset_mon_type` (not folded into it — that function's own name/scope is specifically about type), called at the same 5 switch-in sites. Confirmed M18w's Primal Reversion ordering is unaffected (its own ability-set runs inside `_apply_switch_in_abilities`, AFTER the reset, so it correctly re-applies on top every time — verified with a dedicated test, not assumed from the two functions' names). Confirmed neither `m17h_test.gd` nor `d2_batch_test.gd` (the two origin suites) has any switch-out-and-back-in test for any of these 6 abilities/moves — both reran unchanged (64/64, 82/82), nothing was asserting the old buggy behavior. New `scenes/battle/ability_reset_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 34/34 assertions across 7 sections (setter/capture unit tests; Trace reverting AND immediately re-tracing on the same switch-in, proving the reset runs before switch-in abilities re-apply; Mummy/Lingering Aroma/Wandering Spirit/Skill Swap/Role Play all reverting correctly, including both-sides-independently for the two bidirectional swaps; the Primal Reversion ordering confirmation), stable on the first run. See `[Mimic/Sketch]`'s own entry below for the shared regression sweep (both bugfix tasks landed in the same session). `docs/decisions.md` new `[Ability-reset fix]` entry with full citations.
- **[Mimic/Sketch] (Mimic(102), Sketch(166) — 2 of D4's 4 remaining confirmed NOVEL-MECHANISM moves; Transform/Perish Song remain, per the Step 0 recon's own recommendation to give Transform its own dedicated session): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14, same day. Both copy the target's last-used move, reusing this project's existing `BattlePokemon.last_move_used` directly (confirmed equivalent to source's `gLastMoves`/`gLastPrintedMoves` for every scenario this project can produce — no Dancer ability, no Baton-Pass/Healing-Wish re-attribution chains). **A real, smaller-than-expected ban-flag gap**: `MoveData.BAN_MIMIC`/`BAN_SKETCH` already existed as dormant bitmask constants (same class as `TARGET_ALL_BATTLERS`/`ItemData.pocket` before their own fixes), and `BAN_MIMIC` was already correctly populated on 6 of 8 expected moves — only Metronome(118) and Mirror Move(119) were missing it, now fixed; Transform(144) isn't implemented yet, so its own flag is deferred with a citation rather than silently dropped. **A real asymmetry caught while writing tests, not assumed**: Sleep Talk is `mimicBanned` but NOT `sketchBanned` in source (the real `sketchBanned` list is just Struggle/Sketch itself/Chatter) — caught by a test failure, fixed by switching the discriminator move and adding a permanent regression-guard assertion for the asymmetry itself. **Mimic**: overwrites its OWN move slot temporarily, PP capped at `min(copied.pp, 5)`; new `BattlePokemon.mimicked_slot`/`mimicked_original_move`/`mimicked_original_pp` (the last one confirmed via tracing this project's own PP-deduction code to be Mimic's own PP AFTER its own normal 1-PP-per-use deduction — 9, not full 10 — matching source's real behavior); new `BattleManager._reset_mon_mimicked_move(mon)`, a third sibling alongside `_reset_mon_type`/`_reset_mon_ability`, called at the same 5 switch-in sites (matching source's switch-IN-time restoration, not a switch-out one — this project has no separate party-record layer to fall back on, so an explicit snapshot/restore was needed). **Sketch**: same dispatch shape but full real PP (no cap), permanent (no restoration mechanism exists at all — confirmed by running the real switch-in reset functions and showing nothing changes), and its own "already known" check explicitly skips comparing against OTHER Sketch-flagged slots (confirmed from source, not assumed symmetric with Mimic). Both dispatch blocks reuse `_phase_move_execution`'s existing "ability/moveset-mutation cluster" (right after Role Play/Skill Swap/Worry Seed/Heart Swap) — same upstream foe-targeting/Substitute/type-immunity/Prankster gates, no new gating needed. New `BattleManager.move_learned(pokemon, slot, new_move)` signal. New `scenes/battle/mimic_sketch_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 46/46 assertions across 4 sections (data integrity incl. both ban-flag fixes and the Sleep-Talk/Struggle asymmetry lock-in; Mimic's successful copy/PP-cap/already-known-fail/BAN_MIMIC-fail/switch-in restoration; Sketch's successful copy/full-PP/already-known-fail/BAN_SKETCH-fail/own-slot-exclusion/permanence; a Tackle negative control), stable across 3 reruns. **A real test-authoring bug caught and fixed on the first run (37/43)**: every PP-value check run through a full `start_battle_with_parties` battle failed — the battle keeps running turns after the point of interest, auto-selecting the newly-copied move and consuming its PP further, the exact whole-battle-aggregation pitfall this file's own testing-conventions section documents. Fixed by switching every state-inspecting sub-test to a single deterministic `_phase_move_execution()` call on a manually-constructed `BattleManager` (the same pattern `[D4 Bundle 9]`'s own C.10/C.11 tests already established), and by setting `last_move_used` directly on the fixture rather than orchestrating a preceding real move-use turn. Full regression (both this task and `[Ability-reset fix]` landed in the same session — run together as one full sweep): `scripts/count_assertions.sh` run twice from independent process states — **116 files, GRAND TOTAL 11847, 0 failures both runs** (11767 prior + 34 `ability_reset_test` + 46 `mimic_sketch_test`). A worse-than-usual recurrence of this session's own directory-drift pitfall (4 consecutive sweep-dispatch failures, including one exit-127 even with a bare `pwd` prefix) before a `cd`-prefixed, no-`pwd` invocation finally succeeded — see `docs/decisions.md`'s own entry for the full blow-by-blow; the standing rule going forward is to put `cd` as the literal first token of any background Godot-sweep command, not just a reactive fix. **Total move-implementation count: 713→715.** `docs/move_status_table.md` regenerated and confirmed: **715 implemented / 217 excluded / 2 residual / 16 needs-manual-review** (unchanged review count — `is_mimic`/`is_sketch` are `is_*`-prefixed booleans, already covered by the generator's own generic pattern). **Section D's residual: 4→2 — only Transform(144)/Perish Song(195) remain.** `docs/decisions.md` new `[Mimic/Sketch]` entry with full Step 0 citations.

- **[Sweep-dispatch fix] (tooling — root-caused and fixed the recurring regression-sweep cwd-drift failure hit across `[Charge-cancellation fix]`/`[Mimic/Sketch]` and earlier sessions, properly this time): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14. Every prior session diagnosed this fresh and worked around it ad hoc ("root cause not fully identified"). **The real mechanism, confirmed directly**: the true git repo root this environment enforces is `/home/rob/GodotAsImagined` — ONE LEVEL ABOVE this project's own directory (`as-imagined`). Deliberately ran `cd /tmp` as a diagnostic: the shell did NOT move there — the environment silently reset the cwd to `/home/rob/GodotAsImagined` instead. Any `cd` at any point in a session targeting a path outside that boundary — not just the already-documented `reference/pokeemerald_expansion` case — lands the shell one level too high, silently, and every subsequent relative-path command (including `bash scripts/count_assertions.sh`) then fails to resolve; this happens BEFORE the script's own code ever runs, so no internal fix inside the script could ever have addressed it. Fixed `scripts/count_assertions.sh` itself to `cd` to its own project root unconditionally at the very top (was previously nested inside one branch) — real hardening, but not the fix for the relative-path-resolution failure itself. **The actual fix, now a dedicated standing-rule section in CLAUDE.md** (not just narrative here): always invoke the sweep via its full absolute path in the same command string — `bash /home/rob/GodotAsImagined/as-imagined/scripts/count_assertions.sh` — never a bare relative path, and never relying on a `cd` from a separate prior command (a `cd`-prefixed-then-relative invocation was explicitly NOT adopted as the primary rule, since it has also been observed to fail in this environment). Verified by deliberately reproducing the drift (`cd /tmp`, confirmed the reset) then dispatching a sweep using ONLY the hardened invocation with no manual `cd` — succeeded on the first attempt, matching the exact prior baseline (116 files/11847/0 failures). **One honest caveat**: a separate, still-unexplained transient sweep-dispatch failure (empty log, exit 1, no directory issue, immediate success on a bare retry) still occurred once during this same session's `[Perish Song]` sweeps, using the hardened invocation — flagged explicitly as a distinct, still-open flakiness class, not folded into "fixed." `docs/decisions.md` new `[Sweep-dispatch fix]` entry with the full diagnostic trail.
- **[Perish Song] (Perish Song(195) — the last of D4's residual pool cheap enough to ship without its own dedicated session; Transform remains, per the recon's own recommendation): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14, same day. The FIRST move in this project needing genuine ALL-BATTLERS dispatch — `MoveData.TARGET_ALL_BATTLERS` (value 14) existed as a dormant constant, read only by `AbilityManager.pressure_pp_cost`, until this move actually set `.target` to it (needed adding `target` to `gen_moves.py`'s `DEFAULTS`/`FIELD_ORDER` for the first time ever — confirmed via grep that no move entry had ever set it before). Cast loops over every currently-active combatant, both sides, INCLUDING the caster itself, setting a 3-turn countdown on each one not already counting down and not excluded. **Per-target exclusions confirmed precisely from source, not assumed**: already counting down; Soundproof (`.soundMove = TRUE`, reuses the existing `blocks_move_flag` gate); Prankster-boosted-and-Dark-type-blocked (reuses `blocks_prankster_move`, checked per-target). Traced `IsBattlerUnaffectedByMove`'s literal definition and its only 2 set-sites in the whole reference tree — both are conditions specific to a SINGLE-target damage-resolution pipeline Perish Song's own dispatch (a dedicated Cmd with no `accuracycheck`/Substitute-check of its own) never reaches — concluded this check is effectively always-false for this move and correctly NOT modeled; Commander is moot (no such mechanic exists here). Fails outright ONLY if every single combatant was excluded (source: `notAffectedCount == gBattlersCount`), confirmed exact, not simplified. **End-of-turn timer**: checked BEFORE decrementing (matching source's exact off-by-one shape) — 3 count-down-only ticks (3→2→1→0) then a 4th tick (timer already 0) deals the fatal blow, a direct HP-zero matching Self-Destruct/Explosion's existing shape, confirming the move's own "faints in 3 [full] turns" flavor text precisely. **A real implementation bug found and fixed via this move's own first test run**: a PRE-EXISTING, generic single-`defender`-shaped Soundproof/Bulletproof gate already in `_phase_move_execution` (built correctly for ordinary sound moves like Growl/Roar/Whirlwind, where one defender's immunity correctly blocks the whole move) was incorrectly blocking Perish Song's ENTIRE cast whenever the arbitrary default target happened to hold Soundproof — fixed by exempting `move.is_perish_song` from that generic gate explicitly, deferring Soundproof handling entirely to Perish Song's own correctly-shaped per-combatant loop; confirmed no regression to that gate's own origin suite (`m17n1_test.tscn` 82/82 unchanged). New `MoveData.is_perish_song` flag; new `BattlePokemon.perish_song_active`/`perish_song_timer` fields; cast dispatch placed in the established Haze/field-wide-move neighborhood; end-of-turn tick added to the EXISTING per-mon decrement loop (Disable/Encore/Throat Chop/Taunt/Yawn's own loop) rather than a new one; new `BattleManager.perish_song_activated(pokemon)` signal. **PERISH BODY flagged, not resolved**: the new fields are exactly what its own contact-reactive mechanism would reuse, confirmed mechanically trivial — left excluded per Rob's own explicit instruction, a small well-scoped follow-up whenever he decides to revisit it. New `scenes/battle/perish_song_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 29/29 assertions across 5 sections (data integrity incl. the dormant `target` field; cast dispatch incl. both-sides-including-caster, the already-counting exclusion, the all-unaffected fail case, and the Soundproof bug fix; the full 4-tick countdown-to-faint sequence via direct `_phase_end_of_turn()` calls; doubles reachability, all 4 combatants in one cast; a Tackle negative control). Two real GDScript typed-array bugs and one real missing-initialization bug (`_chosen_switch_slots` never set, crashing `_is_last_to_move` — only manifested in the 4-combatant doubles case) caught and fixed before the first clean run; stable across 4 reruns after. Full regression (this session's own first real test of `[Sweep-dispatch fix]` above, via the new hardened absolute-path invocation): run twice from independent process states — **117 files, GRAND TOTAL 11876, 0 failures both runs** (11847 prior + 29). **Total move-implementation count: 715→716.** `docs/move_status_table.md` regenerated and confirmed: **716 implemented / 217 excluded / 1 residual / 16 needs-manual-review** (the new `target` field needed adding to `gen_move_status_table.py`'s allowlist — the same recurring gap class as before, caught and fixed the same way). **Section D's residual: 2→1 — only Transform(144) remains, the one move in all of M19 confirmed to need its own dedicated session.** `docs/decisions.md` new `[Perish Song]` entry with full Step 0 citations.
- **[Transform] (Transform(144) — the LAST move in all of M19, given its own dedicated session per the recon's own recommendation): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14, same day. Two-part session: a report-only Step 0 re-verification first (re-checking the prior recon's own findings against source rather than trusting them, per explicit instruction), then full implementation once confirmed. **Step 0 confirmed `_reset_mon_ability` (shipped in `[Ability-reset fix]`) already covers Transform's own ability reversion for free** — its `original_ability` guard captures on the mon's FIRST `.ability` assignment (at construction, before Transform could ever fire), so a later Transform-driven overwrite never re-captures over it; source's own `SwitchInClearSetData` collapses every ability-mutating mechanic (Trace, Skill Swap, Transform) to the same natural-ability reset, not a "restore pre-mutation state" model — no new ability-snapshot infra needed. Everything else DID need new infrastructure: `species` (whole reference — nothing touched it before), the 5 computed stats, and `moves`+`current_pp` (a genuinely different CAST-TIME snapshot shape, unlike `original_types`/`original_ability`'s construction-time capture, since PP is consumed as the battle progresses). **`stat_stages` needed zero new infrastructure** — confirmed `_switch_out_clear` already unconditionally zeroes every mon's stat stages on switch-out regardless of cause, so Transform's own stat-stage copy (confirmed WITHIN source's copied byte range — a real, easy-to-miss detail) self-resolves for free. **Shared-Resource mutation hazard confirmed and fixed**: `_set_mon_type`/`_set_mon_type_array` mutate `species.types` in place, so a bare `attacker.species = target.species` would let a later Color-Change/Conversion hit on the transformed attacker corrupt the REAL target's own species Resource — fixed via `target.species.duplicate()` (matching the established Normalize/Hidden-Power/Foul-Play/Body-Press/Photon-Geyser shallow-duplicate pattern) plus an explicit re-duplicate of the nested `types` array (matching `original_types`/Roost/Reflect Type's own established paranoia, not trusting `Resource.duplicate()` alone). Ability copy is a RAW reference copy (`attacker.ability = target.ability`), deliberately NOT through `effective_ability_id` — traced `GetBattlerAbilityInternal` and confirmed copying a Neutralizing-Gas-suppressed value would be permanently wrong once NG later left the field; suppression correctly re-applies on every future read via the normal accessor instead. `times_hit` is a separate, explicit, PERMANENT special-case copy in source (writes into the attacker's own persistent party record, no restoration anywhere) — confirmed real source behavior and reproduced as-is, not reverted on switch-out. `SortBattlersByRawSpeed`'s re-sort confirmed to serve only infrastructure this project hasn't built (Dancer, raw-speed move-end/switch-in iteration order, Snatch's bounce lookup) — `_turn_order` needs zero change. Multitype reconfirmed a non-issue (switch-in-only dispatch, unaffected by anything shipped since the original recon). New `BattlePokemon` fields: `original_species` (setter-captured exactly like `original_ability` — confirmed SAFE via a full-codebase grep finding exactly ONE `.species` assignment site anywhere, `from_species` itself), `original_attack`/`original_defense`/`original_sp_attack`/`original_sp_defense`/`original_speed` (5 scalars, matching the existing scalar style), `transformed: bool`, `pre_transform_moves`/`pre_transform_pp` (cast-time snapshot). New `BattleManager._reset_mon_species`/`_reset_mon_stats`/`_reset_mon_transform`, called in that exact order — species MUST run before `_reset_mon_type` — at all 5 switch-in sites, alongside the existing trio. **Two small, directly-connected fixes to already-shipped code closed as a byproduct**: Mimic/Sketch's own real source-confirmed "attacker already Transformed" fail condition (previously flagged in both moves' doc comments as "not modeled — Transform isn't implemented yet") now added to both dispatch conditions; Instruct's own hardcoded exclusion list gained `is_transform` (confirmed `BAN_INSTRUCT` itself is set on `ban_flags` for documentation completeness but never actually consulted anywhere in this codebase — the real check is Instruct's own per-field list). New `MoveData.is_transform` flag plus a new `not move.is_transform` exemption on the general foe-targeting type-immunity gate — traced `BattleScript_EffectTransform` and confirmed it never calls `typecalc` (the same standing-checklist pattern as Foresight/Purify/Nightmare/Spite/Toxic Thread/Venom Drench/the 16-move audit), so without this exemption a Ghost-type target would have incorrectly blocked Transform outright (Normal-type is a flat 0x vs Ghost in this project's chart). New `scenes/battle/transform_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 59/59 assertions across 11 sections (data integrity; basic successful Transform incl. both PP-cap directions; all 4 fail conditions independently; stat_stages copied from the target, not the attacker's own pre-Transform value; the shared-Resource-mutation-hazard regression test itself — Transform then Conversion on the transformed attacker, confirming the real target's own species.types stays untouched; switch-out restoration via two direct `_do_voluntary_switch` calls, explicitly confirming the reset does NOT fire on switch-OUT and DOES fire on switch back IN — a more precise isolation than a full `start_battle_with_parties` call, which would be confounded by `_phase_battle_start`'s own leads-loop reset firing first; times_hit permanence; ability-copy correctness under forced Neutralizing Gas; Protect bypass; Instruct failing to force a Transform re-use; a negative control). One real test-authoring bug caught and fixed on the first run (58/59): an `atk_true_pp` snapshot taken BEFORE dispatch didn't account for Transform's own cast deducting its own 1 PP before `pre_transform_pp` is snapshotted — the correct restore target is 9/10, not a fresh 10/10; fixed by sourcing the expected value from `pre_transform_pp` itself. Stable across 4 reruns after. Full regression (twice, from independent process states, one deliberately preceded by `cd /tmp` to reconfirm `[Sweep-dispatch fix]`'s invocation still works unattended): **118 files, GRAND TOTAL 11935, 0 failures both runs** (11876 prior + 59) — one transient empty-log/exit-1 sweep-dispatch failure on the very first attempt, matching the same still-open separate flakiness class flagged in `[Perish Song]`, resolved by a bare retry. **Total move-implementation count: 716→717 — the FINAL move in all of M19.** `docs/move_status_table.md` regenerated and confirmed: **717 implemented / 217 excluded / 0 residual / 16 needs-manual-review** (unchanged review count — `is_transform` is `is_*`-prefixed, already covered by the generator's own generic fallback). **Section D's residual: 1→0 — M19 IS NOW FULLY COMPLETE.** `docs/m19_subtier_plan.md` updated throughout (Section E's summary table, top reconciliation, closing prose). `docs/decisions.md` new `[Transform]` entry with full Step 0 citations.
- **[M19.5] (Testing & Hardening pass — recon then implementation of the 5 priority items, plus 2 unplanned infrastructure fixes surfaced along the way): COMPLETE** — 2026-07-14, same day. Recon (report-only) first identified 5 gaps per-bundle testing structurally couldn't catch; this session implemented all 5, in dependency order, with a full regression sweep after each. **Task 1 (ban-flag audit fixes) — the highest-value item, and the one where the actual fix count differed most from the recon's own estimate**: of the 8 ban-flag bits actually CONSULTED anywhere in `battle_manager.gd` (`BAN_MIMIC`/`BAN_SKETCH`/`BAN_METRONOME`/`BAN_COPYCAT`/`BAN_ASSIST`/`BAN_SLEEP_TALK`/`BAN_ENCORE`/`BAN_ME_FIRST` — `BAN_MIRROR_MOVE`/`BAN_INSTRUCT`/`BAN_GRAVITY` confirmed to have ZERO read sites and were deliberately NOT populated, to avoid pure no-op busywork), only 5 actually had gaps — `BAN_MIMIC`/`BAN_COPYCAT`/`BAN_ME_FIRST` were already fully correct going in (confirmed via the same cross-reference script, zero gaps found for any of the three). Fixed 91 additions across 87 moves (mostly `BAN_METRONOME` — ~70 LGPE/legendary-signature/utility moves shipped across many D4 bundles that were never checked against source's `metronomeBanned` field — plus ~15 `BAN_SLEEP_TALK`, `BAN_ENCORE` on Metronome/Mirror Move/Struggle/Copycat, `BAN_ASSIST` on Snatch, `BAN_SKETCH` on Hyperspace Fury) AND 4 removals (Bide/Substitute/Encore/Burning Bulwark incorrectly carried `BAN_METRONOME` with zero source basis — confirmed directly against each move's own `moves_info.h` entry). Applied via a purpose-built, source-verified Python patcher operating directly on `gen_moves.py`'s own text (not a bulk lookup table bolted on afterward) — every move's own dict still carries its true field set in place, matching the file's existing hand-authored convention. New `scenes/battle/ban_flag_audit_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 29/29 assertions across 9 sections (data integrity for all fixes; live dispatch-level discriminators for the 5 flags with real gaps — `_pick_sleep_talk_move`'s cheap in-memory pool made a genuine n=100 statistical exclusion proof practical, while `_pick_metronome_move`'s full-disk rescan-and-reload-717-files-per-call cost ruled that out for BAN_METRONOME, so that flag's dispatch coverage is a data-level check plus a single non-crashing smoke call, explicitly documented as such; 3 regression guards for the already-correct BAN_MIMIC/BAN_COPYCAT/BAN_ME_FIRST, explicitly labeled as guards not fixes). **A real, expected regression surfaced and was fixed**: `tier4_test.gd`'s own S1.19/S1.23/S1.27 had baked in the exact 4 incorrect "extra" BAN_METRONOME flags as passing assertions — updated in place to assert their (correct) absence, the same "a genuine correctness fix legitimately invalidates a stale test assumption" shape as prior sessions' Nature/Solar-Beam regressions. **Task 2 (Transform+Mimic composition bug)**: confirmed exactly as the recon flagged — Transform's dispatch snapshotted `pre_transform_moves` BEFORE clearing `mimicked_slot`, so an attacker with an ACTIVE Mimic overlay at cast time would have the temporarily-mimicked move (not Mimic itself) baked into the snapshot, permanently losing the revert-to-Mimic information on a later switch-out. Fixed with one guarded call: `if attacker.mimicked_slot >= 0: _reset_mon_mimicked_move(attacker)` inserted immediately before the snapshot lines. New `scenes/battle/mimic_transform_composition_test.gd`/`.tscn`: 12/12 assertions — Mimic then Transform in the same stint, confirming the snapshot captures Mimic itself (not the temporarily-copied move), and confirming the full switch-out+in cycle correctly reverts to Mimic (not the Transform target's copied moveset, not the temporarily-mimicked move). **Task 3 (full-roster smoke test, Tier A)**: confirmed no equivalent existed — the `PokemonRegistry` smoke-test print every suite already shows operates on a completely separate, JSON-backed, zero-consumer pipeline. Built as a DEDICATED, standalone, independently-runnable artifact per explicit follow-up instruction — a same-day first draft (`move_roster_smoke_test.gd`, 4 aggregate assertions) was replaced with `scenes/battle/move_smoke_test.gd`/`.tscn`, redesigned to mirror `item_registry_test.gd`'s own Section 1 convention of one assertion per catalog entry: scans IDs 1-934 via `ResourceLoader.exists`/`load()` directly (self-updating by construction — move_status_table.md's own "Implemented" classification is itself derived from this exact same file-existence check, so no hardcoded ID list to maintain), emitting one `_chk` per implemented move — **717/717**, confirming every implemented move loads cleanly as a genuine `MoveData` instance, stable across 4 reruns. **Task 5 (opportunistic doc-generator fix)**: added `stat_change_bypasses_type_gate` to `gen_move_status_table.py`'s allowlist — needs-manual-review count dropped 16→0, confirming (as the recon found) all 16 were a pure doc-generator gap with zero underlying implementation issue. **Two unplanned infrastructure fixes, both discovered as direct byproducts of running Task 1's own regression sweep, not separate scope creep**: (1) **root-caused the "separate, still-unexplained transient sweep-dispatch failure" flagged (but never fully explained) across the Perish Song and Transform sessions** — `count_assertions.sh`'s fresh-sweep branch runs its real per-scene loop under script-wide `set -euo pipefail`, redirecting ALL real output into a `mktemp`'d temp file that a `trap ... EXIT` deletes on ANY exit; a SINGLE scene returning nonzero (a real failure OR an already-documented pre-existing flake) aborts the whole script immediately, before the python analysis step ever runs and before the caller sees any output — looking exactly like the "empty log, exit 1" mystery flagged twice before. Fixed with `|| true` on the per-scene invocation, so one flaky/failing scene can no longer prevent the other 120 from being reported. (2) The fix's own first application surfaced two ALREADY-DOCUMENTED pre-existing flakes doing exactly this — `m19a_gen1_test.tscn`'s Hydro-Pump/Rough-Skin whole-battle-aggregation bug (`[D4 CHEAP bundle]`) and `m18_5g_test.tscn`'s King's-Rock/Shell-Bell statistical test (`[D4 CHEAP bundle]`) — both reconfirmed unrelated to this session's changes, not (re-)fixed, per their own original out-of-scope disposition. **Total move-implementation count unchanged at 717** (M19.5 touched zero move-count/exclusion accounting — pure data-correctness and test-infrastructure work). `docs/move_status_table.md` regenerated: **717 implemented / 217 excluded / 0 residual / 0 needs-manual-review**. Full regression: multiple independent sweeps via the now-hardened invocation, spanning both the original Task 1-5 pass and the same-day `move_smoke_test.tscn` redesign — **121 files, GRAND TOTAL 12693 with zero flakes firing (observed range 12690-12693 across runs depending on which of this codebase's several pre-existing statistical-flake suites fired that run — see the broadened "M19-complete baseline" entry below), 0 failures traceable to this session's own changes any run** (11935 prior + 29 ban-flag-audit + 12 Mimic/Transform-composition + 717 move_smoke_test = 12693). See the "M19-complete baseline" testing-convention entry below for the checkpoint M20+ sessions should diff against. `docs/decisions.md` new `[M19.5]` entry with full findings per task, including the Task-1 estimate-vs-actual discrepancy and both unplanned infrastructure fixes. **`[M19.5 addendum]` (same day, docs-only)**: a follow-up field-coverage audit surfaced 2 candidate findings — one (a claim that Fling/Natural Gift ship with flat/non-varying damage) did NOT survive verification (both moves are confirmed **Excluded**, not implemented at all — no `.tres`, no `gen_moves.py` entry — per Rob's own `[M19-exclusions]` list, matching the existing `ability_manager.gd:972-975` comment) and was dropped rather than documented; the other (skyBattleBanned confirmed fully moot, no Sky Battle system exists or is planned) was documented as a known, accepted limitation, matching the Perish Body precedent. The audit's own methodology was sanity-checked by confirming it independently rediscovered all 4 previously-known field-coverage gaps (`snatch_affected`/`two_typed_move`+`second_type`/`target`/`stat_change_bypasses_type_gate`, all already in `gen_move_status_table.py`'s allowlist) before its 2 new candidates were evaluated. No code/test changes. **This closes out M19.5 completely.**

### Standing Step 0 checklist item: does this foe-targeting move's real script call `typecalc`?

Discovered independently four times before being made a standing checklist item: `[D2 batch 2]` (Foresight/Odor Sleuth), `[D4 bundle 3]` (Purify/Nightmare/Spite), `[D4 Bundle 6]` (Toxic Thread/Venom Drench), and the `[EFFECT_STAT_CHANGE audit]` that finally swept the rest of the family (16 more moves — Growl/Leer/Screech/etc.).

This project's `BattleManager._phase_move_execution` runs every foe-targeting move with a real type through one general type-immunity gate before letting the move's own effect logic run, on the assumption that real source similarly checks `typecalc` for every such move. That assumption is false for an entire family of status moves: any move whose real battle script never calls `typecalc` (confirmed so far: `BattleScript_EffectForesight`, `BattleScript_EffectStatChange` and everything that maps to it, `BattleScript_EffectReflectType`) is NEVER subject to a type-immunity check in the real engine — including against its own primary, flavor-intended use case (Nightmare vs. a sleeping Normal-type target; Toxic Thread vs. a Steel-type switch-in; a plain Normal-type stat-lowering move vs. a Ghost-type).

**Before implementing or auditing any foe-targeting status move (or move family) going forward**: read the move's real battle script directly (`data/battle_scripts_1.s`, or trace `sMoveEffectTable`/`battle_move_effects.h` to find which script the move's `.effect` maps to) and confirm whether it calls `typecalc` anywhere. If it does not, the move needs the same treatment as the precedents above — either its own dedicated `is_*` exemption (if it also needs its own dispatch branch for other reasons) or, if it's one of a family sharing a no-`typecalc` script, the shared `MoveData.stat_change_bypasses_type_gate`-style flag — checked against this project's own `TypeChart.TABLE` to confirm the exemption is actually reachable (not moot, like the 9 Memento-shaped exclusions above) before spending test-writing effort on it.

### Standing Step 0 checklist item: a new consumer of a dormant `MoveData` field needs a full-roster grep, not just the moves already in mind

A recurring gap shape across this whole M19/M21.5 arc: a `MoveData` field already exists in the schema and already has real ability/item logic reading it, but was never actually SET on every move that should carry it per source — only on the specific moves a session happened to be thinking about at the time. Confirmed instances: Ice Ball's `ballistic_move` (flagged in a comment since `[M16b]` but never actually set on the data dict until `[M17n-1]`), Air Balloon/Iron Ball's groundedness (`[M18t]`), Mega Punch/Headlong Rush's `punching_move` and Aerial Ace's `slicing_move` (M21.5 Session 3's Part 4 Punch-family check), and 69 more moves across 10 flag categories found by M21.5's own Bucket 1 full-roster sweep.

**Before building any new ability/item mechanic that reads an existing-but-previously-unconsumed `MoveData` field**: grep the full roster (`gen_moves.py`, or the reference `moves_info.h` struct field directly) for every move that should carry the flag per source — not just the specific named moves already in mind for that session. A session scoped to "does move X need this flag" will reliably miss sibling moves Y and Z that need the identical flag for the identical reason.

## Post-M18 Review — flagged-but-unfixed items queued for disposition

Every item below was discovered during M18 implementation/testing/migration work, deliberately NOT fixed at the time per this project's standing "flag, don't silently fix out-of-scope findings" discipline. Items 1, 2, 5, and 6 were resolved via `[M18.5a]`; items 3 and 4 — originally deferred to M22 (Doubles Battle Support) as doubles-only edge cases unreachable in this project's then-singles-only test scope — were instead picked up and resolved directly by `[M21]`'s own items 1 and 2 (Shell Bell + Red Card interaction, and Shell Bell spread-move accumulation), once M21 built real doubles test coverage for both. **All six items are now resolved.**

1. ~~**Poison Touch has no Shield Dust/Covert Cloak gate**~~ — **COMPLETE** (`[M18.5a]`, 2026-07-08).
2. ~~**Poison Touch poisons the wrong battler**~~ — **COMPLETE** (`[M18.5a]`, 2026-07-08).
3. ~~**Shell Bell + Red Card doubles interaction not modeled**~~ — **COMPLETE** (`[M21]` item 1, 2026-07-15). Shell Bell's heal and Life Orb's recoil are now gated on `not _red_card_switched_this_move` at every call site, relocated to the tail of `_do_damaging_hit` to match source's real dispatch order.
4. ~~**Shell Bell + spread-move doubles interaction not modeled**~~ — **COMPLETE** (`[M21]` item 2, 2026-07-15). The spread-move dispatch loop now accumulates damage/hit-count across all targets hit and applies Shell Bell's heal and Life Orb's recoil exactly once off the combined total.
5. ~~**`m17n7_test.gd` Harvest/Cud Chew failures**~~ — **COMPLETE** (`[M18.5a]`, 2026-07-08).
6. ~~**`m18q_test.gd` Shell Bell discriminator failure**~~ — **COMPLETE** (`[M18.5a]`, 2026-07-08).

## Development workflow

## ⚠️ Known footgun: working-directory drift (READ BEFORE RUNNING ANY TEST)

The git repo root (`/home/rob/GodotAsImagined`) sits ONE LEVEL ABOVE the
actual Godot project directory (`/home/rob/GodotAsImagined/as-imagined`).
Godot's `--path` flag requires the PROJECT directory, not the repo root.

This has caused repeated, confusing failures across this project's
history — commands timing out, silently loading the wrong (or no)
project, or `cd`-then-run patterns losing the correct directory between
tool calls (e.g. `pwd` shows the repo root even after an earlier `cd`
in a prior tool call — each new tool invocation does NOT inherit shell
state from the previous one).

**Standing rule: every Godot invocation must include the full absolute
path in the SAME command string — never rely on a prior `cd`.**

WRONG (drift-prone — a separate/prior `cd` does not persist):
```bash
cd /home/rob/GodotAsImagined/as-imagined
timeout 60 /home/rob/Godot_v4.7.1-stable_linux.x86_64 --headless --path . scenes/battle/m17l_test.tscn
```

RIGHT (self-contained, cwd-independent):
```bash
timeout 60 /home/rob/Godot_v4.7.1-stable_linux.x86_64 --headless \
  --path /home/rob/GodotAsImagined/as-imagined \
  scenes/battle/m17l_test.tscn
```

This applies to EVERY Godot invocation — single test runs, `--import`
passes, and full sweeps alike. `scripts/count_assertions.sh` was
already hardened this way after `[D4 CHEAP bundle]`'s own investigation
found this exact pattern silently truncating sweep output; that same
discipline was never extended to ad-hoc single-scene runs, which is
where it keeps recurring. If a Godot command times out or produces no
output, check the invocation for a bare `--path .` or `--path
as-imagined` before assuming a real test hang.

Run a verification scene headless (self-contained, works from any cwd):

```bash
/home/rob/Godot_v4.7.1-stable_linux.x86_64 --headless --path /home/rob/GodotAsImagined/as-imagined scenes/battle/SCENE.tscn
```

**Note:** if you add a new file with `class_name`, run an import pass before the test scenes
will see it:

```bash
/home/rob/Godot_v4.7.1-stable_linux.x86_64 --headless --path . --import
```

### Data pipeline scripts

Moves, abilities, and (as of the M18 item-data-infrastructure session) items each
follow the same two-track pattern: a hand-authored Python dict as the
human-editable source of truth, regenerated into Godot-native `.tres` Resource
files the engine loads at runtime. Run any of these from the project root, then
re-import (see the note above) before running a scene that depends on new/changed
`.tres` files:

```bash
python3 scripts/gen_moves.py      # data/moves/move_NNNN.tres    (MoveData)
python3 scripts/gen_abilities.py  # data/abilities/ability_NNNN.tres (AbilityData)
python3 scripts/gen_items.py      # data/items/item_NNNN.tres    (ItemData)
```

All three scripts share one structure: a list of dicts (`MOVES`/`ABILITIES`/`ITEMS`),
a `DEFAULTS` dict (skip a field in the emitted `.tres` when it equals its class
default, keeping files lean), a `FIELD_ORDER` list (explicit emit order), a
`render()` function, and a `main()` that writes one file per entry to a fixed
`data/<kind>/` directory, ID zero-padded to 4 digits.

Loading convention: `MoveRegistry.get_move(id)` / `ItemRegistry.get_item(id)` are
path-convention loaders (`res://data/<kind>/<kind>_%04d.tres % id`, no preload
table — see `move_registry.gd`'s own doc comment for the full rationale). There is
no `AbilityRegistry` — abilities are loaded ad hoc per call site (`load("res://data/abilities/ability_%04d.tres" % id) as AbilityData`)
because `AbilityManager`'s actual mechanic dispatch is 100% hardcoded ability-ID
constants and never reads `.tres` fields at battle runtime; the `.tres` layer there
is a metadata catalog (name/description/ai_rating/interaction flags), not a
mechanism input. **Items follow the `MoveRegistry` pattern** (`ItemRegistry`,
`scripts/battle/core/item_registry.gd`), since item mechanics are likewise
hardcoded in `ItemManager` (`HOLD_EFFECT_*` constants) but item data may need
by-ID lookup from future non-battle code (team-building, UI) the same way moves
do.

**Item scope note:** as of M18a, `gen_items.py`'s `ITEMS` dict only contains the
40 items M18a actually implemented — every future M18 sub-tier (M18b onward) must
add its items there and regenerate `.tres` files, matching the moves/abilities
convention, rather than wiring item data inline into `ItemManager` or a test file.
See `docs/decisions.md`'s item-data-infrastructure entry for the full rationale
and the M18a-era gap this closed.
